Praefatio.	Preface.
Postquam compleui uobis o Filii, librum hunc, qui est postremus scientiae in medicina cum complemento ipsius, et consecutus sum finem in eo, ex expositionibus eius, et ipsius declarationibus, uisum est mihi, ut compleam ipsum uobis cum hoc Tractatu qui est pars operationis, id est, chirurgiae cum manu.	After finishing the book for you, my son, which is this last on medical science with its appendix and being completed in it, from its explanations and declarations, I thought to complete it for you with this treatise which is part of surgery itself, that is, surgery with hand.
Quoniam operatio cum manu prostrata est in regione nostra, et tempore nostro priuata omnino: donec fortasse periit scientia eius, et abscissum est uestigium eius: et non remanserunt ex ea, nisi descriptiones paruae in libris antiquorum, quas mutauerunt manus: et accidit eis error et haesitatio, donec clausae sunt intentiones eius, et elongata est uis ipsius: Visum est mihi, ut uiuificem eam cum ordinatione huius Tractatus in ea secundum uiam ex positionis, et declarationis, et abbreuiationis: et ut ueniam cum formis ferramentorum Cauterii, et reliquorum instrumentorum operis: cum fit ex declarationis additione, et ex properatione eius quod est necesse.	Since surgery with hand has been abandoned in our region and time altogether: until perhaps the knowledge of it disappears entirely and its track is severed: and nothing remains from it except brief descriptions in ancient books, which have been transmitted by hands: and error and hesitation occurred to them until their intentions are closed and elongated their own views. I thought that I should make it live for you with the arrangement of this treatise therein according to its positions, and declarations, and abbreviations: and come together with forms of surgical instruments such as Cautery, and other operating tools: accompanied by additions from its clarifications and specifications which are necessary.
Caussa autem propter quam non inuenitur bonus artifex eius cum manu sua in hoc nostro tempore, est: quia ars medicinae est longa, et oportet auctorem eius exercitari ante illud in scientia anatomiae, quam narrauit Galenus, donec sciat iuuamenta membrorum, et ipsorum formas, et eorum coniunctionem, et separationem, et habeat cognitionem ossium, et neruorum, et lacertorum, et numerum ipsorum, et eorum egressionem, et uenarum pulsatilium, et quietarum, et locorum exitus earum.	However, the reason why such a skilled craftsman is not found in our time with his hands on this matter is: because the art of medicine is long-standing, and its author needs to be trained beforehand in the knowledge that Galen described, until he knows the parts of the body, and their forms, and how they are joined together, and separated, and has knowledge of bones, nerves, muscles, their numbers, their outflows, pulse movements, quiescence, where those things end.
Et propter illud dixit Hippocrates, quod nomen cum nomine est multum, et cum opere est paucum, et praecipue in arte manus.	And for that reason, Hippocraster said: a name with a name is much, and little with the work; primarily in manual art.
Nos uero iam diximus de illo in introitu huius libri.	We have already discussed this at the beginning of this book.
Quoniam qui non est sciens, quod diximus de anatomia, non euacuatur, quin iam cadat in errorem, quo interficiuntur homines: sicut ego uidi multos ex illis, qui formantur de hac scientia, et iactant se de ea absque scientia, et sine experimento.	Since who is not knowing what we have discussed about anatomy cannot be emptied out of it so that he does not fall into error, as which many people perish: as I saw many from those formed in this science and boast themselves of it without knowledge, and without experiment.
Quod est, quia uidi medicum stolidum secuisse apostema scrophulosum in collo mulieris, et incidit quasdam arterias in collo: quare fluxit sanguis mulieris, donec cecidit mortua inter manus eius.	What occurred when a foolish doctor followed the abscess of a woman's throat and struck some arteries therein; hence her blood flowed out until she died in his arms.
Et uidi medicum alium, qui praesumpsit ut extraheret lapidem uiro, qui processerat in aetate, et lapis erat magnus.	And I saw a doctor who intended to extract the stone from another man's bladder, which was an old one, and the stone was large.
Peruenit ergo ad eum, et extraxit ipsum cum frusto uesicae.	Thus he approached him, and extracted the remnant of his bladder.
Quare mortuus est uir in tertio die.	Therefore the man died on the third day.
Et ego quidem iam uocatus fueram ad extrahendum ipsum: et uidi ex magnitudine lapidis, et dispositione infirmi, quod moriretur.	And indeed I had been summoned to extract him: and from the size of the stone, and the sickly state, it seemed he would die.
Et uidi medicum alium, qui accipiebat stipem apud quendam Ducum terrae nostrae propter medicinam: et accidit eunucho nigro, qui erat apud ipsum, fractura in crure eius prope calcaneum: et properauit medicus cum ignorantia sua, et strinxit fracturam super uulnus cum puluinaribus, et astellis strictura forti, et non dimisit uulneri expirationem.	And I saw another doctor who had accepted a bribe from someone of our land for his medicine: and it happened to an eunuch black who was with him, that he fractured his leg near the calcaneum; and the doctor acted without knowledge, and compressed the fracture over the wound with bandages, straws tied firmly together, and did not allow for the wound's expansion.
Deinde absoluit eum secundum desyderia sua.	Then he released him according to his desire.
Postea dimisit eum diebus aliquot, et praecepit ei, ne solueret ligamentum: et stetit sic donec apostematum est crus eius, et ipsius pes, et peruenit ad perditionem.	Then he let him go for a few days and instructed him not to break the bandage: but it stayed like this until his leg swelled up, and his foot came, and went towards ruin.
Vocatus sum ergo ad eum: et properaui ad soluendum ligamentum: et consecuta est tranquillitas, et euasit a doloribus suis.	So I was called to him as well, and I desired to break the bandage: peace was achieved, and he was freed from his pains.
Verumtamen corruptio iam confirmata erat in membro: et non potui refraenare ipsam.	But indeed, the rot had already been confirmed in the limb; and I could not restrain it anymore.
Pon ergo cessauit corruptio perambulare in membro, donec periit.	So put an end to the decay roaming within the limb until it died.
Et uidi medicum alium, qui perforauit apostema cancerosum: et ulceratum est post dies, donec magnificata est malicia eius cum domino ipsius.	And I saw another physician who pierced the cancerous swelling; and it became an open wound after days, until its foulness was greatly praised by his master.
Quod est, quia quando est cancer purus ex humore melancholico, tunc non oportet ut perueniatur ad eum cum ferro omnino, nisi sit in membro quod toleret, ut abscindatur totum eius.	Which means that when the cancer is pure from black bile humor, then it should not reach with iron at all unless it's in a limb that can tolerate, to be completely removed therefrom.
Et propter illud o Filii, necesse est uobis, ut sciatis, quod operatio cum manu diuiditur in duas diuisiones: scilicet, operationem cui associatur salus: et operationem, cum qua est periculum in pluribus dispositionibus.	And for this reason, my son, it is necessary that you know that the surgical procedure is divided into two divisions: namely, a procedure associated with healing, and a procedure which entails danger in numerous dispositions.
Et ego iam excitaui in omni loco huius libri, in quo uenit operatio, in qua est terror et timor.	And I have already awakened everywhere in this book where surgery is presented, which involves fear and dread.
Quare necesse est uobis, ut caueatis illud, et dimitatis ipsum: ut non inueniant stolidi uiam ad loquendum, et dehonestandum.	Therefore it is necessary for you to be aware of this and diminish it: so that fools do not find a way to speak, and defame.
Accipite ergo mensuram cum sollicitudine et protectione, et infirmos uestros cum facilitate et firmitudine, et utimini uia meliore perducente gratia Dei ad salutem et successionem laudabilem: et dimittite aegritudines terribiles difficilis sanationis: et tollite animas uestras ab eo quod facit uos timere, ut ingrediatur super uos haesitatio in fide uestra et commodo uestro.	So take the measure with diligence and protection, and assist the sick ones easily and firmly, and make use of a better way to lead to health and praiseworthy succession: and send away terrible illnesses that are difficult to cure: and lift your spirits from what makes you fearful, so that hesitation enters into your faith and convenience.
Est enim magis remanens ad gloriam uestram, et sublimius in mundo isto, et postremo ad quantitates uestras.	It indeed remains more enduring for your glory, and higher in this world, and finally at your quantities.
Galenus enim iam dixit in quibusdam suis admonitionibus.	For Galen has already said in some of his exhortations.
Non medicetis aegritudinem malam: ne nominemini medici mali.	Do not heal the bad illness: do not call me, the physician of evil.
Iam autem diuisi hunc Tractatum secundum tria Capitula. ¶	Now however this Treatebut has been divided into three Chapters. ¶
Capitulum primum.	Chapter One.
De Cauterio cum igne, et Cauterio cum medicina acuta, capitulatum, et ordinatum a capite usque ad pedes, et formis instrumentorum, et ferramentis Cauterii: et omni quod necessarium est in operatione. ¶	Chapter One. Of the use of cautery with fire and sharp medicinal instruments, from head to toe, their shapes and tools for cautery, and everything necessary for surgery operations.
Capitulum secundum.	Chapter Two.
De sectione et perforatione, phlebotomia et uentosis, et uulneribus: et extractione sagittarum, et similibus illius: et totum capitulatum, ordinatum formis instrumentorum. ¶	Chapter Two. Of incision and perforation, phlebotomy and aspiration, wounds: and extracting arrows, and similar things: and the whole chapter on forms of instruments.
Capitulum tertium.	Chapter Three.
De restauratione, et dislocatione, et curatione torsionis, et similibus illius: capitulatum, ordinatum a capite usque ad pedes, et formis instrumentorum.	Chapter Three. Of restoring function and dealing with dislocations, treating torsions of the organs (possibly referring to wrists), and similar matters: chapter organized from head to toe in terms of methods and forms of instruments.
Soli Deo Gloria.	To God alone glory.
Liber Chirurgici Albucasis.	The Surgery Book of Albucasis.
Pars I.	Part One.
¶ De Iuuamento, et Nocumento Cauterii: et quibus complexionibus conueniat, et quo tempore: et si cum ferro, uel auro.	Concerning the application and harm of cautery: when it is appropriate and in which cases, as well as when to use iron or gold.
Caput I.	Chapter One.
Sed Ante Quidem Quam rememorer operationis cum eo, oportet ut dicam qualitatem Iuuamentorum eius, et Nocumentorum ipsius: et in qua complexione exhibeatur.	But before we discuss the application of this procedure, it is necessary that I tell you about the nature and harm of the cautery itself: and which cases it should be used for.
Dico ergo, quod sermo de qualitate iuuamenti Cauterii, et nocumenti eius, est sermo prolixus, et subtilis, scientia, et secretum occultum.	Thus I say that the discourse on the nature of cautery application and its harm is a lengthy, detailed, scholarly and hidden science.
Etiam locuta fuit in eo multitudo sapientum, et dissenserunt in eo: et mihi quidem sufficit parum ex sermonibus eorum, timens prolongationem.	It was also said by many wise men and they disagre cued to that issue: but I find my own discussions sufficient without their debates, fearing excessive lengthening.
Dico ergo, quod Cauterium confert uniuersaliter omni complexioni, quae est cum materia, et absque materia: excaeptis duabus complexionibus, quae sunt complexio calida absque materia, et complexio sicca absque materia.	I say that cauterization generally strengthens every composition, whether with matter or without it; except for two compositions: hot mixture without matter and dry mixture without matter.
In complexione autem calida et sicca cum materia dissenserunt.	However, the hot and dry mixtures separated with matter.
Quidam enim dixerunt, quod Cauterium iuuatiuum est in ea.	Some say that cauterization is helpful in those cases.
Et dixerunt alii contrarium illius, scilicet quod Cauterium non est conueniens in aegritudine, quae est ex caliditate et siccitate: quoniam natura ignis est caliditas: et inconueniens est, ut sanetur ex agritudine calida et sicca, cum calido et sicco.	And others argue against it, namely that casterization is not suitable for ailments characterized by heat and dryness: since the nature of fire is warmth; and unsuitable to be healed from hot and dry conditions with heat and dryness.
Et dixit ille qui dicit contrarium illius: quod per Cauterium fit iuuamentum in omni aegritudine calida et sicca, quae accidit in corporibus hominum: quoniam quando tu comparas corpus hominis, et humiditates eius, ad complexionem ignis, inuenis corpus hominis frigidum.	And he who argues against it said that cauterization helps with all hot and dry ailments found in the bodies of humans: for when you compare a human body and its humidity to the nature of fire, you find the human body cold.
Et ego quidem dico per sermonem eius: quia ex perimentum iam detexit mihi illud aliquotiens.	And I indeed say through his speech: because from experience he has explained it to me several times.
Verumtamen non oportet, ut ueniat super illud, nisi qui iam probatus est, et exercitatus in capitulo Cauterii exercitio ultimo, et cognouit diuersitatem complexionum hominum, et dispositionem aegritudinum in se ipsis, et caussas earum, et accidentia ipsarum, et spacium temporis earum.	However, it is not necessary for him to come upon that unless he has already been proven and trained on the last chapter of Cautery exercise, and knew about the variety of human complexions, and disposition of diseases in themselves, and their causes, and incidents, and the space of time they take.
Ex reliquis autem complexionibus non est super uos timor: et praecipue in aegritudinibus frigidis et humidis.	However, for other complexions there is no fear among you: and especially in cold and wet disections.
Iam enim conuenerunt omnes medici super eas: et non dissenserunt in iuuamento cum Cauterio in eis.	Now, therefore, all physicians have agreed on those: and they did not disagree with their use of cautery.
Et scitote filii, quod ex secreto curationis per Cauterium cum igne, et bonitate eius super Cauterium cum medicina comburente est: quoniam ignis est simplex, cuius actio non peruenit, nisi ad membrum quod cauterisatur: et non nocet membro alio coniuncto cum eo, nisi nocumento paruo.	And know that children understand that from the secret healing by means of Cautery with fire and its goodness is greater than Cautery with burning medicine: because fire is simple, whose action reaches only to the member being cauterized: and it does not harm another adjacent member except in a very slight detr cued.
Medicinae uero comburentis actio peruenit ad illud quod elongatur ex membris: et fortasse facit accidere in membro aegritudinem difficilis sanationis, et fortasse interficit.	However, the action of burns reaches to what is stretched out from the members: and perhaps it causes a sickness difficult to cure on one body part, and possibly kills.
Ignis autem propter subtilitatem suam et bonitatem substantiae suae, non facit illud, nisi superfluat.	Fire, however, for its subtlety and the goodness of its nature, does not do that unless it is excessive.
Iam uero innotuit nobis illud per experimentum, propter longitudinem seruitutis et studii cum arte, et stationem super ueritatem rerum: et propter illud excusor a longitudine sermonis.	Now we have learned that through experience, due to the length of servitude and study with skill, and truthfulness about matters: and for this I am exempting from the lengthy discourse.
Et si non esset, quia non licet huic libro meo, afferrem uobis secretum occultum in igne, et qualitatem operationis eius in corporibus expulsionis suae, qua expellit aegritudines sermone philosophico demonstratiuo, qui acueretur a mentibus uestris.	And if it were not so, because this book of mine is prohibited to me, I would reveal to you the hidden secret in fire and demonstrate the quality of its operation that expels diseases with philosophical speeches, which should be remembered by your minds.
Et scitote filii, quod ipsi dissentiunt in tempore, in quo conuenit fieri cauterium, et ponunt melius tempus ueris.	And you know, children, that they themselves disagree on the time it is best to make a cauterization and place the wound at sunratury.
Et ego dico, quod cauterium conuenit in omni tempore: propterea, quod nocumentum accidens propter tempus submergitur in iuuamento, quod attrahitur cum cauterio.	And I say that a cauterization is appropriate at any time: because the accidental harm caused by timing is mitigated through healing, which is attracted with a cautery.
Et praecipue si cauterium est propter dolores ex doloribus necessariis, fortibus, festinis, qui non tolerant tarditatem: propterea quod timetur ex eis, quod accidat malicia quae est maior, quam paruum nocumentum intrans propter tempus.	And especially if the cauterization is necessary due to pain from urgent, strong, and rapid pains that do not tolerate delay: because it is feared from them, since greater harm accrues from maliciousness than minor damage intrans for time.
Et non cadat in mentibus uestris o filii illud, quod non extimant, nisi uulgus et stolidi medici, scilicet quod illi aegritudini quae sanatur per cauterium, non est reditio semper: et ponunt illud consequens, et res non est sicut putant: propterea quod cauterium non est, nisi loco medicinae, quae alterat complexionem, et exiccat humiditates quae sunt caussae, quare accidunt dolores.	And do not let it be in your minds that the son does not believe such a thing, unless only common and foolish physicians think so; specifically, that illnesses which are healed by cauterization always result in scarring: they claim this is false, as what they assert isn't true. This is because cauterization is nothing other than an aspect of medicine that alters complexion and removes humidities causing the pains.
Verumtamen cauterium superfluit super medicinam per uelocitatem ualetudinis suae, et uirtutem suae operationis, et uehementiam dominii sui: et possibile est, ut redeat aegritudo hora aliqua temporis secundum complexionem infirmi, et locationem aegritudinis suae, et uirtutem eius: et quod praeparatur in corpore eius ex aggregatione superfluitatum in eo: et quod peruenit ad ipsum in acquisitione sua ex cibis, et similibus illis ex caussis, nisi fit aegritudo, in qua administratur cauterium.	However, cauterization is superior to medicine by the speed of its own health improvement and strengthening its own operation' vice-like grip: it is possible that an illness can recover at some time based on the infirmity's complexion, location of its illness, and power; prepared in his body from the accumulation of superfluitates therein: and what brings him to it through gaining it from foods and similar things because of those causes. Unless a disease in which cauterization is applied exists.
Aegritudo subtilis in membro paucarum superfluitatum, et humiditatum, sicut cauterium dentis, propter dolorem, et similia illi, possibile est enim, ut non redeat in eo ille dolor.	The subtle sickness of many overly-sized and moist parts, akin to the treatment for a toothache, likewise other similar things, it is possible that the pain does not return therein.
Sed illud fit in paucis.	But this happens rarely.
At uero sermo uulgi iterum, quod cauterium est postremum medicinae, est sermo rectus: non ad illud quod ipsi intendunt in illo: quoniam ipsi credunt, quod non est curatio quae conferat cum medicina, neque cum alio post occasum cauterii.	But the common speech about this last of medical treatments, namely cauterization, is as follows: not for what they think it to be for in that case: since they believe it does not confer a cure with medicine nor after dusk following cauterization.
Res autem est econtrario illius, et intentio, quod cauterium est postremum medicinae, non est, nisi quod quando nos administramus modos curationis in aliqua aegritudinum, et non conferunt illae medicinae: deinde administramus in fine rei cauterium, et confert: tunc inde cadit, quod cauterium est postremum mediciuae, non secundum intentionem quam intelligunt uulgus et multistolidorum medicorum.	But the opposite of that and intent, which is that cauterization is last in medical treatments, is not such if when we administer remedies for a certain illness and they do not provide benefits: then we administer at the end with cautery and it does confer: thereafter falls what was thought to be true by the common people and most of the learned physicians.
Antiqui autem dixerunt, quod cauterium cum auro est melius, quam cauterium cum ferro: et non dixerunt illud, nisi propter aequalitatem auri, et sublimitatem substantiae suae: et dixerunt, quod non facit pus locus cauterii.	However, the ancients also said that caustic with gold is better than causte with iron; and they did not say this only due to the equality of gold and its substance's sublimity: and they said that it does not make a place for pus.
Verum non est illud absolute: quoniam ego iam probaui illud, et inueni, quod ipsum non facit illud in quibusdam corporibus absque aliis.	However, this is not absolutely true; for I have already tested it and found that it does not do so in certain bodies without others.
Et cauterium cum ipso est bonum, et melius quam cum ferro, sicut dixerunt.	And caustic with itself is good, and better than with iron, as they said.
Verumtamen quando tu ignis cauterium in igne ex auro, non declaratur tibi, quando ignitur secundum quantitatem quam uis, propter rubedinem auri: et quando properat ad ipsum frigus, et si addis super ipsum ignitionem, liquescit in igne, et uertitur in laminas.	However, when you heat the caustic with gold into fire from gold, it is not declared to you how much of it should be heated by its own will: and when it hastens towards its coldness, and if you add more on top of the ignition, it melts into fire, and turns into sheets.
Quare cadit artifex ex illo in occupationem: et propter illud fit Cauterium cum ferro apud nos uelocius et propinquius, ex rectitudine ad operationem.	Why does an artist fall from his craft: and for this reason is cautery with iron quicker and closer among us in the rightness to the operation.
Et ego quidem iam ordinaui hoc Capitulum in Cauterio, secundum capitula: et ordinaui ea a capite usque ad pedes: ut alleuient quaerenti illud quod uult ex eo.	And indeed I have already ordered this Chapter on cautery according to the chapters: and I have ordered it from head to feet so that seekers may obtain what they desire from it.
¶ De modo cauterizandi Caput in commissura coronali.	¶ On the method of cauterizing at the crown's junction.
Caput II.	Chapter II.
Confert hic cauterizatio ad dominium humiditatis et frigiditatis super cerebrum: quae duae sunt caussae sodae, et multitudinis fluxus humorum ex capite ad partes oculorum et aurium, et multitudinis somni, et doloris dentium, et doloris gutturis: et uniuersaliter omnis aegritudinis, quae accidit ex frigiditate, sicut paralisis, et sodae, epilepsiae, et apoplexiae, et similia illis ex aegritudinibus.	This cauterization is for the control of moisture and cold over the head: which two are causes, namely an excess flow of humors from the head to the parts around the eyes and ears, and many forms of sleep, along with toothaches, throat pains; and universally all illnesses that occur due to cold, such as paralysis, swellings, epilepsy, apoplexy, and similar conditions.
Modus cauterizationis est, ut praecipias infirmo: ut euacuetur in primis cum medicina solutiua mundificante caput tribus noctibus, aut quatuor, secundum quod exigit uirtus infirmi, et eius aetas, et consuetudo eius.	The mode of cauterization is to be applied first: that the patient should be cleansed in the beginning with medicinal solutions purifying the head over three or four nights, depending on the strength and age of the patient, and their usual habits.
Deinde praecipe ei, ut radi faciat caput suum cum nouacula.	Then instruct him to make his hair with new combs.
Deinde fac eum sedere inter manus tuas quadratum, ita quod iam posuit manus suas super pectus suum.	Next, have him sit between your hands squarely so that he has already placed his hands on his chest.
Deinde pone radicem palmae tuae super radicem nasi sui inter oculos suos.	Then place the root of your hand above the root of his nose between his eyes.
Vbicumque ergo peruenerit digitus tuus medius, signa locum illum cum incausto.	And so when your middle finger arriveby has reached that place, mark it with a hot instrument.
Deinde igni Cauterium Oliuare: cuius haec est forma.	Then the cautery oil fire of this form.
Deinde pone ipsum super locum signatum cum incausto, descensione, qua constringatur manus tua paulatim, et tu reuolues ipsum.	Then place it over that marked place with a hot instrument, slowly descend as you are bandaging your hand and then roll off the item.
Deinde leua manum tuam uelociter, et aspicias locum.	Then turn on the wrist of your hand quickly, and look at that spot.
Quod si uides iam detegi ex osse quantitatem capitis alkiel, aut quantitatem zeuherbi, tunc eleua manum tuam.	Which if you see now that there is an amount of headache from the bone or an amount of zoherb, then tighten your hand.
Et si non, itera manum tuam ferro ipso, aut cum alio ab ipso si infrigidatur: donec uideantur ossa, quae dixi tibi.	And if not, repeat your hand movement with the same iron or another one from it until you see the bones that I told you to look for.
Deinde sume aliquid ex sale, et solue illud in aqua, et imbibe in ipso cotum, et pone super locum: et dimitte ipsum tribus diebus.	Then take something from salt and dissolve it in water, then drink it mixed with the same cuttlefish broth, and place it over the spot. Let it rest for three days.
Deinde pone super ipsum cotum imbibitum in butyro, et dimitte illum super locum, donec destruatur eschara ignis.	Then apply something dissolved from fat to the cuttlefish broth you have drunk and place it over the spot until the scab is destroyed by fire.
Deinde cura illud cum unguento tetrapharmacon, usquequo sanetur.	Then care for that with four-drug ointment; perhaps it will be healed.
Iam dixerunt, quod quanto uulnus plus remanet apertum, emittit pus: quare est melius et magis iuuatiuum.	Now they say that if the wound remains open for more than a certain amount of time, it releases pus; therefore it is better and provides greater comfort.
Et dixerunt quidam eorum, ut cauterizetur cutis usque ad os: et teneatur Cauterium, donec aduratur quiddam spissitudinis ossis.	And some of them say that the skin should be burned up to the bone; and hold a cautery until something is charred in the thickness of the bone.
Deinde radatur post illud quod adustum est ex osse, deinde curetur.	Next, one should scrape off what has been burnt from the bone, and then treat it.
Et dicunt alii, quod oportet ut cum cauterio perueniatur ad ultimum, donec imprimat in os impressionem for tem, ita quod cadat os, quod fit sicut forma kirate: aut instrumentum quod mulieres ponunt infuso alphabeti parui: et extimant, quod exspirantur ex hoc loco uapores capitis, et dimittatur uulnus apertum tempore longo.	And some say that one must approach with the cauterizing iron to the last point until it makes an impression in the bone as if falling from its original shape: or instrument similar to what women place infused alphabet letters: and they believe that vapors of the head are expelled from this spot, and an open wound is healed over a long period.
Deinde curetur, donec consolidetur.	Then treat it until it solidifies.
Mihi autem non uidentur hae duae species Cauterii omnino nisi in quibusdam hominibus secundum uiam timoris.	However, to me, these two types of cautery are not understood except among certain people according to the pathway of fear.
Et dimittere ipsum, apud me est melius cum salute ipsius.	And I believe it is better for him to be dismissed with his health in my opinion.
Debilitatur enim caput ex solutione continuitatis ipsius naturalis: sicut testificati sumus in reliquis membris: et praecipue quando caput infirmi debile est natura: et species quidem Cauterii prima est magis salua et melior apud me, et ea utor: operare ergo cum ea in salute.	For the head is indeed weakened by the continuation of its own natural deficiency: as we have testified about other limbs; and especially when the head is sickly and feeble by nature, and the first type of ceutery I find to be safer and better in my opinion. Therefore, I use it for operation with safety.
¶ De modo cauterizandi capitis in dolore totius capitis.	Concerning the method of cauterizing the head for pain throughout the entire head.
Caput III.	Head III.
Quando in toto Capite accidit dolor chronicus: et prolongatur illud in infirmo, et utitur hyeris, et cochiis, et caputpurgiis, et oleis, et empleumatis.	When a painful condition occurs throughout the entire head and is persistent; when it continues to afflict an individual, along with cervicals, scalps, purgatives, oils, and emplastes.
Et praecipue si iam cauterizatum est cauterio uno, quod narrauimus, et non confert ei aliquid ex illis: tunc considera.	And especially if the head has already been treated with a single caustic agent, as we have described, and it does not provide any relief from these: then consider this.
Nam si caput infirmi est fortis creationis natura, et non est debile, et inuenit frigus uehemens: tunc cauteriza cum cauterio alio sub illo parum.	For if the head of a sick individual is naturally strong and not weak, and it has found an intense coldness:" then caution with another caustic under that little.
Deinde cauteriza ipsum super omne cornu capitis sui cauterio, do nec pertranseat cutis, et discooperiatur ex osse quantitas, quam narrauimus.	Then caution over the entire head of its own with a caustic as follows: without piercing the skin and revealing from bone the quantity we have described.
Et cauteriza ipsum cauterio uno in occipitio capitis sui, in loco qui nominatur uas: et est locus in quo ponitur uentosa: et eleua matum tuam in hoc, et non discooperias os.	And cauterize it with a single piece of heated iron on the occipital part of its head, at the place called basilica; and there is another place where you should put the sharp thing: and insert your tongue into this hole.
Infirmus enim inuenit propter illud dolorem uehementem, et diuersum a dolore reliquorum cauteriorum capitis omnium.	For he found great pain because of that, and different from the pain of the rest of his head's cauteries.
Et ego dicam hoc Cauterium in loco suo: et oportet quod sit cauterium, quo cauterizantur cornua capitis, et occiput eius subtilius cauterio, quo cauterizatur medium capitis.	And I will say this about the Cautery: it should be in its place; and it is a cautery for shaping the horns of the head, and to subtly shape the occipital part underneath with a finer piece of iron.
Et haec est forma eius.	And this is its form.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in hemicrania, tam cum medicina adustiua, quam cum ferro.	Here is the method for cauterizing hemorrhages, both with hot medicine and with iron.
Caput IIII.	Chapter IV.
Quando accidit in parte capitis dolor et soda, aut extenditur dolor usque ad oculum, et euacuatur cum medicinis mundificantibus caput, et administratur reliqua curatio, quam dixi in diuisionibus aegritudinum, et non confert illud totum: tunc cauterizatio in eo est secundum duos modos: aut cauterizatio cum medicina acuta comburente: aut cum ferro.	When it happens that pain and swelling occur on a part of the head, or extend up to the eye, and when it is evacuated with purifying remedies for the head, and given further treatment as I mentioned in divisions of diseases, but not all together: then cauterization in this case follows two ways: either with sharp acute medicine that burns, or with iron.
Cauterium autem cum medicina acuta comburente, est, ut accipias dentem unum allii, et excortices ipsum, et abscindas extremitates eius ex duobus lateribus.	However, the cautery with sharp medicine that burns is to receive one of its teeth and remove the core itself, and detach the ends from both sides.
Deinde scinde locum doloris in tempore cum phlebotomo lato, donec fiat in eo locus sub cute, in quo dens capitur.	Then cut the place of pain at a time with a wide phlebotomy and keep it open until that spot is under the skin where hair grows.
Intromitte ergo eum in ipso sub cute, donec occultetur: deinde stringe super ipsum cum puluillo constrictione decenti, et dimitte ipsum quantitate quindecim horarum deinde solue eum, et extrahe allium, et dimitteuulnus duobus diebus, aut tribus: postea pone super ipsum cotum submersum in butyro, donec locus efficiat pus: deinde cura ipsum cum unguento usquequo sanetur.	Therefore insert it under the skin at that spot and cover until hidden; then bind tightly over it with a bandage of reasonable constriction, and release it for fifteen hours later dissolve it, and extract it, and rest for two days or three: afterwards place cotton soaked in butter on top of it until the site produces pus: then cure it with ointment as long as necessary.
Et si uis fac illud cum quibusdam medicinis comburentibus, quas ego scripsi in tractatu duodecimo, de Medieinis adurentibus.	And if you do this with some burning medicines which I wrote about in the twelfth chapter, on Middle Eastern remedamovers.
Cauterizatio uero eius cum ferro, est secundum hunc modum.	However, cauterization with iron is done in this manner.
Igni Cauterium, cuius forma haec est.	The shape of the burning caustic.
Et nominatur Clauilis: quoniam forma capitis eius est sicut forma claui, in quo est quiddam curuitatis, et in medio eius est quaedam eminentia parua.	It is called a claymore: because the form of its head resembles that of a claymore, which has some curve and a small bulge at its center.
Deinde pone ipsum super locum, et retine manum tuam: et tu reuolue ferrum paulatim cum uelocitate: et sit quantitas quae aduritur ex spissitudine cutis, sicut medietas eius.	Then place it over the spot and hold your hand on it: then slowly move away with the iron as if gently heating; and let the amount of burning be equal to the thickness of skin, like its half.
Et eleua manum tuam, ut non aduratur arteria, quae est inferius, et accidat fluxus sanguinis.	And elevate your hand so that it does not burn the lower artery and blood flow is reduced.
Deinde imbibe cotum in aqua salis, et pone super locum, et dimitte ipsum tribus diebus: deinde pone cotum cum butyro: postea cura cum unguento usquequo sanetur.	Then soak the thread in salt water and place it over the spot for three days; then place the thread with honey: afterward, apply ointment until healed.
Et si uis, cauteriza hanc hemicraniam cum extremitate cultellari secunda Cauterii.	And if she has a migraine, treat this with the second cutting instrument of the Cautery.
Et caue ab incisione arteriae in hac hemicrania, non antiqua proprie.	And a wound from an incision of the artery in this headache, not old properly.
¶ De modo cauteriezandi in hemicrania antiqua.	Regarding treating hemicranias through cautionary measures.
Caput V.	Head V (possibly a reference to Albucasis's surgical treatise on the head).
Quando curas hemicraniam, cum eo quod diximus ex curatione praecedente, et quod diximus in diuisionibus aegritudinum, et non confert curatio: et uides ex aegritudine, quod non sufficit ei quod diximus ex cauterio primo cum medicina, aut cum cauterio cum igne, tunc oportet ut ignias Cauterium cultellare, donec albificetur postquam signas super locum doloris cum linea, cuius longitudo sit medietas digiti, aut quasi illud: et depone manum tuam uice una, et stringe eam donec incidas arteriam, et peruenias usque ad os.	When you treat a headache, in addition to what we have discussed previously and that which has been mentioned in the classification of illnesses, and not ensuring treatment: then observe from the disease, if it is insufficient for him with the first cauterization using medicine or with fire cauterization, then you must apply Cautery knives until he whitens after when signs appear above the place of pain with a line whose length is half the finger, or almost that: and lower your hand by one hand, and press it until you incise the artery, and proceed to reach the mouth.
Verumtamen necesse est tibi, ut caueas a continuatione mandibulae, quae mouetur apud masticationem, ne aduratur latus, aut neruus qui mouet ipsam, unde accidat spasmus.	However, it is necessary for you to carve the continuity of the mandible that moves during chewing so as not to burn the side or nerve which moves it, from where a spasm occurs.
Et esto super custotiam, et cautelam de fluxu sanguinis arteriae, quae abscisa est.	And this is about the protection and precaution against cutting off of blood vessels that have been severed.
In abscisione enim eius est timor, et praecipue ei qui ignorat illud quod facit, et non est studiosus, nec expertus: et dimittit operationem cum eo in primis.	For the incision is indeed fearful, especially for him who does not know what he does and is not diligent or skilled: hence he abandons the procedure at once.
Et ego ueniam cum rememoratione regiminis fluxus sanguinis accidentis ex arteria secundum modum suum, et in loco suo huius libri.	And I will come with the recollection of the management of blood flow after an incident from a vessel as it should be according to its own nature, and where this book is located.
Quod si uides ex aegritudine, quod non sufficit ei hoc Cauterium, et uides corpus infirmi tolerans cauterium in medio capitis, sicut narrauimus, cura uulnus, donec sanetur.	If from the sickness you see that this caustic is not enough for him and you see the patient's body enduring the caustic at the top of his head as we have narrated, treat a wound until healed.
Et si uis, administra Cauterium, quod diximus in capitulo extractionis arteriae cum Cauterio habente duos cultellos.	And if it is a vein, apply cautery as we mentioned in the chapter on removing an artery with cautery holding two knives.
Est enim cauterizatio melior hac et magis conferens.	For indeed this cauterization is better and more effective.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in dolore Aurium.	Concerning the way to perform a cautionary treatment for ear pain.
Caput VI.	Head VI.
Quando accidit in Aure dolor a frigore, et curatur cum solutiuis, et reliqua curatione quam diximus in diuisione, et non remouetur dolor, tunc igni Cauterium: et est illud quod nominatur Punctum, cuius forma est haec.	When cold pain occurs in the ear and is treated with leeches, along with other treatments that we have mentioned in division, and if the pain does not disappear, then Cautery: and it is a thing called Punctum, whose form is as follows.
Deinde puncta cum eo post eius ignitionem in circumitu auris totius, sicut reuoluitur: aut in circumitu utriusque, si simul dolor est in utrisque.	Then the Punctum after its burning around the ear completely retreats, as it was initially introduced: or on both sides if pain is present at once.
Et elonga te cum Cauterio a radice auris parumper, postquam signaueris loca cum encaustro: et sit cauterii quantitas decem punctorum in omni aure, et quasi illa.	And stretch with Cautery from the root of the ear not too much after you have noticed the spots with wax: and the quantity of Cautery should be ten Puncta in every ear, and so on.
Deinde cura loca, donec sanentur.	Then heal those places until they are cured.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in Tortura.	Concerning the method of cauterizing during torture.
Caput VII.	Head VII.
Tortura quae curatur cum cauterizatione, non est nisi ex speciebus, quae accidunt ex phlegmate, secundum quod diximus in diuisionibus aegritudinum.	The torture that is treated with cauterization is not but of the kinds which occur from swelling, as we have mentioned in divisions of diseases.
Et deuita cauterizationem speciei, quae accidit ex exiccatione, et spasmo nerui.	And he described a type of cauterization, which occurs as a result of drying out and nerve spasm.
Quando curas hanc speciem torturae cum hyeris, et caputpurgiis, et gargarismis, et non confert curatio tua, tunc oportet ut cauterizes infirmum tribus Cauteriis: uno apud radicem auris, et secundo parum inferius a timpore suo, et tertio apud coniunctionem duorum labiorum.	When this method of torture with hyperthermia (overheating), head purges, gargles, and other treatments does not provide your cure, then it is necessary to use three types of cauterization: one near the root of the ear, a second slightly lower from its position, and third at the junction of two lips.
Et pone Cauterium tuum ex contrario partis infirmae.	And place your cautery on the opposite side of the weakness.
Quoniam mollificatio non accidit, nisi in parte quae apparet sana.	Since softening does not occur unless it is in a part that appears healthy.
Et forma cauterizationis est, ut cauterizes ipsum Cauterio in directo extremitatis auris superioris sub cornu capitis parum: et alio in timpore: cuius longitudo sit secundum longitudinem pollicis.	The method of cauterization is as follows: cauterize the very end of the upper ear beneath the head's outer edge slightly below, and at its position; whose length should correspond to the width of a thumb.
Et depone manum tuam cum cauterio, donec comburatur quantitas medietatis spissitudinis cutis.	And place your hand with a caustic substance until half of the thickness of the skin is burned away.
Et haec est forma Cauterii, et est species ex cultellari, cuius forma praemissa est: uerumtamen non est subtilior ea parum, sicut uides: et oportet ut sit cultellus in eo superfluae grossitudinis parum.	And this is the form of Cautery, and it is a species from scissors, whose shape precedes: yet it should not be too delicate as you see; and it must have a blade with insufficient thickness in it.
Deinde cura loca, cum eo quod praecessit: donec sanetur.	Then care for the places, where that preceded has passed: until healed.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in Apoplexia antiqua.	¶ Concerning the method of cauterization in ancient apoplexy.
Caput VIII.	Chapter VIII
QUando antiquatur Apoplexia, et curas eam cum eo quod diximus, et non confert medicatio tua, et infirmus non habet febrem, tunc cauteriza eum quatuor cauteriis super omne cornu capitis sui, et cauterio in medio capitis, sicut diximus, et cauterio in occipitio capitis, secundum quod praecessit: et modus cauterii sit secundum quod praecessit.	When apoplexy becomes old and its treatment according to what has been said does not help, and the patient no longer has a fever, then cauterize him with four cauteries over all of his head's horns as we have described, and with a cautery in the middle of his head, and with a catury at the back of his head, according to what preceded: and the mode of the cautery should be as it was before.
Etiam cauterizatur cum Cauterio super os stomachi: et est magis ultimum.	Also, he is cauterized with a cautery over the gullet's bone; and this is the most extreme.
Deinde curetur, cum eo quod praecessit.	Then it is treated as was described before.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in Obliuione.	¶ On the method of cautioning for oblivion.
Caput IX.	Head IX.
Oportet ut in potu dentur in primis infirmo hyerae magnae, et pillulae mundificantes cerebrum.	It is necessary to treat the head as first with large iron rods, and pills purifying the brain.
Deinde rade caput infirmi totum, et pone super occipitium eius emplastrum de synapi descriptum in tractatu emplastrorum: et pone ipsum aliquotiens.	Then thoroughly scrap the head of the sick person and put on top of his occiput an ointment described for plasters in the treatise on plasters, and place it several times.
Ipsum namque est modus Cauterii: et fac illud secundum ordinem eundem, quem dixi illic.	This is a method of cautery, and do as I have described therein.
Si ergo sanatur per illud, bonum est.	If therefore healed by this [method], then it is good.
Si non: tunc fac ei cauteria tria in posteriori parte capitis sui, quae sint descendentia a superiori parte capitis usque ad inferiorem partem oculi: et pone inter omne cauterium grossitudinem digiti.	If not: then do three cauteries on the posterior part of his head, which are descending from the upper part of the head to the lower part of the eye; and place between each c
Deinde cura Cauterium, cum eo quod praecessit.	Then care for the cautery with what preceded it.
Si autem uis additionem, et infirmus est tolerans illud: tunc fac ei Cauterium in medio.	If however there is an additional issue and he can endure it: then perform a cautery on him at the center.
Quod si uis additionem: tunc cauteriza ipsum super duo cornua.	What if there is an additional issue: then cauterize it over two points.
Deinde cura ipsum, donec sanetur: sitque Cauterium oliuare secundum formam, quae praemissa est.	Then care for him until healed: and the cautery oil as per the prescribed method mentioned earlier.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in Paralisi, et mollificatione.	Regarding the way of cautioning in paralysis, and softening.
Caput X.	Head X.
Oportet ut procedas in mundificatione capitis cum hyeeris, et cum eo quod diximus.	It is necessary to proceed with the washing of the head as we have described.
Deinde rade caput infirmi: postea cauteriza ipsum cauterio in medio capitis, et cauterio super omne cornu capitis, et cauterio super posterius ipsius, et tribus super spondiles colli.	Then wash the head of the sick man: then caution with a cautery at the center of the head, and with a cutaneous cautery over each corner of the head, and with a cauterio over its back part, and three times over the spondiles (cervical vertebrae) of the neck.
Si autem indiges in aegritudine mollificatione corporis pluribus illis, et infirmus est tolerans, et aegritudo est fortis: tunc cauteriza ipsum quatuor cauteriis super spondiles dorsi, et ultima cum cauterio, donec comburatur ex cute plurimum eius, et eleua manum tuam.	If however you find in a sickness requiring the softening of multiple parts of the body and he can tolerate it, and the illness is severe: then caution with four cutaneous cauterizations over the spondiles (cervical vertebrae) of his back, and the last one to completely burn into its skin until your hand becomes easy.
Deinde cura ipsum, donec sanetur: et sic cauterium Oliuare.	Then he cares for it until it is healed; and thus applies a hot oil poultice.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in Epilepsia.	§ On the manner of treating epilepseby cauterization.
Caput XI.	Chapter XI:
Non Cauterizatur epilepticus, nisi ille cuius epilepsia est ex phlegmate.	XI. He should not cauterize the person with epilepsy unless that person's epileps cuases from phlegm.
Oportet ergo ut mundifices cerebrum eius in primis cum hyeris, et cum reliqua curatione quam diximus in diuisione: quando infirmus est magnus, aut est tolerans in accaeptione medicinarum.	Therefore, it is necessary to first cleanse his brain with wine and the rest of the treatment as we have described in section IV: when he is severely ill or can endure medicines well.
Si autem est puer, qui non tolerat medicinas, tunc administratur gargarisma, et masticationes mundificantes cerebrum, ante illud diebus multis cum bonificatione ciborum.	However, if the child cannot endure medicine, then an emetic is administerired and cleansing mouthfuls are given to cleanse his brain before many days with good nourishment food.
Deinde rade caput eius, postea cauteriza ipsum Cauterio uno in medio capitis, secundum quod praecessit in modo: et cauterio alio in occipitio eius, et super omne cornu capitis sui cauterio.	Then clean his head, then he is cauterized with a single caustic on the top of his head as described previously: and another at the back of his neck, and over all corners of his head are other caustics.
Quod si infirmus fuerit fortis, et fuerit tolerans, tunc cauteriza ipsum cauteriis, quae dixi in habente paralisim, et mollificationem corporis super spondiles colli, et spondiles dorsi: et sit Cauterium oliuare secundum modum qui praecessit.	If the patient is strong and tolerant, then cauterize him with cauldrons as I have described in those having paralysis, and softening of the body over the spondyles of the neck and spondyles of the back: And let the Cautery be oilated according to the aforemente mentioned.
Si autem infirmus est puer, tunc pone cauterium subtile, secundum hunc modum.	If however the patient is a child, then place the cauldron delicately, following this manner.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in Melancholia.	Regarding the method of cauterizing in melancholy.
Caput XII.	Chapter XII.
Quando caussa melancholiae sunt humiditates corruptae, et phlegma grossum, tunc cauteriza ipsum Cauteriis, quae diximus in habente paralisim.	When the cause of melancholy are rotten moistures and thickened phlegm, then cauterize him with cauldrums as we have described in those having paralysis.
Et si caussa melancholiae est superfluitas decliuis ad melancholiam, et est corpus infirmi humectum, tunc da ei in potu quod mundificet cerebrum eius, secundum quod praecessit in diuisione: deinde rade caput infirmi, et fac postea tortellam decenter factam ex lino, sicut circulum.	And if the cause of mel <|assistant<|im_sep|>elanches is excessive sweat to melancholy, and the body is a sick humidified one, then give him in his mouth what purifies the brain as it preceded in division: afterwards shave the head of the sick person, and make thereafter a neatly crafted band from linen, like a circle.
Deinde pone ipsam in medio capitis: et infirmus sedens quadratus teneatur ab omni parte.	Then place it on top of his head and he should sit squarely so that he is supported from all sides.
Deinde praesenta linimentum.	Then apply the present ointment.
Et est dignius ex butyro ouium antiquo.	And it's better than an old balsam of butter.
Et calefac ipsum super ignem calefactione temperata mensura, quam toleret digitus, quando intromittitur in ipsum.	And heat the mass above a fire with moderate heating as measured by finger when it is introduced into it.
Deinde euacua ipsum in medio capitis eius in circulo, et dimitte ipsum donec infrigidetur.	Then immerse it in the middle of his head in a circle and let go until it cools down.
Fac illud infirmo omni hebdomada semel, cum reliquo regimine eius bono, donec sanetur.	Do this to the sick person every week once, with the rest of his good regime until he is cured.
Aut si uis, cauteriza ipsum faciendo puncta parua plurimum eius, praeter quod teneas manum cum cauterio: imo sit odorando.	Or if it's a wart, burn it by making many small points of it except that you hold the hand with the caustic. It should be smelling sweet.
Haec enim species cauterii humectat cerebrum cum qualitate.	These types of cauterization moisten the brain in a certain way.
Deinde pone super ipsum cotum imbibitum in butyro, aut adipe gallinae.	Then he placed over the soaked bandage a layer of fat on wax or chicken grease.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in aqua descendente ad oculum.	Of the method of cauterizing with a descending water flow towards the eye.
Caput XIII.	Chapter XIII.
Quando declaratur tibi principium aquae in oculo per signa, quae dixi in diuisione, tunc incipe et pota infirmum, cum eo quod mundificet caput eius.	When the master states that water is to be poured into the eye with signs as I mentioned in division, then begin and pour weak wine, so it purifies his head.
Et custodi ipsum ab omnibus humiditatibus, et fac eum sedere in balneo, in ieiunio diebus aliquot.	And protect him from all moisture, and let him sit in the bath for several days of fasting.
Deinde praecipe ei, ut radat caput suum, et cauteriza ipsum in medio capitis sui.	Firstly instruct him to shave his head and then burn it in the middle of his own head.
Deinde cauteriza ipsum super duo timpora duobus cauteriis, si est incaeptio descensus aquae in duobus oculis simul: aut ex latere uno, si est incaeptio aquae in oculo uno: et abscinde cum cauterio omnes uenas et arterias quae sunt sub cute: et sint cauteria in ea longa in latitudine timporum: et caue a fluxu sanguinis.	Then burn it with two pieces of heated iron, if there is an influx of water into both eyes at the same time: or from one side, if there is an influx of water in one eye: and cut away all veins and arteries that are under the skin with a cauterizing instrument: and make the burn long in width like the pieces of iron.
Quod si uides aliquid ex eo, tunc abscinde eum statim cum quacumque medicina est possibile: et ego ueniam cum sapientia, quae est in extractione arteriarum, et abscisione earum, et cautela a fluxu sanguinis.	If you see something coming from it, then cut it off immediately with whatever medicine is possible: and I will come with wisdom, which lies in the extraction of arteries, and their cutting away, and preventing blood flow.
Et quandoque cauterizatur in ceruice, sub duobus ossibus, duobus cauteriis ultime productis.	And sometimes burn under two bones with the last pieces of iron produced from two cauldrons.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in Lachrymis antiquis.	Concerning the way of performing cauterization on old tears.
Caput XIIII.	Chapter XIV
Quando lachrymae oculorum sunt antiquae, assiduae: et sunt super uenas, et arterias quae sunt in manifesto capitis exterius, uerificatur quod illud est ex superfluitatibus frigidis, phlegmaticis: tunc cauteriza cauterio eodem quod narraui in incaeptione aquae descendentis, cauterio in medio capitis, et duobus cauteriis super duo timpora, et duobus cauteriis in ceruice sub duobus ossibus.	When the tears of the eyes are old: they should be treated frequently; and they are above veins and arteries that are outside on the external part of the head—the coldness is proven to be from superfluidity, phlegmatic substance—then cauterize with a caustic (cauter) as described in stopping the descent of water, with a mid-head caustic, and two caustics over two temperatures; two caustics on the scalp under two bones.
Et si indiges additione, tunc cauteriza ipsum in omni latere caute oculi, super extremitatem supercilii cum cauterio paruo.	And if it requires additional treatment: then cauterize around the entire eye carefully; on the outer end of the eyebrow with a small caustic.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in foetore Nasi.	Concerning the way of performing cauterization on foul smells from the nose.
Caput XV.	Chapter 15.
Quando tu medicaris illud, cum eo quod diximus in diuisione, et non confert medicatio: tunc propera, et da in potu infirmocochias tribus noctibus: deinde rade caput eius, et cauteriza ipsum cauterio medio, cum cauterio oliuari.	When you treat that which we have divided in the previous section and it does not strengthen with treatment: Then quickly give him three infusion cups at night: then shave his head, and cauterize it using a medium cautery: and use an olive oil-based cautery.
Deinde cauteriza ipsum cum cauterio clauili duobus cauteriis, super duo supercilia sub capillis parum.	Then cauterize it using two finger cauteries on the eyebrows: over two areas just above the hairline.
Et custodite ab arteria, ne incidas eam.	And protect from the artery to prevent cutting it.
Et haec est forma cauterii Clauilis.	This is the form of Clauili's burn-treatment.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in mollificatione Palpebrae.	¶ In this manner, one treats inflammebility of Eyelids with burning (cauterization).
Caput XVI.	Chapter 16:
Quando mollificatur Palpebra oculi ab aegritudine, aut humiditate: tunc cauteriza Palpebram cauterio uno, cum hoc cauterio lunari.	When the Eyelids are softened by illness or moisture: then burn (cauterize) the Eyelids with a single burning tool, using this burner as well.
Et si uis, cauteriza ipsum supra duo supercilia parum duobus cauteriis in omni parte: et elongentur a duobus timporibus: et sit longitudo omnis cauterii, secundum longitudines supercilii: et non ultimes manum tuam cum cauterio, imo secundum quantitatem quod aduritur tertia palpebrae.	And if possible, burn (cauterize) the same spot above two eyebrows with a little more than two burning tools in all parts: and they are lengthened from two sides of heat; and make the whole size of the burner equal to the lengths of the eyebrow: and do not end your hand when cauterizing, but rather according to how much is hardened on the third eyelid.
Et haec est forma cauterii secundum hunc modum cauterii lunaris.	And this is the form of burn (cauterize) following this method with a moon-shaped burning tool.
¶ De modo cauterizandi Palpebram cum pili inuersantur pungentes oculum.	Of the way of cauterizing the eyelid when sharp hairs are directed towards an eye.
Caput XVII.	Head XVII.
Cauterium in eo est secundum duos modos: aut cauterium cum igne: aut cauterium cum medicina comburente.	The cautery is of two ways: either a cautery with fire or a caustic medicine that burns.
In cauterio autem cum igne, praecipe infirmo ante illud, ut dimittat pilos suos, si est ex illis qui mundant eos, donec prolongentur et aequentur.	But with the fire cautery, instruct the patient beforehand to shake out their hairs if they are among those who comb them, until they are straightened and level.
Si autem pungunt eum apud ortum suum: tunc constringe oculos eius cum uitta, ut non moueantur, donec nascantur.	If they prick him at the point of his origin: then bind their eyes with a cloth, so that they do not move until healed.
Cum ergo nascuntur et aequantur, tunc pone caput infirmi in sinu tuo: deinde signa super Palpebram oculorum eius cum encaustro, signo quod sit secundum figuram folii myrti: et sit principium signi prope pilos.	When they are born and evened out, then place the patient's head in your lap: then apply a caustic on his eyelids with an encaustic, marking it according to the shape of the leaves of myrtle: and make this mark near the hairline.
Deinde pone cotum imbibitum in albumine oui: aut in mucilagine psilii super oculum.	Then he placed a cloth soaked and inserted into an egg white or psyllium-based paste over the eye.
Deinde igni cauterium, cuius forma est haec.	Next is the application of a form of cautery as follows:
Deinde cauteriza super figuram, quam signasti paulatim in uicibus multis, donec comburatur superficies cutis, quae est sicut figura folii myrti, totam apparentem proprie.	Next, he cauterizes over the figure you marked out, gradually applying it to many places until the skin surface is burned off completely, as if all parts of the leaf were properly exposed in their entirety.
Et signum sanitatis operis tui est: ut si uideas Palpebram oculi iam contrahi, et pilos eleuari apud puncturam oculi.	And the mark of success of your operation is: when you see that the eyelid starts to contract, and hairs are being plucked near the eye' cuffing point.
Eleua ergo manum tuam tunc: et dimitte ipsum tribus diebus.	So cleanse your hand then: and let it rest for three days.
Deinde pone super ipsum Cotum cum butyro, donec eradicetur eschara.	Then place a cloth soaked with butter on the wound until all scab is gone.
Deinde cura ipsum cum unguento, donec sanetur.	Next take care of it with an ointment until it heals.
Quod si redeat aliquod ex pilis post horam, et mollificetur palpebra: tunc itera Cauterium super illum locum, sicut fecisti in primis.	If any hair should return after the hour from the eyelid and be smoothed out, then repeat the cautery on that place as you did at first.
Si autem pili sunt in inferiori: tunc cauteriza ipsam, donec eleuetur ad locum suum naturalem: et aequetur ut non pungant pili oculum.	If however hairs are on the lower part: then burn it with heat until it returns to its natural place; and equalize so that they do not hurt the eye.
¶ De modo cauterizandi cum medicina comburente in eodem casu.	§ On how to cauterize using a medicine with a burning agent in this case.
Caput XVIII.	Chapter XVIII.
Est ut praecipias infirmo, ut dimittat pilos, donec prolongentur et aequentur.	Ensure that the patient is instructed to remove hairs until they grow out and even up.
Fac ex charta de panno formam folii myrti.	Make an impression of paper on a leaf shape from linen.
Deinde accipe ex sapone cognito, et ex calce non imbibita ex unoquoque pondus uncia I aut quasi illud: deinde tere ea simul contritione bona, et fac illud cum festinatione, ut non infrigidetur.	Then take soap from a known source, and one and a half pounds of salt that has not been soaked: then grate it together finely with good cleanlinkee, and do this quickly, to prevent cooling off.
Deinde ex pande ex eo super chartam quam fecisti sicut formam folii myrti, et pone ipsum super palpebram oculi unius, aut duorum.	Then take an object from it over the paper that you made like a leaf shape of myrtle, and put it on one or two eyelids.
Et pone sub oculo cotum imbibitum in albumine oui: et caput infirmi sit in sinu tuo.	Place under your eye a poultice soaked with alabaster and let the head of the patient rest in it.
Et pone digitum tuum indicem super medicinam, et preme ipsum parumper.	And place your index finger over the medicine, pressing it gently.
Et tu moueas ipsum quotiens sentit infirmus mordicationem medicinae: quoniam inuenit eius mordicatio sicut ignis.	And you stir the mixture whenever the patient feels a sting from the medicine, as it is like fire.
Dum ergo perseuerat hoc quod ipse inuenit mordicatio, tunc dimitte medicinam, et moue ipsam cum digito tuo.	While therefore you continue this that he himself found painful from the medicine, then remove the medicine and stir it with your finger.
Cum ergo quiescit mordicatio, tunc remoue medicinam, et ablue oculum cum aqua.	When therefore the stinging has subsided, then remove the medicine and wash the eye with water.
Et considera tunc, si uides palpebram eleuari, sicut eleuatur apud contractionem cum igne, aut cum incisione, est bene: et si non, tunc itera super ipsam ex medicina super locum, in quo non imprimit medicina, et non denigrat, donec aequetur operatio tua, et contrahatur oculus.	And then consider if you can evert the eyelid, as it is everted during contraction with fire or incision, this is good: and if not, repeat over the same place with medicine until there are no signs of imprinting, and the eye returns to its operation.
Deinde pone super ipsum Cotum cum butyro, donec eradicetur cutis adustionis.	Then apply a layer of cotton soaked in butter until it removes the burned skin.
Deinde cura ipsum cum unguento diaphinicon, aut alio, donec sanetur.	Then care for it with ointment made from diaphanous or another remedy, until healed.
Et necesse est tibi apud operationem, ut custodias ultima custodia, ne in oculum cadat aliquid ex medicina.	And you must take particular care during the operation, to guard against anything falling into the eye from medicine.
Quod si mollificatur palpebra post dies, et pugnat ex capillis aliquid in oculo, tunc itera medicinam super illum locum, qui mollificatur ex palpebra proprie, sicut fecisti in primis.	And if the eyelid becomes soft after a day and struggles something from the hairs into the eye, then repeat medicine over that place which was softened by the eyelabits itself just as you did at first.
Deinde cura ipsum, donec sanetur.	Then care for it until it heals.
Et haec est forma folii myrti.	And this is the form of a myrtle leaf.
Et scias, quod oculi hominum diuersificantur in magnitudine, et paruitate.	And know that human eyes differ in size and thickness.
Ergo secundum illud sit consideratio tua: et non occultatur uia rectitudinis illi, cui est studium de hac arte.	Therefore take this into consideration: nor does the path of truth that is his study from this art remain hidden.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in Fistula lachrymali.	Concerning the method of cauterizing a tear duct fistula.
Caput XIX.	Chapter 19.
Quando curas Fistulam, cum eo quod diximus in diuisionibus aegritudinum, et non confert curatio tua: tunc, oportet ut cauterizes ipsam secundum hunc modum.	When treating a fistula with the method we described earlier for certain diseases and if your treatment is not effective: then you should proceed to cauterize it according to this method.
Praecipe infirmo, ut ponat caput suum in sinu tuo, et teneat caput eius minister inter manus suas taliter, ut non moueatur, neque agitetur cum capite suo.	Instruct the patient to place his head in your lap and hold it with his hand so that he does not move or turn with his own head.
Deinde pone Cotum infusum in albugine oui, aut in mucilagine psilii super oculum eius: deinde igni Cauterium, cuius forma est haec.	Then place the cotyledon soaked in aloe or silk wormwood juice over his eye; then apply a burn with fire of this shape.
Sit concauum, sicut forma cannae pennae uulturis ab extremitate una, cum qua fit Cauterium: et si uis sit penetrans usque ad extremitatem aliam, et si uis sit sursum sic tenta.	Make the cautery like the form of a reed pen or goose's feather from one end, as the cauterization is done: and if you have something that can reach to the other end, try it in this way.
Verumtamen hoc concauum est melius ad opus tuum.	However, this shallow cavity is better for your purpose.
Deinde exprime fistulam, si est aperta, et extrahe ex ea saniem, et exicca ipsam: et si non est aperta, tunc aperi eam, et extrahe pus eius.	Then express the fistula if it is open and remove its contents; extract the tumor itself as well: and if it is not open, then open it, and remove the pus within.
Deinde pone tunc super eam Cauterium, quod fit ignitum ualde.	Then place a cautery over that which has been opened, which is made very hot indeed.
Et tene cum eo manum tuam parumper apud Cauterium ab oculo, ad partem nasi, ut non erret manus tua, aut inquietetur infirmus: et ponas Cauterium in adipe oculi, et corrumpas ipsum.	And hold with your hand very near the cautery from the eye to the nose so that your hand is not disturbed or troubled by the weakened patient; and place the caster on fat of the eye, and consume it.
Si ergo peruenis in principio Cauterii tui usque ad os, erit bene.	So if you arrive at the beginning of your cautery until your mouth, it will be well.
Et si non: tunc itera Cauterium semel, aut bis, si indiges illo: et dimitte illud tribus diebus.	And if not; then repeat the cautery once or twice, as necessary; and dismiss that after three days.
Deinde pone Cotum cum butyro, et cura ipsum cum unguento exiccatiuo, donec sanetur.	Then place the wool with butter and take care of it with an ointment until it heals.
Quod si praeterierint ei quadraginta dies, et non sanatur: tunc pone super ipsum medicinam acutam corrosiuam, donec detegatur os: et rade ipsum secundum quod uenit in capitulo suo.	If these do not improve within forty days and it does not heal: then place a sharp medicine on top of it until the bone is exposed. After that, trim it according to how it appears in its chapter.
Et est modus alius Cauterii fistulae, quem quidam primi dixerunt.	And there is another method of cautery for fistulas, which some have said the first ones mentioned.
Intende ad locum fistulae, et finde ipsum: deinde pone in ipsam fissuram camahan subtile, id est, Cannulam subtilem, cuius forma haec est.	Attend to the place of the tube (or canal), and find it; then insert into that crack a very thin reed (which is a very thin cannula), which shape this is.
Et funde in ipsum quantitatem drachmae ex plumbo liquefacto, et tene manum tuam cum Canna retentione bona, et non moueatur infirmus omnino, ut non currat, uel perueniat plumbum liquefactum ad oculum eius.	And find in it the quantity of a drachma from melted lead; and hold your hand with the reed retaining well (a cannula), so that the patient does not move at all, nor let go, nor run away, or else the melted lead will reach his eye.
Et oportet ut ponas super oculum infirmi cotum infusum in albumine oui, aut in aqua.	And it is necessary to place above the patient's eye a soaked cloth in albumen or water.
Plumbum enim comburit locum fistulae, et sanat ipsam sanatione mirabili.	For lead burns the space of the tube (or canal), and heals it with a remarkable cure.
Quod si sanatur fistula, cum eo quod diximus ex Cauterio, et curatione, est bonum.	Which if the tube is healed (or canal), together with what we have said from caustic and treatment, it is good.
Et si non, tunc necesse est administrare foramen nasi, et reducere fistulam ad cursum nasi, secundum quod ueniet in loco suo sibi proprio.	And if not, then it is necessary to administer a nostril passage and return the fistula along its course within the nose itself, according to where it comes into place for itself.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in fissuris Labiorum.	De the method of cauterizing within the labial fissures.
Caput XX.	Head twenty.
Multotiens accidunt in Labio fissurae, quae nominantur Pili, et praecipue in labiis puerorum.	Often occurs in the labial fissures that are called Piles and especially in boys' lips.
Cum ergo tu curas has fissuras, cum eo quod diximus in diuisione aegritudinum, et non confert curatio, tunc igni cauterium paruum cultellare, secundum hanc formam.	So how you care for these f cuissureuses, as we said in the division of diseases, and if it does not provide relief, then with a small cautery knife cut them, according to this shape.
Et sit concauitas eius secundum subtilitatem cultelli.	And let it be incised according to the sharpness of a knife.
Deinde pone ipsum ignitum festinanter in ipsis fissuris, donec perueniat cauterium ad profundum fissurarum.	Then place it burning quickly into those cracks until it reaches the depth of the fractures.
Deinde cura ipsum cum caeroto, donec sanetur.	Then dress it with plaster, until it is healed.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in fistula Oris.	§ Method of Cauterizing the Fistula of the Mouth.
Caput XXI.	Chapter 2n.
Quando accidit apostema in radice gingiuae, aut in palato, aut in radicibus dentium: deinde facit pus, et rumpitur: postea antiquatur, et currit pus, et fit fistula: deinde curas ipsam, et non confert in ea curatio, tunc oportet ut ignias cauterium secundum quantitatem, quod capiat in fistula.	When an abscess occurs at the root of the gums, or on the palate, or at the roots of teeth: then it makes pus and bursts open; afterwards it is cleaned out, and pus flows, resulting in a fistula. Then care for that wound and do not continue to treat an already healed condition. At that point, hot cautery should be applied to the amount taken by the fistula.
Deinde intromitte ipsum ignitum in foramine fistulae, et tene manum tuam, donec perueniat ferrum ignitum ad profundum eius, et ultimum eius: fac illud semel, aut duabus uicibus.	Then insert the hot iron into the fistula's opening and hold your hand; wait until it reaches its deepest point, and finally: do that once or twice.
Deinde cura ipsum post illud, cum eo quod diximus de curatione usquequo curetur.	Then care for that afterwards as we have discussed about the healing process until it is fully recovered.
Si ergo abscinditur sanies, et sanatur, erit bonum.	If therefore the pus separates and it heals, then it will be good.
Et si non, tunc necesse est detegere locum, et auferre os corrupum secundum quod ueniet in capite suo.	And if not, then it is necessary to explore the location and remove the rotting bone according to what appears at its end.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in Gingiuis, et Dentibus mollificatis.	Concerning the method of cauterizing on the gums and softened teeth.
Caput XXII.	Chapter 22.
Quando mollificatur gingiua propter humiditates, et mouentur dentes, et curas eam cum medicinis, et non confert: tunc pone caput infirmi in sinu tuo.	When the gums are softened due to moisture and the teeth move, if not strengthened with medicine, then place an unwell head in your lap.
Deinde igni cauterium, cuius forma ueniet post haec, ita ut ponas Cannulam super dentem: et intromitte in ea Cauterium ignitum festinanter: et tene manum tuam parumper, donec sentiat infirmus calorem ignis iam peruenisse ad radicem dentis.	Then apply a cautery of the form that comes after this, so as to place a cannula on the tooth: and insert the lit cauterium swiftly into it; and hold your hand slightly, until the ill patient feels the heat of the fire has already reached the root of the toe.
Et eleua manum tuam: deinde itera Cauterium aliquotiens, secundum quod uis.	And turn your hand slightly; then repeat the cautery a few times as you judge necessary.
Deinde impleat infirmus os suum aqua salis, et teneat ipsam hora una: et exspuat ipsam.	Then let the sick person fill their mouth with salt water and hold it for one hour; then spit out that same water.
Dens enim motus firmatur, et gingiua mollificata stringitur, et siccatur humiditas corrupta.	The tooth is moved and the gums are softened; thus, it binds together and dries out decayed moisture.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in dolore Dentium.	In regard to how one performs cauterization on a toothache.
Caput XXIII.	Chapter XXIII.
Quando dolor dentis est propter frigiditatem, aut in ipso est frigus, aut uermis, et non confert curatio cum medicinis: tunc Cauterium in ipso est secundum duos modos: aut Cauterium cum butyro: aut cauterium cum igne.	When a toothache is due to cold, or the teeth are cold themselves, or have been wounded, and no healing occurs with medicines; then one performs cauterization in two ways: either with butter, or with fire.
Cauterium autem eius cum butyro est, ut accipias butyrum uaccinum, et bullias ipsum in cochleari ferreo, aut in uenera.	The cautery with butter is taken as boiled butter, and poured into a bronze horn or flask.
Deinde accipe cotum, et inuolue ipsum super extremitatem tentae.	Then take woolen thread, and wrap it around the said extremity of the instrument.
Deinde submerge ipsum in butyro bullito: et pone ipsum super dentem dolorosum festinanter, et tene ipsum donec infrigidet: deinde itera ipsum aliquotiens, donec perueniat uirtus ignis ad radicem dentis.	Then immerse the instrument in boiled butter and place it quickly upon the aching tooth; hold it until it becomes cold, then repeat this several times, until fire's strength reaches the root of the tooth.
Et si uis, submerge lanam, aut cotum in butyro frigido, et pone ipsum super dentem dolentem: et pone super ipsum ferrum ignitum, donec perueniat ignis ad profundum concauitatis dentis.	And if it is a wound, immerse the thread in cold butter or cotton and place it over the sore tooth: then put hot iron on it, until the fire reaches deep into the cavity of the sore toque.
Cauterizatio autem eius cum igne est, ut intendas ad cannulam aeris, aut cannulam ferri.	And cauterization with fire is as follows for a tube of air or iron:
Et sit in corpore eius quiddam grossitudinis, ut non perueniat acuitas ignis ad os infirmi.	And there should be something of thickness within it, so that the intensity of fire does not reach the ill body's mouth.
Deinde igni Cauterium, cuius forma ueniet: et pone ipsum super illum dentem: et tene manum tuam, donec infrigidetur Cauterium.	Then the cautery fire, whose form comes: and put it over that tooth; and hold your hand until the cautery is cooled down.
Fac illud aliquotiens, nam dolor remouebitur, aut in illo eodem die, aut die alio.	Do this several times, for pain will be relieved, or on that same day, or the following day.
Et oportet in impressione illius Cauterii, ut impleat infirmus os suum buyro bono, et teneat ipsum hora una: deinde exspuat ipsum.	And it is necessary to apply this cautery so that the sick body fills its mouth with good butter and holds it for an hour: then expel it.
Et haec est forma Cauterii.	This is the form of the cautery.
Cauteriza cum quacumque extremitate uis secundum quod est possibile: et haec est forma Cannulae.	You cauterize with whatever extremity you can, as possible: and this is the form of the cannula.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in Strophulis.	On how to cauterize a strophe.
Caput XXIIII.	Head XXIV.
Quando Strophulae sunt a phlegmate, et ab humiditatibus frigidis, et non sunt obedientes digestioni per mecicinas, et uis digestionem earum uelociter: tunc igni Cauterium concauum, cuius forma est haec.	When the strophe is from phlegm and cold humors, and do not comply with their digestion through mechanical means, and the heat of cautery quickly digests them: then a hollow cautery, whose form is this.
Habens duas extremitates apertas, ut egrediatur fumus apud Cauterium ab extremitate altera: et pone ipsum ignitum super ipsum apostema semel, et secundo, si indiges illo, donec perueniat ad profundum apostematis.	Having two open ends to let the smoke out from the caster at one of its ends: and place it on fire over a sore spot once, and again if necessary until you reach deep into the boils.
Quod si apostema est paruum: tunc pone Cauterium secundum quantitatem apostematis.	If an abscess is present: then place a cautery according to the amount of abscesses.
Deinde dimitte ipsum tribus diebus, et pone super ipsum cotum infusum in butyro, donec remoueatur quod combussit ignis.	Then remove it after three days and place a cloth soaked with oil on it until the inflammation caused by fire subsides.
Deinde cura ipsum cum unguento dentis, donec sanetur forma cannulae.	Next, treat it with toothpaste, until the form of the tube heals.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in raucedine uocis, et constrictione anhelitus.	¶ Regarding the method of cauterizing in a throat ulcer and a wheezing tightness.
Caput XXV.	Head XXV.
Quando uincunt humiditates super cannale pulmonis, et praecipue quando illud est cum frigiditate complexionis, tunc oportet ut euacuetur infirmus in primis cum medicinis solutiuis.	When humidity overpowers the airway and especially when it is accompanied by a coldness of nature, then it is necessary to first strengthen the weak with dissolved remed cups.
Deinde cauteriza ipsum in nocrati apud radicem gutturis in loce depresso: et caue, ne peruenias cum Cauterio ad guttur, neque in cute, nisi quiddam eius.	Then you should cauterize it at the beginning of a bony spur near the roots of the throat on a depressed location: and do not approach with a cautery to the throat itself or into the skin, unless something is necessary about that.
Deinde cauteriza ipsum cauterio alio apud iuncturam colli in ultimo spondili eius ultimando: et sit Cauterium clauile secundum modum, qui praecessit.	Then he burns the thing with a cauterizing iron at another joint of its neck near the last vertebrae: and it should be a cautery rod as before done.
Deinde cura ipsum cum eo quod praecessit, donec sanetur.	Then care for it as well with what preceded until healed.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in aegritudinibus Pulmonis, et Tussi.	¶ Regarding the method of cauterization in cases of Pneumonia and Coughing.
Caput XXVI.	Head XXVI.
Quando Tussis et aegritudo Pulmonis sunt ab humiditatibus frigidis, et infirmus non habet febrem, neque phthisim, et aegritudo antiqua: tunc cauteriza ipsum duobus cauteriis supra furculam in locis depressis, lenibus, uacuis.
