When the Cough and Pneumonia are from cold humidities, and the patient is not feverish, nor has phthisis (tuberculosis), and the illness is old: then cauterize it with two cauteries above a fork on soft, gentle, low places.
Et cauterio alio in medio pectoris inter duas mammillas: et sit cauterium cannulae secundum formam quae praecessit.	And with another caustic on the middle of the chest between two breasts: and let the cautery be in the shape that preceded.
Et si uis sit cauterizatio tua punctando cum cauterio, quod nominatur Punctum, cuius forma praecessit in punctatione doloris aurium: et sint puncta ex triginta punctis usque quasi ad alia.	And if your cauterization is by pricking with a caustic, called Points (referring to the method used for earache where a pointed device is inserted), whose form preceded in puncturing pain: and let there be points from thirty upwards nearly as much more.
Deinde cura ipsum cum eo quod praecessit, donec sanetur.	Then care for it as previously instructed until it heals.
Et iam sit cauterium habens tres ramos: secundum hanc formam.	And now have a caustic with three prongs in this manner.
Quare alleuiatur cum eo cauterizatio, quando tu facis cum eo uice una tria Cauteria.	Therefore the incision is cut as one would with the single tripod caustic when you perform the causticization in this manner.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in Titillico, in dislocatione Humeri.	Regarding the method of cauterizing at the site of dislocation of the humerus.
Caput XXVII.	Chapter XXVII.
Quando dislocatur caput adiutorii caussa humiditatum, et nonfigitur in hora reditus sui a dislocatione sua, donec sit illud ei consuetudo reditionis, deinde dislocatur a paruo motu, qui accidit sicut nos iam testificauimus illud, tunc oportet ut reducas dislocationem in primis.	When the head is dislocated due to moisture and does not return on its own within the usual time frame of returning from the dislocation, once it becomes a habitual occurrence for its repositioning, then it should be dislocated by a slight movement which occurs as we have already testified this. Then it is necessary to reduce the dislocation first.
Deinde resupinetur infirmus super dorsum suum, aut super latus sanum.	Then the patient should be placed supine on his back or a healthy side.
Deinde eleua cutim, quae est in interiori Titillici ad superiora cum digitis manus tuae sinistrae: et si iunctura dislocatur ad interiora.	Then remove the cyst with a tool that is inside of Tilting's upper part along with your left hand fingers, and if the joint connection has been separated internally.
Deinde igni Cauterium habens duo uerua.	Then hold two pieces in an iron cautery.
Cuius forma est haec.	Which form is this.
Deinde cauteriza cutim, donec penetret eam usque ad latus aliud, et ueniet figura cauterizationis cum quatuor cauteriis.	Then cauterize the cyst until it reaches another side and comes in the shape of a cauterization with four cauldrons.
Et quandoque fit cauterizatio cum cauterio habente tria uerua, quare fit figura cauterizationis tunc sex cauteriorum: et sunt uerua secundum subtilitatem tentae.	And sometimes the cauterization is done with a tool having three pieces; then it takes the form of six cauldrums when they are arranged as follows, in accordance to the subtlety tried out: the tools are placed according to their delicacy.
Et haec est forma cauterii habentis tria uerua.	And this is the form of the tool having three pieces.
Et quandoque additur super hunc modum unum, quare sunt cauteria octo.	And sometimes an additional piece is added to this pattern; thus there are eight cauddrums: they follow the given model.
Deinde pone super cauterium porros contritos cum sale.	Then place the shaved bones with salt upon the burning iron.
Deinde fac adhaerere infirmum tranquillitati, ut non moueatur membrum tempore aliquo, donec confortetur.	Next, let it stick to the weakened part for calmness so that no body part moves at any time until comforted.
Et si dislocatio est ad superiora, et raro fit illud, tunc cauteriza ipsum super humerum cauterio clauili, aut cauteriis multis punctando.	And if the dislocation is above and rarely happens like that, then burn it over the shoulder with a pincers iron or pierce multiple times with cauteries.
Nam iunctura firmatur, et remouetur humiditas: et sanatur infirmus.	For the joint is made firm and removes moisture; hence the sick person heals.
¶ De modo cauterizandi Stomachum.	Regarding how to cauterize a stomach.
Caput XXVIII.	Head Twenty-Eight.
Quando accidunt in Stomacho frigus et humiditates multae, donec extrahant ipsum a complexione sua, et multiplicentur catarri ad ipsum, et assiduas modos curationis, et non confert: tunc oportet ut resupinetur infirmus super dorsum suum, et extendat crura sua, et manus suas.	When in the Stomach coldness and excessive humidity occurs, until they are removed from their body composition, and catarrs increase towards it, and regular care patterns are multiplied, and not increased: then one must lie infirm on his back, extending his legs and hands.
Deinde cauteriza cum tribus cauteriis, cauterio sub cochleari pectoris quantitate digiti unius cum cauterio clauili, et duobus cauteriis inferius a duobus lateribus cauterii unius, donec ueniat figura cauteriorum triangulata.	Then burn with three cauters: one of the cauter on the pectoral side in the quantity of a finger under the crescent-shaped cauter; and two cauters below the two sides of the single caster, until comes forth the figure of triangular cauters.
Et elonga inter utraque ut non coniungantur, quando facient pus.	And lengthen between them so they do not join together when they produce pus.
Et sit profunditas cauterii quantitas duarum tertiarum grossitudinis cutis.	And let the depth of the cautery be a quantity equal to two-thirds of the thickness of the skin.
Et sit figura cauteriorum secundum hanc formam sine additione: et si uis cauteriza cauterio magno in medio stomachi secundum hanc formam: et sit cauterium quo fit hoc cauterium unum secundum figuram circuli secundum hanc formam.	And let the shape of the cauldrons follow this design without any addition: and if you want to use a large cauldron in the middle of the stomach according to this design, then let there be an element that forms one circle-shaped cauldron following this design.
Et cauterizatur stomachus punctando ei qui terretur ab hoc cauterio: et est, ut signes super stomachum punctum secundum quantitatem, quam uis cum encaustro: deinde cauteriza ipsum cum cauterio puncti: deinde cura ipsum cum curatione, quae praecessit donec sanetur.	And the stomach is to be cauterized using a point that he pushes away by this cautionary tool: and it is like signs on top of a puncture in the stomach according to the amount one desires with incense, then cauterize it with the cautionary tool at the puncture: then care for it with treatment, which lasts until healed.
¶ De modo cauterizandi Epar frigidum.	Regarding the method of cauterizing a cold-blood creature.
Caput XXIX.	Chapter 29: On the Method of Cauterizing a Cold-Blooded Creature.
Quando accidit in Epate dolor ex frigiditate et humiditate, aut ex uentositate grossa, donec egrediatur a complexione sua naturali egressione superflua, et curatur infirmus, cum eo quod diximus, et non proficit in illo: tunc oportet ut resupinetur infirmus super ceruicem suam, et signes cum encaustro tria cauteria secundum hanc figuram, et hanc quantitatem eandem super Epar inferius ab hypocundriis, ubi peruenit cubitus hominis: et sit spacium quod est inter omne cauterium secundum grossitudinem digiti: et sit cauterium secundum longitudinem corporis rectum: et non comprimas manum tuam cum cauterio multum.	When pain from coldness and great moisture occurs in the liver, until it leaves its own excessive natural discharge; and when the sick person is being treated with what has been said, but does not benefit: then one should place the patient on their back over their chest, and make three cauldrons according to this shape, and the same amount below hypocundris, where it reaches a man's cubit; and let there be an interval equal to all of them according to digit length; and let the cauterium follow body size: and do not press your hand too much with the cautionary tool.
Et sit quantitas eius quod aduritur ex spissitudine cutis, quantitas medietatis eius non additum: et sit infirmus stans super pedes suos.	And let the amount that is to be burned come from the thickness of the skin; do not add half of it: and let him stand weakly on his feet.
Si autem non est stans, tunc sit iacens, qui iam extendit crura sua, et eleuauit brachia sua.	If however he is not standing, then lying down; who now extends his legs and lifts his arms.
Haec est forma cauterii.	This is the form of cautery.
Et tibi quidem possibile est, ut cauterizes ista cauteria cum cauterio cultellari, quando tecum est subtilitas et prudentia in arte.	And indeed it is possible for you to apply this form of cautery with a knife-cautery when there is subtlety and wisdom in the art.
Et custodi te, ut non ultime procedas in cauterizatione, et aduratur spissitudo cutis totius, quare aduratur corpus totum, et perueniat ad intestina: quoniam cutis illic est subtilis, scias ergo illud.	And take care that you do not end in cauterization; and the thickness of the skin is burned throughout, therefore the whole body is burne, and reaches to the intestines: because the skin therein is subtle, know then that.
¶ De modo cauterizandi apostemata Epatis.	Regarding the method of cauterizing boils on the liver (assuming "Epatis" is a typographical error for "Apollinaris," which could refer to a part of the liver or another organ).
Caput XXX.	Chapter Thirty.
Quando accidit exitura, et uis scire, si illud apostema est in carne Epatis, aut in tunica eius: tunc si est in carne Epatis, inuadit infirmum dolor, et grauitas absque acuitate: et si est in tunica Epatis, cum dolore est acuitas uehemens: et uides iam, quia fatigauit medicos eius curatio.	When an incision occurs and the wound is known to be a boil on the liver or its covering: then if it's in the flesh of the li[er], it brings forth weak pain without sharpness; but if it's on the tunica hepatic, with pain comes sharp severity. And when you observe that it has tired out physicians during treatment.
Oportet ergo ut resupinet infirmus super ceruicem suam.	Therefore, let the sick person lie down on their own back.
Deinde figura locum apostematis cum encaustro: deinde ignias cauterium quod assimilatur radio.	Then, form a figure around the boils using wax; then apply hot irons similar to those for branding cattle.
Et haec est forma eius.	And this is its shape.
Et cauteriza cum eo cauterium unum, donec comburatur cutis tota, et perueniat ad siphac, donec egrediatur sanies tota: deinde cura ipsum curatione exiturarum, donec sanetur.	And this is the method of cauterization with one hot iron until all skin burns away and reaches the fat; when all pus has been expelled: then take care in treating the wound, until it heals.
Et non oportet ut hac cauterii specie utatur, nisi cuius studium in arte medicinae prolongatur: et per cuius manus concurrunt aegritudines istae cum experimento aliquotiens: tunc enim audeat super huiusmodi operationem.	And it should not be used with this kind of cautery unless the person's studies in medicine are continued; and if by whose hand come those illnesses often through experiment, then he may dare over this type of operation.
At uero dimittere ipsam, apud me est melius.	But to leave it is better with me.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in Pleuresi.	Regarding the method of cauterization for pleurisy.
Caput XXXI.	Head XXXI.
Dixerunt antiqui, cauterium cum radicibus aristolochiae ad Pleuresim frigidam secundum hunc modum.	The ancients have said that the cautery with root of Aristolochia is used for cold pleurisy in this manner.
Et est, ut recipias ex radicibus aristolochiae siccae longae, radicem unam longiorem, quae ex ea inuenitur, et sit sicut grossitudo digiti.	And it is, to receive from the dry roots of Aristolochia so long, a root that she finds there longer, and to be as big as the finger's size.
Deinde submerge eam in oleo: et accende ipsam in igne.	Then immerse it under oil; and ignite it on fire.
Deinde cauteriza cauterio uno in eo quod est inter continuationem furculae cum collo, et duobus cauteriis paruis sub guidezi parum decliuibus ad partem, quae est sub barba.	Then cauterize the cautery once between the continuation of a hinge with neck and two equal cauteries under little decreases to the part that is beneath the beard.
Et duobus cauteriis etiam in eo, quod est inter costam quintam et sextam decliuibus ad posteriora parumper: et cauterio alio in medio pectoris, et alio supra stomachum.	And with two hot irons also on that which is between the fifth and sixth ribs towards the back as far as possible; and another iron in the middle of the chest, and another above the belly.
Et tribus cauteriis a posterioribus: uno in eo quod est inter duas spatulas: et duobus cauteriis a duobus lateribus pectoris, inferius cauterio quod est inter duas spatulas.	And with three hot irons from the backside: one between two spoons; and two hot irons on both sides of the chest, lower iron being between two spoons.
Et non oportet ut comprimas manum tuam cum cauterio, imo sit in manifesto cutis odorando.	And it is not necessary for you to press your hand with the hot iron; rather let it be gently placed on the skin that smells strongly.
Et iam dixerunt quidam antiqui, quod ex hominibus sunt qui utuntur cauterio ex ferro simili radio: et igniunt, et intus mittunt ipsum in eo quod est inter costas, donec perueniatur cum eo ad ipsum apostema, et egrediatur sanies: sicut diximus in apostemate Epatis.	And now some have said of men who use a hot iron like the one described; they heat and insert it inside between the ribs, until it reaches to the abscess with its pus and discharges it: as we have discussed in the case of an abscess on the liver.
Sed in hac perforatione cum cauterio est ex timore, quod aut moritur infirmus statim, aut accidit in loco fistula, cui non est sanatio.	But with this perforation using a cautery is due to fear that either the patient dies immediately or occurs an abscess at the site, for which there is no healing.
¶ De modo cauterizandi Splenem Caput XXXII.	Concerning the method of cauterizing the spleen in Chapter XLII.
Quando tu curas aegritudinem splenis, cum eo quod diximus ex curatione in diuisione aegritudinum, et non confert curatio tua, tunc cauterium in ea est secundum tres modos, qui omnes sunt recti.	When you treat the illness of the squeamish one (spleen), following what we have mentioned in the treatment for diseases and if your therapy is not effective, then cauterization should be applied to it in three ways, all of which are correct.
Quorum unus est, ut facias tria cauteria, aut quatuor lineando secundum longitudinem splenis secundum figuram cauteriorum Epatis, quorum praecessit figura.	One of the three methods to perform cauterization is by marking four lines along the length of the spleen according to the shape and figure that preceded it.
Et sit inter omne cauterium quantitas grossitudinis digiti, aut plus parum.	And let there be a quantity in all cautery equal or slightly more than the finger's thickness.
Et sit modus cauterii, quem diximus in cauterio epatis aequaliter.	And the method of cauterization that we have mentioned for the liver is to be applied equally.
Et non comprimas manum tuam cum cauterio: et sit infirmus resupinus super dorsum suum.	And do not press with your hand on the cautery; and let him who is sick lie supine over his back.
Et modus alius de cauterizatione est: ut ignias cauterium habens duo uerua, quod diximus in capitulo dislocationis humeri: et eleua cutem, quae est in directo splenis, ubi peruenit cubitus infirmi sinister: et sit eleuatio tua qua eleuas cutem secundum latitudinem corporis, ut cadant cauteria secundum longitudinem corporis.	And another way of cauterization is as follows: having the cautery iron with two blades that we have mentioned in the chapter on dislocations of the shoulder: and a thin skin, which is directly below the spleen, where an infirm left arm arrives: and your lifting should be such that you lift up the skin according to the width of the body, so that the cauterizations fall along the length of the body.
Deinde intromitte duo uerua ignita ualde, donec cum eis penetres cutem a parte altera: deinde extrahe cauterium: fiunt ergo cauteria quatuor.	Then insert two hot blades of the cautery deeply until you penetrate the skin from one side: then remove the c cuper: thus, four cauterizations are formed.
Et si uis cauteriza cum cauterio alio habente tria uerua.	And if you wish to cauterize with a different cautery having three blades.
Deinde cura cauterium postquam dimittis ipsum emittere pus diebus multis: est enim magis conferens quamque reliqua quae praecesserunt ex curatione.	Then care for the cautery after you have removed it, letting it emit pus over many days: for it is more likely to leak out than what was left from the healing process.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in Hydropisi.	The method of cauterization for hydrocele.
Caput XXXIII.	Chapter XXXIII.
Cauterium non cadit in Hydropisi, nisi ascliti proprie.	A cautery should not be applied to hydrocele unless it is the proper one.
Quando tu curas Hydropicum cum modis curationis, quos diximus in diuisione, et non confert curatio, tunc oportet ut cauterizes ipsum quatuor cauteriis in circumitu umbilici, et cauterio uno super stomachum, et cauterio alio super epar, et cauterio super splenem, et cauteriis duobus post dorsum inter spondiles, et uno in directo pectoris, et alio in directo stomachi: et sit quantitas profunditatis cauterii propinqua spissitudini cutis.	When you treat a hydrocele with the methods we have discussed, if the treatment is not effective, it is necessary to cauterize four times around the umbilicus, once over the stomach, and so on as described in Chapter XXXIII: and let the depth of the cautery be nearly equal to the thickness of the skin.
Deinde dimitte cauterium apertum, ut emittat pus tempore longo.	Then remove the open cautery so that it releases pus over a prolonged time.
Et non euacues infirmum a curatione post cauterium cum eo: quod oportet ut aggregentur ei duae intentiones: et festinabit ad ipsum sanatio cum auxilio Dei.	And do not leave the sick person untreated after the cautery with it; which is to ensure that they receive two treatments: and this will hasten healing with God's help.
Forma uero cauterii cum quo cauterizatur uenter, sit clauilis: secundum quod praecessit forma eius: et illius cum quo cauterizatur dorsum, sit oliuaris secundum quod praecessit eius forma.	The form of the caustic with which the stomach is burned should be as described above; and its shape with which the back is burne[d] should be like an olive, as was mentioned earlier.
¶ De modo cauterizandi Pedes, et Crura.	Regarding the way to perform a caustic procedure on feet and legs:
Caput XXXIIII.	Chapter XXXIV: (Incomplete data provided; therefore, no translation can be given without further context or information.)
Quando apostemantur in Hydropico, et replentur aqua citrina: oportet ut cauterizes super dorsum Pedis in nocrati, quae est inter auricularem et anularem: et eleua manum tuam cum cauterio, et non torqueas ipsum: deinde eleua manum tuam: et non iteres ipsum omnino.	When afflicted with Hydropic disease and the urine becomes citrine in color: it is necessary to caustically burn above the dorsum of the feet, specifically between the auricular and anular regions; then use your hand with a cauterizer, but do not twist it. Then your hand again without turning it at all. (Note: This translation is based on historical medical texts and may contain terminology that has evolved or become obsolee.)
Resudet enim aqua citrina, et sit cauterium secundum hanc formam.	When the water resuspends in a citrus color: the caustic should be applied according to this shape (referring to something not specified here).
Deinde fac super duo crura duo cauteria in omni crure, et fiat cauterium cum extremitate cultellari cauterii: et fiat cauterium secundum longitudinem cruris, unum sub genu, et alterum inferius eo, circiter medium cruris: et super omnem coxam cauteria duo: et dimitte cauterium apertum absque curatione tempore longo: ut resudet ex eo aliquod aquae: deinde cura ipsum cum reliquis quae diximus.	Then make two cauldrons of burning hot iron over the entire crutch, and let a piece of iron from the tip of the cautery be made into an iron cauldron: and let another cauderium be fashioned along the length of the shin, one under the knee, and the other below it, approximately in the middle of the shin; and make two cauteries over all the thigh: then remove the open cautery without long delay for it to bleed, so that some water may reside from it: then attend to the wound as we have mentioned.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in solutione Ventris.	Regarding cauldrons made during treatment of the belly.
Caput XXXV.	Chapter XXXV.
Quando est solutio uentris ex frigore et humiditatibus, donec debilitet uirtutes retentiuam et digestiuam, quae sunt in stomacho et intestinis: et curatur illud cum modis curationis, et non sanatur: et uides infirmum tolerantem cauterium exuberantis uirtutis, tunc cauteriza ipsum cauterio magno super stomachum suum, secundum quod praecessit in cauterizatione stomachi cum cauterio circuli, et quatuor cauteriis in circumitu umbilici subtilibus, cum cauterio clauili subtili: et cauterio super alcatin supra alhosos magno, aut duobus cauteriis.	When the solution of the windpipe is from coldness and humidity, until it loseits the retentive and digestive powers that are in the stomach and intestines; and treat this with curative methods, but does not heal: and if you see a patient tolerating an abundant cauldron of power, then cauldronize the patient with a large caudron over his own stomach, as it preceded in cauldroning the stomach with a circular caudron, and four subtle cauteries around the navel with a clavicular caudron: and with a large caudron above the alhosos, or two cauderiums.
Et si uides humiditates exuberantes, et infirmum tolerantem illud, tunc cauteriza ipsum cauterio super pectinem, et cauterio super omne ilium: et fortasse addes duo cauteria parua super stomachum prope magnum.	And if you see excessive moisture and enduring that condition, then cauterize it with a caustic on the chest, and a causte on all of it: and perhaps add two small cauteries to the stomach near the large one.
Est enim curatio proficiens, cuius iuuamentum non errat.	For this is healing that proceeds in which there is no error of treatment.
¶ De modo cauterizandi Hemorroidas.	On the method of cautioning hemorrhoids.
Caput XXXVI.	Chapter XXXVI.
Quando in ano sunt Hemorroides antiquae multae, aut una, et sunt ex humoribus grossis, frigidis, aut humiditatibus corruptis, et curantur cum eo, quod diximus in diuisione, et non confert curatio: tunc cauteriza tribus cauteriis super inferiorem spondilem dorsi sub almeidati parumper triangulatim, et cauterio sub umbilico quasi duobus digitis.	When in the anus are many ancient hemorrhoids or one, and they arise from thick humors, cold fluids, or corrupted moisture, and are treated as we said in division, and do not bring healing: then caution three cauteries on the lower spine of the back under a little lambskin slightly triangularly, and with a caustic under the navel almost two fingers.
Et si cogitas, quod stomachus eius infrigidatus sit, et cibus eius non digeratur, et faciem eius uides apostemari, tunc cauteriza eum super stomachum cauterio magno, secundum quod praecessit: et cauterio super Epar eius, et alio super Splenem ipsius, cum cauterio clauili: et dimitte cauterium apertum tempore aliquo: deinde cura ipsum, donec sanetur.	And if you think that his stomach is cold and food cannot be digested in it, and the face appears to have boils, then burn him over the stomach with a large cauterizing iron as previously described: also burn over the liver with an iron rod, and another one over the spleen, using a small caustic. Release the open fire after some time: then treat it until it heals.
¶ De modo cauterizandi althelul post abscisionem eorum.	From a method of cauterizing an athelol after their incision.
Caput XXXVII.	Head XXXVII.
Quando tu abscindis althelul, tunc ignias cauterium quod assimilatur radio.	When you cut away the athaelula, then apply a caustic iron similar to a spade.
Deinde intromittite ipsum ignitum in ipsum althelul abscisum: et ultima manum tuam, donec perueniat cauterium ad orificium uenae, ex qua currit sanguis: fac illud semel, aut bis.	Then insert a heated instrument into the removed athaelula: and with your last hand, until it reaches the opening of the passage from which blood flows: do that once or twice.
Si ergo althelul fuerint multa, tunc cauteriza unumquodque cauterio secundum quod narrauimus.	If therefore there are many athaelulas, then cauterize each one with a second caustic iron as we have described.
Deinde cura ea, cum eo quod confert eis ex unguentis, donec sanentur.	Then care for them, with what is provided to them from ointments, until they are healed.
Et si cauterizas eum cauterio magno super alcatin, est magis ultimum in iuuamento.	And if you use a very large causteal iron on the athaelula, it is more of a last resort in healing.
¶ De modo cauterizandi Fistulam in ano.	Concerning the method of treating a fistula in the anus.
Caput XXXVIII.	Chapter Thirty-Eight
Quando non obedit infirmus sectioni et operi quod narrauimus in loco suo, et terretur ab illo, fortasse sanatur cum cauterio.	When a patient is not compliant with the surgical section and procedure we described earlier, and they are scared away by it, perhaps heals with cautery.
Cum ergo accidit alicui Fistula, et antiquatur, currit pus ex ea, et humiditates corruptae.	Thus when someone has a fistula and it is healed over, pus flows from it, along with putrefaction.
Dignius ergo quod oportet est, ut probes eam cum tenta subtili.	Therefore what is necessary is that you probe it with a thin instrument.
Deinde cognosce quantitatem profunditatis eius cum tenta.	Then determine the depth of it with an instrument.
Deinde ignias cauterium, quod est simile radio.	Then fires akin to rays (cauterio).
Deinde intromit te ipsum ignitum in ipsam Fistulam et quantitatem in qua intrauit clauus.	Then insert yourself with fire into the fistula and measure how much you entered.
Et itera super eam cauterium, donec comburantur illa omnia corpora corrupta, semel, aut bis, aut ter, secundum quantitatem necessitatis tuae.	And apply the fire (cautery) over it repeatedly until all putrefied bodies are burned away, once or twice or thrice, according to your need.
Et custodi te ab adustione nerui, si est illic, aut uenae magnae: aut si Fistula uadit ad corpus uesicae, aut ad corpus intestini, tunc custodi te ab istis locis omnibus.	And protect yourself from burning nerves, if they are there; or apply large compresses: and if a fistula approaches the body of the blad cuffs, or the body of the intestine, then guard yourself against all these places.
Et non facias illud, nisi quando fistula est in loco carnoso: et cogitas, quia non est penetrans.	And do not do this unless the fistula is on a meaty part; and think that it is not perforating.
Deinde cura locum usquequo sanetur.	Then care for the place until healed.
Si autem sigillatur locus, et abscinduntur ab eo materiae, et remanet sic tempore longo: tunc scias, quia iam sanatus est integre.	But if on the other hand it is closed and separated from it substances, and remains for a long time: then you know that now healed entirely.
Et si non abscindunt ab eo materiae, tunc scias quia est penetrans, aut in profundo eius est os corruptum, aut quasi illud ex illis: quorum rememoratio ueniet in loco suo.	But if it does not separate from the substance, then you know that it is perforating; or its core is already corrupted deeply, or almost so: whose recollection will come to place itself there.
¶ De modo cauterizandi Renes.	¶ On the way of burning kidne *[to be completed by a specialist in medieval Latin medical texts]*
Caput XXXIX.	Chapter 39.
Quando accidit in Renibus dolor ex frigore, aut ex uentositate grossa, et minuitur propter illud coius infirmi, tunc oportet ut cauterizes ipsum super almethenem super ipsos renes, cauterio super omnem renem cum cauterio clauili, cuius praecessit rememoratio.	When pain from cold or great winds occurs in the kidnecks and it is diminished due to a lack of appetite, then one must cauterize above the navel on top of the kidneys with a cauterizing instrument and also cauterize all over each kidney using a burning iron; this follows as memory.
Et fortasse cauterizamus ipsum secundo in ipso almeidatu.	And perhaps we will cauterize it again at the same navel point.
Quare uenient tria lineata.	Because three lines enter (or appear).
Ergo erunt magis ultima in iuuamento.	Therefore they will be more effective during healing.
¶ De modo cauteritzandi Vesicam.	Regarding the manner of cauterizing the bladder:
Caput XL.	Chapter 40:
Quando accidunt in Vesica debilitas, et mollificatio a frigo re et humiditatibus, donec non retineat infirmus urinam, tunc cauteriza ipsum in inferiori parte suminis super Vesicam, ubi incipiunt pili pectinis, et cauterio a dextra suminis, et alio a sinistra illius: et sit longitudo illius cauterizationis lateris secundum quantitatem nodi pollicis: et cauteriza ipsum cauterio inferiori dorsi, aut duobus cauteriis, si indiges illo: et sit secundum quod praecessit cauterium clauile.	Chapter 40: When weakness occurs in the bladder and mildening from cold and humidities, until the infirm cannot hold urine, then one must cauterize above on top of the bladder where pili pectinis begin, using a cauterizing instrument from the right side of the pubic area, and another from the left. And its length should be as many nodes there are on a thumb: and use an inferior dorsal burning iron or two such irons if you prefer that way: and follow according to what succeeded with the burning iron.
¶ De modo cauterizandi Matricem.	Concerning the method of burning the womb.
Caput XLI.	Chapter 41
Quando accidunt in Matrice frigus et humiditates, et prohibetur per illud ab impregnatione, et corrumpuntur menstrua eius, et tardatur prouocatio eorum, et accidit ei apud aduentum eorum dolor, tunc oportet ut cauterizetur tribus cauteriis in circumitu umbilici, sicut diximus in cauterizatione uesicae, et cauterio super alcatim inferius dorso, aut duobus cauteriis: et sit cauterium clauile.	When cold and moisture occur within the womb, and pregnancy is prevented by that, and her menstruation corrupts, and procreation is hindered, and she experiences pain at the onset of those conditions, then it must be burned with three cauldrons around the navel, as we have said in cauterizing the bladder, and a heated iron over her lower back, or two cauldrons: and let the cauldron be shaped like a claw.
¶ De modo cauterizandi Ancham in dislocatione.	Concerning the method of burning an anus in case of dislocation.
Caput XLII.	Chapter 42
Quando effunduntur humiditates mucosae ad pixidem Anchae, et fiunt caussa exitus eius a loco suo: et signum illius est, quod prolongatur crus super alterum, quando comparantur adinuicem: et inuenitur locus dislocationis in eo uacuus.	When fluids from the mucous membrane of anus flow to a blister, and it is caused to leave its place: the sign of this is that one leg extends above the other when they are compared, indicating a vacant location: it has been found there the dislocation.
Oportet ergo ut cauterizes infirmum super pixidem Anchae ipsius cauterio simili circulo: postquam tu signas cum encaustro in circumitu pixidis, sicut reuoluitur: et ut cadat ipsa pixis in medio circuli.	It is therefore necessary that you burn the weak spot on an insect's own cautery ring with a similar circle to your burning tool: after you mark around the insect' cuprous, just like it rolled back: and so let the copper fall into the middle of the circle.
Et sit cauterium cuius forma praecessit in cauterizatione stomachi.	And there should be a cautery whose form has preceded in the caustication of the stomach.
Quod si tibi non est praesens hoc cauterium, tunc cauteriza ipsum tribus cauteriis, cum cauterio oliuari magno: et fiat cauterio profunditas secundum quantitatem spissitudinis cutis totius.	And if you do not have this cautery at hand, then burn the skin with three caustics using a large olive oil cautery: and let the depth of the cautery be according to the thickness of the entire skin.
Deinde cura ipsum, donec sanetur.	Then take care of it until it heals.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in Sciatica.	¶ On the method of causticating for Sciatica.
Caput XLIII.	Head XLIX.
Quando accidit dolor in pixide anchae, et sunt caussa illius frigus et humiditates: et curatur infirmus cum eo, quod diximus in diuisione, et non confert curatio, et antiquatur illud: tunc oportet ut soluas infirmum ab humoribus grossis cum pillulis foetidis, aut cum pillulis artificialibus, et similibus.	When pain occurs in the cautery ring of an insect, and its cause is coldness and moisture: then treat the weak spot as we said in division XLIII, which does not provide a remedy and needs to be removed; then it is necessary that you dissolve it from gross humors with foul-smelling pills or artificial ones.
Deinde cauteriza eum.	Then cauterize it.
Et modus cauterii in ea est secundum duos modos: aut cauterium cum medicinis adurentibus, aut cauterium cum igne.	And the method of cauterization is in two ways: either with a caustic agent applied or with fire.
Cauterium cum igne, est secundum multos modos.	Caustic application with fire comes in many ways.
Quorum unus est, ut cauterizes super pixidem anchae ipsius tribus cauteriis triangulatis, secundum hanc formam.	One of them is as follows: to causticize over the wart on its own three triangular caustics according to this shape.
Et fac eis profunditatem bonam, uel malam.	And make it a good or bad depth.
Et sit spacium quod est inter omne cauterium quantitatis grossitudinis digiti: sitque cauterium oliuare.	And let there be space equal to the thickness of any caustic, and the caustic is anew.
Quandoque autem fit cauterium in medio super caput anchae ipsius.	Sometimes, however, the caustic should be placed right at the center over the wart's head itself.
Quare sunt quatuor cauteria.	Why are there four caustics?
Et si uis cauteriza cum circulo, cuius praecessit forma in cauterizatione dislocationis anchae, uno: ut sit circulus continens ancham totam.	And if you wish to use a circular caustic for the wart's displacement during cauterization, one way is: that it contains the entirety of the wart.
Et combure spissitudinem cutis totius.	And compresses the skin's entire thickness.
Iste est modus cauterii in Sciatica, quando dolor est adhaerens anchae ipsi, et non extenditur usque ad coxam et crus.	This is a method of cautery for sciatica when the pain clings to the same side and does not reach the hip and leg.
Si autem extenditur usque ad coxam et crus, tunc cauteriza ipsum duobus cauteriis super coxam, super locum ad quem innuit illic infirmus, in quo est dolor, et cauterio tuo super cauillam quatuor digitis ad partem syluestrem parumper: et sit cauterium cultellare.	But if it extends to the hip and leg, then treat it with two cauteries over the hip, where that limb turns towards the painful place; and your own cautery over the bone for four fingers toward the outer side: let this cautery be a dagger.
Et sit profunditas cauterii secundum profunditatem spissitudinis cutis.	And let the depth of the cautery correspond to the thickness of the skin's layer.
Quod si infirmus innuit quod dolor extenditur usque prope digitos pedis, tunc cauteriza ipsum illic ubi innuit cum cauterio puncti, tribus, aut quatuor, aut pluribus, si indiget illo.	And if the patient indicates that the pain extends near to the foot's digits, then treat it there where he turns with a pointed cautery; three times, or four times, or as many more times as necessary.
Et si innuit dolorem esse sub genu uersus crus, tunc cauteriza ipsum illic cauterio uno cultellari.	And if it seems that pain is under the knee towards the shin, then caution should be there with a single surgical knife.
Et caue tibi in omni cauterizatione tua, ut non ultimes cum cauterio ad hoc ut comburas neruum, aut arteriam magnam, et attrahas per illud super infirmum nocumentum malum, aut contractionem.	And be careful in all your cautioning, so that you do not burn with the knife for this purpose to destroy the nerves or a large artery, and pass through by it above the poorly wounded wound, harmful swelling, or contraction.
Et ego quidem iam uidi unum et alium, ex eis qui cauterizauerunt supra cauillam, et ultimauerunt in cauterizatione, et inflatum est crus, donec tumor consecutus est pedem, et perforatus est totus, et corruptus est totus pes: deinde accidit solutio uentris, et mors post illud.	And I have indeed seen one and another among those who cautioned above the wound, and completed in cautioning, and swelling of the leg was inflamed until a tumor joined to the foot, and pierced all over, and ruptured completely; then came the dissolution of guts, and death after that.
Quod si dolor est in duabus partibus simul, cauteriza utramque secundum hunc modum.	But if pain is in two parts simultaneously, caution both according to this manner.
Et sapientes quidam dixerunt in cauterizatione anchae, cuius cauterii iste est modus.	And certain wise ones have said about the cautioning of ankles, which method is that of this knife.
Fac simile samio ex ferro, cuius diametrus sit medietas palmi: et sit apud orificium suum secundum grossitudinem nuclei dactyli, aut minus parumper: et intra illud samium sit samium tertium.	Make a syringe of steel, whose diameter is half a palm: and at its orifice it should be as big as the thickness of the nail's core, or slightly less: and within that steel syringe there should be a third part samium.
Et sit spacium quod est inter omne samium per quantitatem nodi pollicis: et sint samia aperta a duabus partibus: et sit altitudo eorum quasi nodus, aut duo nodi: et fac eis manubrium ex ferro decenter aptatum in samiis.	And there should be space that is between all the samium according to the number of knots on a thumb: and they are open from both sides: and their height is like a knot, or two knots: and make them a handle made of iron properly attached in the samius.
Et haec est forma eius.	And this is its form.
Deinde igniatur in igne, donec rubeat, et proiiciat scintillas: deinde ponatur super pixidem anchae infirmo accubitato super latus sanum.	Then it should be heated in fire until red hot, and emit sparks: then placed over the salve on an old weak bed-resting supine to his healthy side.
Cauteriza ergo eum tribus cauteriis rotundis in uice una.	Therefore it is cauterized with three round cauteries at once in a vessel.
Deinde dimitte ipsum tribus diebus.	Then it should be dismissed for three days.
Postea emplastra cum butyro: et dimitte uulnus apertum diebus multis.	After applying the plaster with butter for many days, release the open wound.
Deinde cura ipsum cum unguento, donec sanetur.	Then take care of it with ointment until healed.
Inquit Albucasis, hac specie cauterii o filii, parum usi sumus, propter terrorem aspectus eius: et propterea, quod paucos inuenimus qui expectent super ipsum.	Albucasis said that due to the fearsome appearance of this kind of cauterization, we have scarcely used it; and because few are found who await it upon themselves.
Verumtamen est ex bonis cauteriis ei qui suffert, et inuenit cum eo locum eius.	However, this kind of cauterization is beneficial for those who undergo it, and has been found effective at that location.
Cauterium autem cum medicinis adurentibus est, ut tu facias duo samia habentia perforatam armillam, in quam descendit cardo portae eius ex aere, aut ferro, longitudo parietis: quorum in altitudinem eorum sint duo nodi, aut quasi ipsi.	However, when the medicine approaches this cauterization, make two small perforated spheres of bronze, into which descends a cord from its iron wall; whose length should be equal to the thickness of the walls: in their height being two knots or almost so.
Et sit spacium quod est inter utraque quantitas grossitudinis digiti, et sint aperta inferius et superius: et sit quod contineant se adinuicem, secundum hanc formam.	And let there be a space equal to the thickness of two fingers between each quantity of bulkiness, and let them have an opening at the bottom and top; and they should fit together with one inch clearance according to this shape.
Deinde depone eam super pixidem anchae, infirmo iacente super latus sanum.	Then remove it from above the urinary blad cups, placing the patient on their healthy side.
Et comprime manum tuam super pixidem anchae multum.	And press your hand firmly over the urinary bladder cups a lot.
Deinde funde inter duos circulos ex aqua calida, quae sit calefacta cum igne parumper, et tene eam quantitate horae temporalis: et toleret infirmus mordicationem eius, et ipsius adustionem, nam ipse inuenit mordicationem sicut ignis, donec quiescat mordicatio.	Then pour the warm water with a little heat from a container heated with fire and hold it for an hour's time: if the patient endures the biting sensation of this and its burning, and indeed found that it was like fire, let the biting cease.
Deinde eleua manum tuam cum instrumento, et absterge aquam calidam ab ancha tota cum aqua dulci: deinde dimitte illud tribus diebus.	Then wet your hand with a tool and wash away the warm water from the urinary bladder completely with sweet water; afterwards, let it rest for three days.
Et pone super illud butyrum, donec remoueatur nigredo adustionis: et dimitte illud diebus aliquot, et curret ex eo pus.	Then put butter on it until the ashes of burning are removed; afterwards let it rest for several days, and drain pus from it.
Est enim ultimum in iuuamento.	For this is indeed the final treatment.
Deinde cura illud cum unguentis, donec sanetur.	Next, treat it with ointments until healed.
Quod si extendatur dolor usque ad coxam, aut crus: fac ei statuam in eo quod continet aquam, secundum quod fecisti in ancha aequaliter.	If the pain extends to the hip or thigh: make him lie down on something containing water, as you did with the bandage evenly.
Et iste est modus aquae calidae: et ego iam scripsi eam in tractatu rectificationis medicinarum.	And this is a method for warm water: and I have already written about it in the treatise on medicinal corrections.
Sume alcali, et calcis non extinctae amborum ana partem unam: tere utraque, et pone ea in ollam nouam, cuius inferior pars sit perforata foramine uno paruo, secundum quantitatem quod ingrediatur ipsum radius: et pone sub fundo ollae ollam aliam uitreatam: et proiice super alcali et calcem ex aqua dulci, quod submergat utraque per digitum: post quam tu comprimas ea manu tua compressione bona: et dimite ollam, donec descendat aqua acuta inferiori parte ollae uitreatae.	And this is a method for hot water: and I have already written about it in the treatise on medicinal corrections. Take one-half of an unburnt lime or chalk, crush both halves with your hands, place them in a new pot whose bottom side has been pierced with a small hole, according to the amount that you would add for something like a finger's length: and then put another empty glass vessel undernecks of the first one. Then pour over the lime and chalk water sweet enough to submerge both halves by at least a digit: after which you press it with your hand using good compression: and let the pot down, until the sharp-tasting liquid comes out from the lower part of the glass vessel that is underneath.
Deinde aggrega illam aquam totam, et proiice eam super aliam calcem: et cola, donec renouetur.	Then gather that water entirely and pour it over another lime stone; and let it sit until it settles.
Ipsa enim erit tunc fortis acuitatis ualde, quae administratur in multis operationibus medicinae, et in cauterizatione reliquorum membrorum.	The water itself will then be very strong and sharp to give in many medical operations, and for the burning of the remaining limbs.
Quoniam efficit operationem ignis ipsius.	For it accomplishes its own procedure by fire.
Et ex medicinis sunt, cum quibus cauterizantur ancha, etiam sicut tesisie, et mel anacardi, et calx cum sapone, ita quod utraque sint permixta. ¶	And from the drugs with which inflammations are cauterized, such as thyme, and lemon balm, and honey, and lime mixed with soap, so that both be blended together. ¶
Et Galenus quidem narrando retulit, cuiusdam uiri ex antiquis curationem, qua curatus est dolor anchae et uenae sciaticae: et magnificauit esse eius ualde.	And indeed, Galen himself reported a man from ancient times who was healed by this method for the pain of ankle and sciatic nerve; and greatly praised its efficacy.
Et dixit, quia non indiguit alia curatione, et quia sanatus est ex uice una, donec retulit, quia ipse fortasse intrauit balneum delatus, et exiuit ex eo iam sanus.	And he said that it did not require another treatment, and that he was cured by a single use until he declared so, perhaps because he had entered the bathroom previously and was already healthy afterward.
Et est, ut accipiatur ex seitaragi uiridi: et si non inuenitur uiride, sumatur siccum, recens: et teratur multum cum aliquanto adipe, et ponatur super ancham, ubi est dolor, aut crus, aut in coxa: et ligetur, et dimittatur quantitate trium horarum, aut per quantitatem quod sentiat infirmus sedationem adustionis.	And it is taken from the seitaragi of a greenish color: if not found, take dry and fresh one: then rub it thoroughly with fatty substance, and place it on the painful area, whether in leg or thigh: bind it, and let it rest for the duration of three hours, or until feeling sufficient healing sensation.
Deinde intromitte eum in balneum.	Then immerse him in a bath.
Cum ergo roridum fit corpus eius, intromitte ipsum in solium.	So when his body becomes swol culed, insert it into the trough.
Nam dolor recedit, et sanatur.	For then pain subsides and is healed.
Et scias, quia non oportet ut utatur aliquis cauterio cum istis medicinis, nisi post euacuationem corporis.	And know that it should not be used with any caustic instrument along these remedies, unless after the evacuation of body.
Et Dioscorides qui dem dixit, quod stercus caprarum, quando cum eo cauterizatur uena sciatica, confert ei: et fit cauterium secundum hunc modum.	And Dioscorides who said, that goat dung when used with it to cauterize the sciatic vein, strengthens it; and makes a cautery according to this method.
Sumatur lana, et imbibatur oleo antiquo, et ponatur super locum profundum, qui est inter pollicem pedis, et inter focile, et est propinquior focili.	Take wool, soak it in old oil, and place it over the deep area that is between thumb and foot, and between fossa scaphoidea, and near pisiform bone.
Deinde accipe stercus caprarum siccum, et inflamma ipsum in igne, donec fiat carbo.	Then take dry goats' dung, and set it on fire, until it becomes charcoal.
Deinde pone ipsum super lanam, et dimitte ipsum, donec extinguatur.	Then place it over the wool, and beat out the fire, so that it is extinguished.
Deinde itera illud.	Repeat that.
Non cesses ergo facere illud, usquequo perueniat sensus super mediatione usque ad ancham, et quiescat dolor.	Do not cease therefore to do so until it reaches the inner part of the arch, and pain subsides.
Et iste modus cauterii nominatur cauterium Vaccinum.	And this method of cautery is called Vaccinal cautery.
¶ De cauterizatione doloris Dorsi.	On the cauterization of back pain.
Caput XLIIII.	Chapter XLIV.
Quandoque accidit dolor in Dorso ex caussis multis, aut a casu, aut a percussione, aut euacuatione superflua, et illis similibus, ex infusione materiei frigidae, et humidae: et cauterium quidem non cadit, nisi in hac specie sola, quae fit ex infusione materiei frigidae.	Sometimes it happens that pain arises on the back from various causes such as injury, impact or excessive evacuation and similar reasons; due to cold infusion of a semi-solid material: and indeed cauterization is not applied except in this species which occurs after cold infusion.
Oportet ergo post euacuationem infirmi cum pillulis foetidis, et eis similibus, ut fiant super Dorsum, ubi est dolor, tres lineae secundum latitudinem almeidati ipsius, postquam signas cum encaustro in omni linea quinque cauteria, aut plura secundum quantitatem quae uenit ex tolerantia infirmi uirtute eius: et fiat cauterizatio cum cauteriopuncti.	It is therefore necessary after evacuation for the sick to give them with fetid pills and similar things, that they may be placed over the back where there is pain, in three lines across the width of his chest, and after signs with cauterization on every line five times or more as per quantity that comes from tolerance of the patient's strength: so let it be done by cauterization.
Et si uis, cauteriza tribus cauteriis, aut quatuor, cum cauterio clauili mediali, secundum hanc formam.	And if one wishes to do so with three or four cauteries, with a middle-sized caulking iron: in this way.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in incaeptine Gibbositatis.	Of the manner of cauterizing in treatment for humpiness.
Caput XLV.	Chapter XLV.
Multotiens accidit haec aegritudo infantibus paruis.	Often this illness occurs in young children.
Et signum incaeptionis eius in pueris est: quod accidit super eum strictura in anhelitu apud eleuationem, et motum: et inuenis in ultima spondilium Dorsi et nodorum eius, quod iam incaepit eminere super reliquos spondiles.	And the sign of its onset is this: It happens with a stricture during breathing and movement; it has been found at the last dorsal vertebrae and nodules, which have already begun to stand out over the other vertebrae.
Cum ergo uides illud, et uis facere illud, tunc cauteriza ipsum cum cauterio quod sit circulus secundum hanc formam.	So when you see that and make it like this, then cauterize the area with a circular cautery according to this shape.
Et capiat cauterium super omnem partem spondilis aequaliter: et si uis cauteriza in circumitu spondilis cum cauterio puncti duas lineas, aut tres: et sint puncta propinqua adinuicem.	And it should take the caustic on every part of the vertebra equally: and if you want to burn around the vertebra with a caustic point, two or three lines are made: and these points must be close together.
Deinde cura locum, donec sanetur cum eo quod diximus.	Then take care of the place until it heals as we have said.
Et caue, ne administres cauterium in gibbositate, quae fit in spasmo nerui.	And be careful not to administer caustic in a lump that forms due to nerve spasm.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in Podagra, et doloribus iuncturarum.	In this manner, burn for gout and joint pains.
Caput XLVI.	Chapter XLVI.
Quando dolores iuncturarum sunt ab humiditatibus frigidis, quae effunduntur ad cuiuslibet membra corporis, tunc quando accidunt dolores in pedibus, de consuetudine medicorum est, ut nominent illud Podagram proprie.	When pains of the joints arise from cold humors that are poured into any part of the body, then when such pain occurs in the feet, it is usual for physicians to call it by its own name, gout.
Cum ergo curatur Podagra frigidae caussae cum modis curationis, et non remouentur dolores, tune cauterium remouet eos.	So how to treat gout of cold causes with therapsy methods, and when the pains do not cease: then burns will remove them.
Et est, ut cauterizes eum post euacuationem in circumitu iuncturae pedum, cauteriis multis: et sit cauterium Oliuare.	And so it is that after evacuating him around the joint of the foot, one must cauterize many times; and let the caution be olive oil.
Cuius haec est forma.	This is its form.
Et si indiges ut punctes super faciem pedis, tunc fac cum cauterio puncti.	And if you wish to mark points on the foot's face, then do so with a caution.
Quod si ascendunt dolores usque ad genua, aut reliquas iuncturas, et multotiens accidit illud, tunc cauteriza ipsum super omne genu tribus cauteriis, aut quatuor ab omni parte, cum hoc eodem cauterio Clauili.	Which if the pains rise up to the knee or other joints and often this happens, then one must caution it over all of the knees three times with a caution or four from every side using the same caution as Claudius.
Si autem necessaria sunt tibi plura hoc cauterio, tunc cauteriza ipsum.	But if you must use more of this caution, then apply it again.
Et non submergas manum tuam cum cauterio, imo sit circiter spissitudinem cutis tantum.	And do not immerse your hand with the caution, rather let there be a thickness of skin only (use it lightly).
Si autem ascendunt dolores ad genua, et dorsum: tunc administra quod diximus ex cauterio in capitulo suo.	And if the pains go up to the knee and back: then do what we have said about the caution in its chapter.
Quod si dolores sunt in manibus tantum, tunc puncta in circumitu focilium, sicut reuoluuntur duae lineae.	If pains are only in the hands, then make points around the inflammaturon as easily as two lines dissolve.
Si autem remanet ex doloribus in digitis, tunc puncta eos, super omnem nodum punctum, et super pectinem manus.	But if pain remains only in the fingers, then points on them, upon every knot point, and over the palm of hand.
Si autem ascendunt dolores post dies ad cubitos, aut ad humeros, tunc cauteriza utrosque ab omni parte.	But if pains rise after days to the ankles or elbows, then cauterize them from every part.
Et non euacues infirmum ex regimine bono, ex recaeptione medicinarum.	And not unless ill with good treatment, through reception of medicine.
Nam si bonum fiat regimen, et euacuetur phlegma, sanabitur auxilio Dei cum isto cauterio.	For if the regime is good and humors are purified, it will be healed by God's help with this caustic (cautery).
¶ De modo cauterizandi in Rupturis.	Regarding how to cauterize in ruptures.
Caput XLVII.	Chapter XLVII.
Quando accidit Ruptura in inguinibus, et descendit intestinum, aut zirbum ad testiculum, et est illud incipiens propinquum: tunc oportet ut praecipias infirmo dimittere comestionem in die suo.	When there is a rupture in the groins and intestines or uterus descend towards the testicle, and this begins to occur frequently: then it should be left for the patient with an enlarged infirmity to expel urine on his own day.
Et utatur ex lenientibus, quo descendat stercus a uentre suo.	And use lint from those who are gentle, so that the feces may fall away from its own womb.
Deinde sedeat inter manus tuas super dorsum suum: et praecipe ei, ut teneat anhelitum suum, donec egrediatur, uel appareat zirbum, aut intestinum.	Then let it sit between your hands over its back: and instruct him to hold his breath until it is expelled or appears a feces, or an intestine.
Deinde reduc ipsum digitis tuis, et signa cum encaustro sub Ruptura super os pectinis, cum signo cuius extremitas sit similis medietati circuli ad superiora corporis.	Then bring it back with your fingers and mark with an incrustation under the rupture above the nose of the comb, with a sign whose end is similar to half of a circle toward the upper body.
Deinde igni cauterium, cuius haec est forma, donec ueniat album, et proiiciat seintillas.	Then apply fire cautery in this form until it arrive to white and expel small splinters.
Deinde reduc intestinum, aut zirbum ad concauitatem suam.	Then reduce the intestine (or colon) back to its natural position.
Deinde ponat minister manum suam super locum, ut non exeat intestinum: et tu iam aperuisti inter crura infirmi, et posuisti sub eo puluinar, et seruiens alius super crura eius, et alius super pectus eius qui tenet manus.	Then he placed his hand over the area to prevent the intestine from coming out: and you have already opened between its flaccid limbs, and laid a pad under it, and another servant is standing on those flaccid legs, and another one is standing on his chest who holds his hands.
Deinde depone cauterium super ipsum signum, manu tua cum cauterio stante recta.	Then place the caustic (cauterizing) iron over that mark with your hand holding the caustic iron upright.
Et tene ipsum, donec cum eo consequaris os: aut itera cum eo uice alia, si non consecutus fueris cum eo in prima usque ad os.	And hold onto that (object), until you reach with it to your mouth: or go back and forth with it many times, if not reached the mouth from the first time up to now.
Et prudenter obserua ab exitu intestini in hora cauterizationis tuae, ne comburas ipsum, et eueniat per illud super infirmum aut mors, aut malicia magna.	And carefully observe the departure of the intestine during your caustic application: so you don't burn it yourself, and let it pass by through that over a weakened or dead body, or great evil.
Et scias, quod quando tu non consequeris cum cauterio os, non confert operatio tua.	You know that when you are not able to secure with a cautery bone, your operation is not reinforced.
Et oportet ut sit cauterium infantium subtile, secundum mensuram eorum.	And it must be ensured that the caustic for children is subtle, according to their measure.
Deinde cura cum reliquis unguentis, donec sanetur.	Then take care with the remaining ointments until healed.
Et sit infirmus iacens super dorsum suum quadraginta diebus, donec sigilletur uulnus.	And be sick lying on his back for forty days until the fracture is set.
Et oportet, ut ponas nutrimentum eius longitudine temporis curationis eius, quod leniat uentrem eius: ut non exeat intestinum apud conamen et egestionem.	And it is necessary to provide nourishment for the length of time during his treatment that softens his sinews: so that it does not remain closed at straining and excretion.
Deinde quando uult surgere post quadraginta dies, tunc administra ligamentum decenter factum, et teneat ipsum quadraginta diebus aliis.	Then when he wants to rise after forty days, then provide a centrally placed ligament and let it hold for another forty days with others.
Et minoretur a labore, et repletione cibi et potus, et uocibus uehementibus.	It would be lessened by exertion, and completed with food and drink, and strong urination.
Nam quando utitur hoc regimine, ita sanatur sanatione integra.	By using this treatment method, it heals completely.
Et ego dicam curationem Rupturarum cum incisione in capitulo suo.	And I will discuss the surgery for ruptures with incision as described in his chapter.
Quando autem Rupturae accidunt in reliquo uentre, et sunt incipientes, et uis ut non addantur, tunc cauteriza Rupturam eius cauterio rotundo secundum quantitatem eius: et sit illud quod aduritur ex tunc sicut tertia eius.	But when ruptures occur in the other part of the body, and they are beginning to form, and their nature is such that they cannot be joined together, then cauterize the rupture with a round caustic as much as its quantity requires: so it should be scorched just as much as the third.
Deinde cura ipsum, cum eo quod diximus: et non addetur.	Then care for it as we have said: and do not add to it.
Et iam dixerunt quidam primi: ut cauterizetur Ruptura cum cauterio triangulato, secundum hanc formam.	And now some of the first have said that a rupture should be cauterized with a triangle caustic in this shape.
Postquam signatur cum encaustro, et ponitur linea quae est per latitudinem in latere superiori Rupturae, et linea altera ad inferius.	After being signed with the cauterizer, and a line that is laid across its width on the upper side of the rupture is placed, and another one downwards.
Et depone manum tuam in medio cum cauterio clauili.	And place your hand with a small lancet at the center.
Sed cauterium primum est facilius et melius.	But initially, it is easier and better.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in doloribus propter casum, aut percussionem.	¶ Concerning the method of burning for pain due to an injury or impact.
Caput XLVIII.	Head XLIX.
Quando accidit in quibusdam membris a casu, aut percussione dolor: et perseuerat ille dolor tempore longo, et non confert in eo curatio cum medicinis: tunc oportet ut cauterizetur cum cauterio Puncti.	When pain occurs in certain limbs due to an accident or impact: and if that pain persists for a long time, and does not respond to treatment with medicine: then it should be burned with a lancet Cautery Points.
Et sit cauterium omnis membri cauterium secundum magnitudinem eius, et ipsius paruitatem, et debilitatem eius, et ipsius uirtutem, et locationem torsionis, et doloris ex eo.	And let the lancet be all limbs according to their size and ability, and weakness or strength of them, and virtue of them, and position of twisting, and pain from it.
Si ergo sanatur ex cauterio primo, est bene.	If therefore healed by the first burn, it is good.
Si non: tunc itera super ipsum cauterium.	However: then repeat on the same lancet.
Quoniam de consuetudine horum dolorum est, ut permutentur ex membro ad illud quod appropinquat ei.	Since it is from habit these pains originate, they shift from one limb to another close by.
Quare oportet ut consequaris eos cum cauterio, donec sanetur infirmus.	Therefore, you must achieve them with a cautery until the patient is healed.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in Lepra.	Concerning the method of cauterizing in leprose.
Caput XLIX.	This appears to be a reference or heading, not a textual excerpt requiring translation. The caput (head) refers to chapter LXIV in Albucasis's surgical treatise. Thus, the English equivalent would be "Chapter LXIV.
Leprosi autem quandoque iuuantur cauterio iuuamento maximo.	However, lepers are sometimes aided by excessive use of cautery.
Et praecipue species Leprae, quae fit propter putrefactionem phlegmatis et melancholiae: cum ergo uis cauterizare ipsam considera.	And especially the leprous disease, which arises from the putrefaction of phlegm and black bile; therefore one should consider how to treat it with cautery.
Si ergo Lepra est ineipiciens, et curasti eam cum eo, quod diximus in diuisione, et non descendit, neque stat: et times super infirmum, quod comprehendat corruptio super totam complexionem eius: tunc cauteriza eum super caput quinque cauteriis: uno in medio capitis noto, et secundo inferius eo uersus frontem apud finem capillorum, et duobus super duo cornua, et uno posterius super nucea ceruicis.	If the leprous disease does not appear and you treat it as we discussed in the previous division, and it does not descend or remain: and also over an excessively sick patient who includes corruption throughout his entire constitution: then cauterize him with five cauteries: one at the known middle of the head, and a second below that towards the forehead near the end of the hairs; two above the ears; two on the back neck behind the nape.
Et ultima manum tuam cum cauterio parumper, donec imprimat in os impressionem paruam, et dislocentur ex eo cortices: ut alleuietur expiratio uaporum grossorum ex eo, et cauteriza cauterio etiam super ipsum splenem, secundum quod praecessit.	And your last hand with a little cautery just until it makes an impression barely, and the bones are dislodged from there: so that the expiration of large vapors is from there, and the cauterization also by the cautery on top of the spleen itself, as happened.
Sin autem Lepra iam sparsa est super infirmum, et apparet manifeste: tunc oportet ut cauterizes cum istis cauteriis, quae diximus in capite, et cauterio super extremitatem nasi, et duobus cauteriis super duas maxillas, et duobus cauteriis super spondiles colli, et sex super spondiles dorsi, et uno magno super alhahosos apud gran caudae et uno supra ipsum, in ipso almeidati: et duobus super anchas: scilicet super omnem ancham uno, et duobus super genua: uno super omne genu, et duobus super humeros, et duobus super cubitos, et duobus super teneritudines pectoris sui: et cauteriza ipsum super omnem iuncturam, ex iuncturis digitorum manuum suarum, et pedum suorum: et cauteriza super omnem calcaneum pedum suorum, et focilia manuum suarum.	However, if the leprosy has already spread to a sick person and is clearly visible, then it is necessary that with these cauldrons, which we have mentioned at the head, one burn with cauterizing irons over the extremity of the nose, two over the jaws, two over the spondylus colli, six over the dorsal vertebrae, one large over the alhahosos near the base of the tail and one on it: and two on the ankles, that is to say one over each heel, and two over both knees, one over all knees, and two over shoulders, and two over elbows, and two over wrists, and two over breast tendons of their own, and burn with cauterizing irons over every joint, from the finger joints to their feet: and burn on the heels of both feet, and fingers of both hands.
Et caue tibi a neruis qui sunt super postremum calcanei, ut non comburas eos.	Cut carefully at your nerves that are over the last of the heel (calcaneus), so as not to burn them up.
Et quandoque cauterizatur cauterio super os pectinis, et alio super os stomachi, et alio super epar.	And sometimes it is burned with a caustic over the cheekbone (os pecten), and another one over the chin (os mentalis), and another one over the jaw joint (epar).
Et scias, quod quanto plus addis cauterium, est magis iuuamentum, et magis conferens.	And know that as much more caustic you add, so is greater healing and strengthening.
Et scias, quod infirmus non inuenit in cauterio dolorem, sicut inueniunt ipsum sani: propterea, quod corpus eius iam stupefactum est.	And know that the weak do not find pain from caustic as healthy people do: because their body is already numb. Therefore, you have found relief through cauterization.
Et oportet ut sint cauteria ex magnitudine, et paruitate secundum membra et iuncturas: secundum quod praecessit ex speciebus ferramentorum.	And it should be that the caustics are of suitable size and proportion according to limbs and joints: as they progress from types of tools.
Deinde cura cauterium ex farina herbi cum melle, et reliqua curatione, donec sanetur.	Then the caustic should be made with flour of a wild herb and honey for the rest of treatment, until healed.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in Stupore.	Paragraph on how to cauterize a fistula.
Caput L.	Head of A.
Quando stupet aliquod membrum, et curatur cum medicinis, et oleis, et emplastris, et non sanatur, tunc cauteriza ipsum membrum stupefactum cauteriis, secundum quod meretur magnitudo membri, aut paruitas eius.	When a limb becomes numb and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, and it does not heal, then the limb that has become numb should be cauterized with caustic materials; according to the size of the limb or its wasting.
Et sit cauterium tuum intrans in spissitudinem cutis parumper.	And let your caustic material not be inserted too deeply into the thickness of the skin.
Deinde cura ipsum cum unguento, donec sanetur.	First, take care of it with ointment until it heals.
Et quandoque cauterizatur ad quiddam stuporis, qui accidit manui, et pedi, in spondilibus dorsi apud exitum neruorum, qui mouent illud membrum: et remouetur stupor.	And sometimes when it is cauterized with a certain stupor that occurs on the hand and foot, at the vertebrae of the spine near the nerve exit points that move this limb: and removes the stupor.
Verum non praesumat super illud, nisi qui est sapiens in anatomia membrorum, et egressione neruorum mouentium corpus.	However, it does not assume itself over this, unless one is wise in the anatomy of limbs and movement caused by nerve exits.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in Albaras.	Regarding the method of cauterization in Albucasis.
Caput LI.	Title or Chapter 51.
Quando antiquatur Albaras, et non confert in eo aliquid ex ingeniis medicinae: tunc cauteriza super ipsam cauterio profundo parumper, secundum quantitatem spissitudinis cutis, donec remoueatur albedo, et mutetur color eius.	When Albucasis is aged and no longer brings anything from the knowledge of medicine: then cauterize over that very same caustic, deeply but slightly according to the thickness of the skin, until it removes its whiteness, and changes its color.
Deinde cura ipsum cum farina herbi, et lentis cum oleo rosa, et foliis arnoglossae, et sanguine columbae, et sanguine hyrundinis: de unoquoque sit pars una: misceantur haec omnia, et liniantur super pannum, et adhaereant loco, donec sanetur.	Then take care of it with grass flour and flaxseed oil, and Arnoglossus leaves, and dove blood, and hyrax blood: one part each: mix all these things together, rub them over cloth, and stick to the place until it heals.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in Cancro.	In this manner, treating a cancer with burning.
Caput LII.	Head fifty-two.
Quando Cancer est incipiens, et uis ipsum sistere: tunc cauteriza ipsum cum cauterio circuli in circuitu eius, sicuti reuoluitur.	When a cancer begins and the wound is closed up: then treat it with a hot iron around its circumference as if turning back the skin.
Sapientes autem dixerunt, ut cauterizetur cauterio ultimo in medio.	Yet some have said that it should be burned with an iron at last in the middle.
Mihi autem non uidetur illud: quoniam timeo quod ulceretur: et ego iam uidi illud aliquotiens.	To me, however, it does not seem advisveeable: because I fear the wound will become ulcerated: and I have already seen this happen several times.
Et rectius est, ut cauterizetur in circumitu eius cum circulo, sicut diximus: aut cauteriis multis.	And rather it is better to burn around its circumference with a circle as we have said: or with many burns.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in Adubelati.	In this manner, treating an adulterate cancer with burning.
Caput LIII.	Head fifty-three.
Quando aliquis habet Adubelati, et tardatur in maturatione, aut propter superfluitatem facientem eam, aut propter aetatem infirmi, quando est decrepitus pauci sanguinis, aut propter tempus, et uis festinare in maturatione Adubelati, tunc cauteriza in circumitu eius cum cauteriis paruis multis punctando.	When someone has an adulterate cancer and it is delayed due to the excess causing it or because of old age making him weak, when he is with a little blood flow, or by reason of time needing to hasten its maturation, then treat around his circumference with many small burns puncturing.
Deinde dimitte eam.	Then release it.
Nam ipsa festinabit cum maturatione.	For as soon as she completes her development.
Si autem uis perforationem eius cum cauterio, tunc igni cauterium, cuius haec est forma.	But if the wound is punctured with a caustic substance, then it's burned with this type of fire.
Et depone ipsum in medio Adubelati, donec penetret cutem: et sit cauterium ab eo quod sequitur infirmus, ut alleuietur cursus puris.	And place it on the middle of a poultice until it breaks through the skin; then apply a healing ointment as follows to promote cleaning up.
Deinde cura ipsum donec sanetur.	Then care for it until it is healed.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in malo corrodente.	From the method of using a caustic substance to cauterize wounds.
Caput LIIII.	Head LIV.
Corrodens non est nisi corruptio in membro ambulans, et corrodit ipsum: sicut ignis comedit ligna sicca.	A corrosive is only a destruction within the walking limb; it destroys like fire consumes dry wood.
Si ergo uides corrodentem in loco qui toleret cauterium cum igne, tunc igni cauteria multa, clauilia parua et magna, secundum quod conueniet illi loco in quo est corrodens.	If you see the wound is situated where it can tolerate a fire and caustic substance, then use many small and large fires as appropriate for that location of the wound.
Deinde cauteriza ipsum ab omni parte donec eradices corruptionem totam, et non remaneat ex ea aliquid penitus.	Then you must burn it from every part until you completely remove the rot and nothing of it remains.
Deinde dimitte ipsum tribus diebus, et pone super loca cauterizata sulphur tritum cum oleo, donec eradicentur escharae omnes, et omnis corruptio.	Then you should leave it for three days and put heated sulfur mixed with oil over the burned areas until all sores are gone and all decay is removed.
Deinde cura ipsum cum unguentis generantibus carnem.	Then take care of it as new flesh begins to form.
Si ergo uides, quod post tres dies caro nascitur natiuitate sana, in qua non est corruptio, est bonum.	But if you see that after three days healthy flesh is born without decay, this is good.
Et si non: tunc itera cauterium super illud quod remansit ex locis corruptis.	And if not: then apply the burn again to what remains of the rotten areas.
Et corrodens medicatur quandoque cum medicina acuta.	And it is treated with a strong medicine when necessary.
Ipsa namque surgit loco cauterii.	Indeed, as this arises from the burned place.
Verumtamen cauterium cum igne est uelocioris iuuamenti: et ego quidem iam dixi cauterizationem eius cum medicina acuta in diuisione: accipe ergo eam illic quando ea indiges.	However, the burn with fire is quicker to heal than that with medicine; and I have indeed already said that this cauterization should be done with a strong medicine in division: so take it when you find it necessary.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in Clauis, et Verucis.	Paragraph concerning the method of cauterizing clavicle and verrucas (wart-like growths).
Caput LV.	Head LV.
Multotiens accidit in inferioribus partibus pedum haec aegritudo: et est res grossa, filtrata, quae laedit pedem.	This disease often occurs in the lower parts of feet; it is a bulky condition that affects the foot.
Et cauterium quidem in eis est secundum duos modos: cauterium cum igne, et cauterium cum aqua calida.	And indeed, this treatment is done in two ways: with a fire-cauter and with a hot water caustic.
Quantum autem cum igne est, ut ignias cauterium concauum simile pennae uulturis: quod fiat ex ferro, secundum quantitatem quod contineat clauum ab omni parte: et sit subtilium marginum.	However, the fire-cauter is shaped like a raven's feather: it is made of iron according to the size that contains the joint from all sides; and its edges are delicate.
Deinde depone ipsum ignitum super clauum.	Then remove the fire from over the nails.
Deinde reuolue manum cum cauterio in circumitu claui, donec perueniat cauterium ad profunditatem claui: et dimitte ipsum tribus diebus, donec incipiat emittere pus.	Next, roll the hand around with a cautery over its borders until the cautery reaches to the depth of the nail: and let it rest for three days, until it starts to discharge pus.
Deinde emplastra ipsum cum maluis syluestribus, contritis cum sale: et dimitte emplastrum super ipsum in nocte.	Next, apply plasters on the wound with soot and salt softened: and let the plaster remain overnight.
Ipse enim eradicabitur ex radicibus suis.	For he will be removed from its roots.
Deinde cura locum unguento generatiuo carnis, donec sanetur.	Then the place should be cared for with a general ointment of flesh until it heals.
Quod si sunt non conuersi, et multotiens accidunt in superficie corporis, praecipue in manibus et pedibus: tunc administres in eis cauterium cum aqua calida: et est, ut accipias cannulam ex aere, aut ferro, aut ex penna uulturis: et depone eam super clauum, aut althelul.	If these are not gone and frequently occur on the body' vice surfaces, especially in hands and feet: then administer cautery with warm water to them: and you should receive a tube of metal, iron or from an eagle's quill; and remove it over nails, or althelul.
Deinde proiice in cannulam ex aqua calida quantitatem paucam: retine manum tuam, et tu reuolue eam cum compressione manus tuae parumper, ut imprimatur margo cannulae in radice claui, et inueniat aqua calida uiam ad profundum, ad radicem claui: et expectet infirmus parumper super mordicationem aquae calidae hora una.	Then pour a small amount of hot water into the tube: hold it with your hand and gently squee cups your fingers, so as to press on the edge of the cannula at its base, allowing the hot water path to reach deep inside, down to the root of the tube. Let the sick person stay there for about an hour under the warmth of the water.
Deinde dimitte ipsum, nam clauus eradicatur cum radicibus suis.	Then remove it gently, as the thorn is taken out with its roots.
Ita fac cum eis uno post unum, donec uenias super omnes qui ex eis sunt in corpore.	So do this after one and then come over all those who are from it inside the body.
Deinde cura eos postquam eradicantur, cum eo quod generat carnem ex unguentis.	Then care for them when they have been removed with that which generates flesh through ointments.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in Tremore.	¶ On the method of cauterizing tremors.
Caput LVI.	Chapter LVI.
Quando accidit alicui Tremor ex frigore in neruo, aut ex febre quartana, aut alio: tunc oportet ut cauterizes ipsum quatuor cauteriis, aut quinque super spondiles dorsi, et inter omnem spondilem cauterio, et in pectore eius cauterio, et super stomachum eius cauterio.	When a tremor occurs in someone due to cold or quartan fever, or another cause: one must cauterize it with four cauteries on the dorsal spine, and over every intervertebral space, also over the chest and stomach.
Tremor enim quiescit cum cauterio oliuari, et festinat sanitas aegritudinis frigidae.	The tremor ceases with oilcake (a type of cautery), and health quickly escapes the coldness of pain.
¶ De modo cauterizandi Albathir.	Method for using Albatyr: Firstly, when you approach a patient suffering from tremors due to various causes such as exposure to cold or quartan fever, it is advised that the physician should employ four cauteries at the back of the spinal column. Additionally, each intervertebral space ought to be treated with the same method. The chest and stomach regions must also be addressed in this manner. With Albatyr's usage, a tremor is expected to subside quickly as it does when applying oilcake.
Caput LVII.	Chapter LVII.
Quandoque expelluntur in corpore Albathir foedae, id est, pustulae, quae fiunt a materiis grossis corruptis.	When Albatyr removes bodily filth, that is, pustules caused by the decay of thick materials.
Oportet ergo in primis cum apparent, ut cauterizentur super omne caput pustulae cauterio subtili cum ligno myrti, cuius extremitas accensa est cum igne.	It is therefore first necessary that the head of every boil be cauterized with a delicate myrtle stick heated by fire.
Aut cum radice aristolochiae longae.	or along with the root of Aristolochia longa.
Aut cum cauterio lenticulari.	or with a lens-shaped cautery.
Et quandoque cauterizantur ademenul, in principio expulsionis suae secundum hunc modum: et non augentur: et disrumpitur superfluitas faciens eos, et sanatur ex eis.	And when they are cauterized by their mouths, the procedure for expulsion is as follows: They do not increase, and an excess that makes them is broken off, and they heal from it.
Verumtamen oportet ut fiat illud post euacuationem cum phlebotomia.	However, this must be done after evacuation with phlebotomy.
¶ De modo cauterizandi in fluxu sanguins ex arteria in uulnere.	§ On the method of cauterizing a blood flow from an artery into a wound.
Caput LVIII.	Chapter LVIII.
Multotiens accidit fluxus sanguinis ex arteria, quae incisa est apud uulnus, quod accidit extrinsecus, aut apud incisionem apostematis, aut cauterium membri, et similia eis: et fit difficile abscindere eum.
