Often it happens that bleeding occurs from an artery which has been cut near a wound externally or during the removal of abscesses or burns on limbs and similar events: thus, it is difficult to separate them.
Cum ergo accidit alicui illud, tunc propera cum manu tua ad orificium arteriae, et pone super ipsum digitum tuum indicem: et stringe eum multum, donec obsessus sit sanguis sub digito tuo, et non egrediatur ex eo aliquid.	So when this happens to someone, quickly approach the opening of the artery with your hand and place your index finger on it: press firmly until blood is captured under your fingertnail, and nothing comes out from there.
Deinde pone in ignem cauteria oliuaria parua, et magna numero plura: et suffla super ea, donec fiant ignita ualde.	Then place the small olive oil caustic over fire and many other things: then blow on it until they are burnt thoroughly.
Deinde accipe ex eis unum, aut paruum, aut magnum, secundum uulnus et locum, in quo disrupta est arteria, et depone cauterium super ipsam uenam, post quam tu remoues digitum tuum festinanter: et tene cauterium, donec abscindatur sanguis.	Then take one [cautery], two or three of small size, or a large one according to the wound and location where the artery was disrupted, and place the caustic over it: then quickly remove your finger: hold the cauterium until blood is separated.
Quod si expellatur cum eleuas digitum ab orificio arteriae, et extinguis cauterium, tunc accipe cauterium aliud festinanter, ex cauteriis quae in igne sunt praeparata.	If the blood is ejected through the opening of an artery and the heat source is removed, then quickly take another heated caustic from those prepared on fire.
Non ergo cesses facere illud cum uno post aliud, donec abscindatur sanguis.	Do not cease doing that with one finger after the other until the blood has been separated.
Et caue, ne comburas neruum qui est illic, et accidat super infirmum malicia alia.	And be careful to avoid burning the nerves there; otherwise harm may come upon another part of a sickly person.
Et scias, quod quando ex arteria fluit sanguis, tunc non est possibile abscindere ipsum: praecipue quaudo arteria est magna, nisi cum uno quatuor modorum.	And know that when the blood flows from an artery, it is not possible to sever it; especially if the artery is large, unless with four different methods.
Aut cum cauterio, sicut diximus.	Or as we have mentioned with a caustic.
Aut cum extractione, quando non est extracta.	Or by excision when it cannot be removed.
Nam quando extrahitur, contrahuntur extremitates eius, et abscinditur sanguis.	For when extracted, its ends contract and blood is severed.
Aut ligetur cum filo ligatione forti.	Or it can be tied with a strong thread.
Aut ponantur super ipsum medicinae de proprietate, quarum est abscindere sanguinem, et stringatur cum puluinari constrictione decenti.	These are placed above the affected area of surgery, which is to remove blood, and it is tightened with a reasonable ligature pressure.
Qui autem administrat abscisionem eius cum ligamento, et strictura cum panno, aut positione rerum comburentium, et similium, non confert ei penitus, nisi raro.	However, whoever performs the incision with a bandage and a stricture using cloth or similar substances does not completely close it unless rarely.
Si autem accidat alicui illud, et non sit ei praesens medicus, neque medicina: tunc incipiat cum positione digiti indicis super orificium uenae ipsius, sicut narrauimus, et constrictione eius ualde, donec obsessus sit sanguis a superiori parte uulneris, et super arteriam.	If however it happens to someone that no doctor or medicine is present: then start with the positioning of the index finger over the wound site, as we mentioned, and tighten its constriction greatly until blood from the upper part of the wound is pressed out and on top of the artery.
Et digitus non remoueatur, desuper ipsum cum aqua frigida uehementis frigoris semper, donec congeletur sanguis, et ingrossetur, et abscindatur.	And the finger should not be removed; it must always stay above with very cold water of intense coolness until the blood coagulates and thickens, then separated from the area.
Et interim consideret in eo, quid indiget ex cauterio, aut ex medicina.	And meanwhile, he should think about what is needed with a cauterizing tool or medicine.
¶ Partis Primae Finis.	The First Section'e Finale'.
Liber Chirurgici Albucasis Pars II.	The Book of Surgeons by Albucasis, Part Two'.
¶ De Incisione, Perforatione, et Phlebotomia in uulneribus, et his similibus.	On Incision, Puncture, and Phlebotomy in Wounds, and Similar Procedures'
Iam Diximus in Capitulo Primo, omnem aegritudinem in qua conueniens est cum igne cauterium et medicina comburente, et occasiones eius, ipsius caussas, et instrumenta eius, et formas cauteriorum.	Now We Have Discussed In the First Chapter: All Illnesses Wherein It Is Convenient To Use Fire-Cautery and Burning Medicine And Its Occasions, Causes Of Its Application, And The Tools Used For It And Shapes Of Surgical Instruments.
Et posui illic capitula a uertice usque ad pedem.	I attached heads there from top to toe.
Et ego procedam in hoc capitulo illa eadem uia: ut alleuietur super quaerentem quaesitum eius.	And I will follow this chapter with the same method: by easing the pain of the one seeking relief.
Et antequam incipiam illud, oportet ut addiscatis o filii, quod in hoc capitulo est ex terrore illud quod est in capitulo primo de cauterizatione.	And before I begin that, it is necessary to add what the son has learned from this chapter, which is about a fear that exists in Chapter One on Cautery.
Et propter illud oportet, ut sit cautela in eo uehementior, quoniam in operatione quae est in hoc capitulo, multotiens cadit euacuatio cum sanguine, cum quo stat uita apud apertionem uenae, aut incisionem super apostema, aut apertionem exiturae, aut curationem uulneris, aut extractionem sagittae, aut incisionem super lapidem, et illis similia: ex quibus omnibus associatur tremor, et timor, et cadit in pluribus eorum mors.	And because of this reason, it is necessary to be especially cautious with that operation which is described in this chapter; as often as evacuation occurs along with blood loss, by which life remains at the entrance of a wound or an incision on an abscess, a perforated body opening, a wound's healing, arrow extraction, stone cutting incision, and such like: all these are associated with trembling, fear, and death in many cases.
Et ego moneo uos, ne cadat super uos illud in quo est haesitatio, nam quandoque cadunt ad uos in hac arte modi hominum cum modis infirmitatum.	And I advise you not to fall for that issue which is hesitation because sometimes people with diseases are confronted by this method.
Ex eis enim est qui irascitur cum aegritudine sua, et est leuis apud eum mors: propter uehementiam eius quod inuenit ex infirmitate sua et longitudine eius maliciei.	This is indeed tormented by his own illness, and death approaches him quickly; due to the severity of it because he discovered it from his sickness and its great lengthiness.
Et cum aegritudine est ex timore quod significat mortem.	And with illness comes fear, which signifies death.
Et ex eis est, qui dat tibicensum suum, et ditat te cum eo, sperans sanitatem, et aegritudo eius est perniciosa.	And from these is the one who gives his flute and shares with you in it, hoping for health, and his sickness is harmful.
Non ergo oportet ut consentiatis ei qui uenit ad uos ex eis, cuius modus est talis.	Therefore, one should not allow that who comes to you from them, whose manner is such.
Et sit cautela uestra uehementior, quam cupiditas et uestra rapacitas.	And let your caution be stronger than your desire and greed.
Et non praesumatis super aliquid ex illo, nisi post scientiam certam, quae uerificat apud uos illud ad quod peruenit successio laudabilis.	And do not assume anything from it unless proven by knowledge that verifies to which credible succession it has led.
Et utimini in curatione omnium infirmorum uestrorum, prognosticatione et indicatione de eo ad quod conuenienter sit salus.	And use all your skills for the care of all sick people, with diagnosis and recommendation that is most suitable for their well- being.
In illo namque est uobis adiutorium super acquisitionem famae et gloriae, et memoriae et laudis.	For in this you will find help over the acquisition of fame and glory, as well as memory and praise.
Inspiret uobis Deus o filii, intellectum suum, et non auferat uobis directionem et inspirationem: quoniam illud est in manu eius.	May God enlighten you, my son, with His understanding, and do not take away your guidance or inspiration: for it is in his hand.
Et ego quidem ordinaui hoc Capitulum distinguendo per capitula, secundum quod praecessit in capitulo Cauterii, a ceruice usque ad pedes: ut alleuietur uobis quaesitum quod uultis ex eo, et quo indigetis.	I indeed ordered this chapter to be distinguished by chapters as it proceeded from the head downward in Chapter of Cautery: so that you may find what you seek from it and whatever is needed.
¶ De curatione Aquae quae aggregatur in capitibus puerorum.	Concerning the treatment of water collected in boys' heads.
Caput I.	Head I.
Scias, quod haec infirmitas multotiens accidit pueris apud partum: aut quando stringit obstetrix caput pueri absque leuitate.	Know that this illness often occurs in boys during birth: either when the mother is gripped by a contraction without leniency.
Et quandeque accidit etiam ex caussa occulta quae non scitur.	And also whenever it happens because of a hidden cause which is not known.
Et ego quidem non uidi hanc aegritudinem in aliis quam in pueris: et ad omnem quem ex eis uidi properauit mors: propter illud ergo uisum est mihi dimittere operationem in ea.	And indeed, I have not seen this disease occur among others than boys: and to all whomsoever it has led to death, which is why I decided to dismiss the treatment for that case.
Et ego quidem uidi ex eis puerum, cuius caput impletum erat aqua, et caput magnificabatur in omni die, donec non poterat sedere super seipsum, propter magnitudinem capitis sui: et humiditas augmentata fuit, donec mortuus est.	And indeed I have seen a boy whose head was filled with water and it expanded every day until he could not sit upright on himself due to the size of his head; and the wetness increased, until he died.
Et haec quidem humiditas, aut aggregatur inter cutem et os: aut aggregatur sub osse super sifac.	This moisture indeed lies between the skin and the bone or is gathered beneath the bone tissue.
Et operatio in illo, si est humiditas inter cutem et os, et apostema est paruum, tunc oportet ut findas in medio capitis fissura una in latitudine: et sit longitudo fissurae quasi duo nodi, donec currat humiditas.	And the operation for this condition, if there is moisture between the skin and bone or an abscess of a pus pocket, then one should find in the middle of the head a fissure with a width like two knots until the moisture runs out.
Et haec est forma spatumilis.	This is indeed the form of a tumor.
Si ergo humiditas est magis augmentata, et apostema est maius, tunc pone eas duas fissuras, secundum formam hanc.	However, if moisture is greatly increased and abscess is larger, then place two fissures according to this shape.
Et si humiditas est sub osse, et signum eius est, quod uides commissuras capitis apertas ab omni parte: et aqua deprimitur quando comprimis eam manu tua ad interiora, et non occultatur tibi illud: tunc oportet ut findas in medio capitis tribus fissuris, secundum hunc modum.	And if moisture is under the bone and you see a sign that the junctions of the head are open from all sides; when pressing it with your hand, water flows outward into the interior: then one should find in the middle of the head three fissures according to this method.
Et post incisionem extrahe humiditatem totam.	And after making an incision, remove all moisture entirely.
Deinde stringe fissuras cum pannis et puluillis.	Then bind the cracks with bandages and poultices.
Deinde embroca illud desuper cum uino et oleo usque ad diem quintum.	Then apply that remedy from above with wine and oil until the fifth day.
Deinde solue ligamentum, et cura uulnus cum tentis, et unguentis.	Next dissolve the ligament, and treat the wound with bandages and ointments.
Et non dimittas stringere caput cum aequalitate.	And do not leave off binding head injuries equally.
Et ciba infirmum omni cibo sicco paucae humiditatis, usquequo confortetur membrum, et sanetur.	And feed the patient with dry food in small amounts until they are comforted and healed.
Et modus alius incisionis est, ut consideres ubi apparet magnitudo apostematis, et collectio aquae.	Another method of incision is to consider the size of swellings and fluid collection.
Quoniam quandoque est in occipitio plus, aut in sincipite, aut in dextra, aut in sinistra.	For sometimes it appears atop the back or on one side or another.
Ascende ergo cum incisione ubi apparet tibi apostema et impletio aquae: et scinde illud secundum quod tibi possibile est.	Thus ascend with the incision where you see a swelling and fluid collection, and cut as much as is possible for you.
Et obserua, ne incidas arteriam, et accidat fluxus sanguinis, et moriatur infirmus ex illo fluxu cum euacuatione humiditatis.	And observe, do not injure the artery, and let blood flow happen, and that the sick person dies from this flow when expelling moisture.
¶ De incisione Arteriarum quae sunt post aures.	Concerning incision of arteries located behind ears.
Caput II.	Head II
Quando accidunt alicui catarri ad oculos, aut ad pectus, et antiquatur illud, et non confert curatio medicinarum: tunc magis ultima curatio est in illo, incisio harum duarum arteriarum.	When diarrhea occurs to the eyes or chest, and when that condition is longstanding without medical treatment being helpful; then the final remedy lies in incision of those two arteries.
Oportet ergo quando uis incidere eas, ut radat infirmus caput suum.	Therefore, when incision is made into them, it should relieve the sick person' cups and heads.")
Deinde frica locum cum panno aspero, ut appareant arteriae.	Then scrape the area with coarse cloth so that the arteries appear.
Deinde stringat infirmus collum suum, cum quolibet panno suo.	Then the sick person should bind his neck with any of his own cloths.
Deinde considera, ubi pulset uena.	Therefore, consider where the pulse flows.
Et loca utriusque sunt loca quae sunt post aures depressa: et raro occultatur, nisi in quibusdam hominibus.	The places that are behind both ears are rarely hidden except in certain individuals.
Deinde signa cum encaustro super utraque: et incide utramque cum spatumili utrimque acuro, incisione perueniente ad os: et fiat illud per latitudinem capitis.	Then make marks with wax over both and incise each side up to the mouth: and let this be made through the width of the head.
Et si uis, intromitte spatumile sub arteria, et incide eam ad superiora cum incisione.	And if you can, insert a catheter under an artery and incise it upward with an incision.
Et sit longitudo incisionis quasi duo digiti iuncti.	And let the length of the incision be nearly as two joined fingers.
Nam quando inciditur uena, egreditur sanguis egressione pulsatili, qui salit ad interiora saltu frequenti.	For when a passage is cut open, blood gushes out by the pulse's throbbing and rushes to the innards frequently.
Si autem arteria non apparet sensui, tunc oportet ut mensures ab aure quantitatem spacii trium digitorum.	But if an artery does not appear by sense, then it is necessary to measure from the ear the space of three fingers.
Deinde signa cum encaustro, et finde usque ad os.	Then make marks with wax and reach up to the mouth.
Et illud quod oportet emittere ex sanguine, est VI uncia et fortasse emittis ex eo plus, aut minus.	And what needs to be expelled from blood is six scruples; perhaps more or less can be expelled.
Totum illud secundum quantitatem quae apparet tibi ex uirute infirmi et repletione arteriae eius.	And the amount to be taken depends on what is evident in terms of the patient's sickness and the congestion of that artery.
Deinde considera ad uulnus.	Then, consider the wound.
Tunc si remanet ad os ex sifac aliquid, tunc incide illud, ut non accidat apostema calidum: tunc stringe uulnus cum liciniis ex panno lini.	Then if anything remains at the site of the wound, then cut it out so that inflammation does not occur; tightly bind the wound with linen threads.
Deinde cura ipsum cum unguento, donec sanetur.	Next, take care of it with ointment until it heals.
¶ De extractione arteriarum, quae sunt in timporibus.	¶ Regarding the extraction of vessels that are on the temples.
Caput III.	Chapter III.
Quando accidit homini hemicranea antiqua, aut catarri acuti propter humiditates acrimoniales, et caliditate in lacertis timporum, aut soda antiqua, uehemens, et similia illis: et medicatur cum modis curationis medicinae, et non confert illud: tunc experti sumus in his aegritudinibus extractionem arteriarum ex timporibus, aut cauterizationem earum, sicut narrauimus.	When this happens to a man with an old head injury or acute drip because of acidic moisture and warmth in the temples, or with an ancient wound, bleeding profusely, and similar: and it is treated according to methods of medical treatment, without increasing that; then we are experienced in these diseases by extraction from the temple vessels, or cauterization thereof, as we have described.
Et modus operationis in extractione earum, est, ut radat infirmus pilos qui sunt in timporibus, et intendat ad arteriam apparentem in timpore.	The method for removing them is that the patient should comb out the hairs that are present in the temples and focus towards the visible vein behind it.
Ipsa namque ostenditur tibi ex pulsu suo, et raro occultatur nisi in paucis hominibus, aut uehementia frigoris.	It is also shown to you by its own pulse and often hidden only in a few people or with strong coldness.
Quod si occultatur tibi, tunc stringat infirmus caput suum cum quolibet panno suo: deinde frica locum cum panno aspero.	What if it is hidden from you; then the patient should rub his head with any of his cloths: then scrape the place with a rough cloth.
Aut uapora locum cum aqua calida, donec appareat tibi apparitione manifesta.	Or wash the place with warm water until it becomes clearly visible to you.
Deinde accipe spatumile, quod paulo ante formaui.	Then take an instrument that I have previously shaped.
Deinde excoria cum eo cutem cum facilitate, donec peruenias ad arteriam.	Then remove the skin with it easily until you reach the vein.
Deinde proiice in eam uncinum, et extrahe eam ad superiora, donec extrahas eam ex cute, et facias eam euadere ex tunicis quae sunt sub ea ab omni parte.	Then insert a hook into it and pull the vein out from above until you extract it from the skin, and make it exit through the tunics which are underneeet from all sides.
Si autem arteria est subtilis: tunc inuolue eam cum extremitate uncini.	If however the artery is delicate: then gently tie it off at its extremity with hooks.
Deinde incide ex ea partem secundum quantitatem qua elongentur extremitates eius, et contrahantur, et non accidat fluxus sanguinis.	Next, incise that portion according to the length of its ends, and contract them, so that no blood flow occurs.
Nam si non inciditur, et si non abscinditur, non ascendit sanguis penitus.	For if it is not incised, and if it is not separated, the blood does not rise completely.
Deinde euacua ex sanguine ana VI unci, usque ad .III.	Then cleanse with wine vinegar up to III.
Quod si arteria est magna: tunc oportet ut liges eam in duobus locis ex filo duplo, forti, ex serico: aut ex chordis alhohod, ut non properet ad ipsam putrefactio ante consolidationem uulneris, et accidat fluxus sanguinis.	If the artery is large: then one must ligate it in two places with a strong thread of silk or linen so that decay does not occur before wound healing and blood flow happens.
Deinde incide superfluitatem, quae est inter duo ligamenta.	Then make an incision between the two ligaments which is excessive.
Fac illud in illa hora, aut post horam aliam.	Do this at that hour or another.
Et si uis, cauteriza eam cauterio usque ad os, cum cauterio cultellari: donec incidantur extremitates eius, et stabit loco eiusdem operis.	And if it is veinous, burn it with a branding iron up to the mouth, with a small branding iron as when cutting off its ends, and until they are incised, and stand in place.
Et est melius opus, nisi si infirmus habet febrem, autest calefactae complexionis.	And it is better done unless he has a weakness or hot fever conditions.
Quoniam cauterium est ex eis, quae iuuant ad finiendas humiditates.	For the branding iron is among those things that help to dry off moisture.
Ergo est melius iuuamentum.	Therefore is a better remedy.
Et oportet post extractionem arteriarum, ut impleatur locus cotto antiquo: et ponantur super ipsum puluilli decenter facti.	And it should be filled with an old-time paste after the removal of the veins: and they are placed above it neatly made pills.
Et post solutionem curetur cum medicinis siccis, quae faciunt nasci carnem, et cum liciniis, donec sanetur.	And after the treatment with dry medicines that generate flesh and with liniments until healed.
Quod si interim dum operaris accidit fluxus sanguinis ex arteria, tunc propera ad abscindendum eum cum cauterio, aut ut impleas locum cum zegi: et stringe manum tuam, donec abscindatur sanguis.	If in the meant vice blood flow occurs from an artery, then quickly attempt to excise it with a cautery or fill the place with wax. Hold your hand tightly until the bleeding stops.
Quod si nihil ex illis est tibi praesens, tunc pone super locum digitum tuum, donec congeletur sanguis.	If none of these things are currently available to you, then place your finger over the spot until the blood hardens.
Et embroca locum cum aqua uehementis frigoris, donec quiescat acuitas, et stringatur secundum quod oportet.	And apply cold water to the wound vigorously until the intensity subsides and bind it according to what is necessary.
Et ex eo quod est leuius et facilius extractione arteriae, est, ut cauterizes uenam cum hoc cauterio habente duos cultellos: sitque acuitas duorum cultellorum similis almagdatem.	And because it is easier and simpler to remove the artery, hold a caustic with this caustic device having two knives: make sure both blades have equal sharpness.
Verumtamen sunt multo minoris acuitatis, quam duo cultelli.	However, they should be much less sharp than two knives.
Quoniam si sunt acutae, sicut duo cultelli, properat utrisque frigus: et non incidunt carnem cum uelocitate.	Because if they are as sharp as two knives, hurry both coldnesses: and do not cut the flesh hastily.
Cum ergo in eis est aliquantulum grossitudinis, tenetur in eis calor ignis, et abscinditur caro uelociter: cum hoc ergo opus est melius omni opere, et leuius, et facilius.	When there is a certain amount of swelling, heat must be applied to them; the flesh quickly peels away as a result: hence this method is better for all purposes and easier.
Et sit spacium quod est inter duos cultellos quantitas grossitudinis digiti, postquam tu signas duo loca cum encaustro: et depone utrosque ignitos ualde, donec perueniant ad os, et incidant uenam in duobus locis: ut elongetur quod est inter extremitates eius.	And there must be space that is between two knives a quantity of swelling, once you mark the two places with an encaustic: remove both ignited and let them reach until they meet at the mouth; then penetrate into these two places so it elongates what is in-between.
Nam non consolidantur cum hoc cauterio penitus.	For this, they do not become solid with this caustic completely.
Et haec est forma cauterii.	And this is the form of a caustic.
¶ De cura cursus lachrymarum acutarum assiduarum ab oculis.	¶ On the treatment for frequent, severe eye irritation from tears.
Caput IIII.	Head IV.
Quando sunt lachrymae assiduae, et est cursus earum ex uenis, quae sunt super craneum capitis exterius: et non confert in eis aliquid curationis medicinae cum medicinis, et uides faciem infirmi iam rubere, et sentit in fronte sua deambulationem, sicut est deambulatio formicarum: et oculi eius sunt extenuati, humidi, ita quod iam corrosi sunt pili eorum cum corrosione: et calefactae sunt palpebrae eius ex acuitate lachrymarum: tunc antiqui indiguerunt in curatione earum hac operatione, et denominauerunt eam curationem, cum Ense.	When tears are continuous and their course is through the veins outside of the skull: and there is no confinement to anything for healing from medicines, and you see that an invalid's face has turned red, and feels movement on his forehead, as with ant movements; and his eyes have weakened, moistened, so they are now eroded by their own secretions: and his eyelids are warmed by the sharpness of tears. At that time, ancients resorted to treating these problems through this operation, and named it healing with a sword.
Et est, ut praecipias infirmo radere pilos qui sunt in fronte sua.	And it is as though the hair on one's forehead has been removed from an invalid.
Deinde incide in fronte tres fissuras aequedistantes secundum longitudinem frontis: et sit longitudo fissurae quasi duo digiti, et fissura una sit aequedistans longitudini nasi in medio frontis, et secunda secundum longitudinem parumper a motu lacertorum, et tertia a parte altera: et caue ab incisione arteriarum quae sunt in duobus lateribus: et elonga manum tuam a continuatione duarum mandibularum, et sit spacium omnis incisionis quantitas trium digitorum coniunctorum: et sit tibi frustum spongiae praeparatum, aut panni siccati multi, cum quibus exsicces sanguinem.	Then make three cuts in the forehead at equal distances along its length; and let the length of each fissure be about two fingers, with one fissure being equidistant from the midline of the nose on the face's front part, and another following slightly less than perpendicular to the motion line, and a third elsewhere: and stop bleeding by making incisions along the arteries which are located at both sides; and extend your hand as much as would match three fingers together; and let there be space equal to the thickness of all the cuts. Take some dried sponge or many layers of clean cloth with you, to soak up any excess blood.
Deinde intromitte spatumile duarum acutarum extremitatum, cuius mox sequens est forma.	Then introduce a rounded instrument at the sharp ends of both sides, whose next step is as follows.
Ab incisione quae est a parte timporis, usque ad incisionem secundam: et excoria cum eo totam cutem, quae est inter duas incisiones, cum sifac, quod est super os.	From the incision that is from the side of the time (temporal region), up to the second incision: and along with it remove all skin between these two incisions, which is above the bone.
Deinde fac illud etiam ab incisione media usque ad incisionem secundam.	Then do this also from the median incision up to the second incision.
Deinde extrahe hoc spatumile, et intromitte in incisionem primam iterum instrumentum aliud, quod nominatur cultellare acutum, ab una parte lene, non acutum ab altera parte.	Then extract this rounded instrument and reintroduce another tool into the first incision named as a sharp curette from one side that is not sharp at the other end.
Et haec est forma eius.	And herein lies its form.
Et pone latus eius acutum uersus carnem annexam cum cute, et latus eius lene uersus os: et impelle ipsum, donec perueniat ad fissuram mediam: et abscinde cum eo omnia uasa, quae descendunt a capite ad oculos: praeter quod continuetur incisio usque ad illud quod apparet de cute.	And herein is its shape. Then lay the sharp side of it against the adjacent flesh and the blunt side towards the bone, and push it until it reaches the midline fissure: then cut with it all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes; except for continuing the incision up to what appears on the skin.
Deinde fac illud in fissura media usque ad fissuram aliam.	Then perform it from the middle furrow up to another furrow.
Et postquam currit ex sanguine quantitas aequalis, exprime loca ex frustis sanguinis coagulati.	And after when an equal amount of blood has run out, express the coagulated places with poultices.
Deinde pone in omnem fissuram licinium ex cotto ueteri, et pone super eos puluillos imbibitos in uino, et oleo, aut aceto.	Then place lime on every furrow from the old cooked mortar, and put moistened poultices over them with wine, oil, or vinegam.
Et uide ut non accidat apostema calidum.	And watch that it does not become inflamed.
Et in die tertia solue ligamentum, et administra infusionem multam cum aqua tepida.	And on the third day dissolve the bandage, and apply a large quantity of warm water infusion.
Deinde cura illud ex unguento basilicon, et reliquis quibus curantur uulnera: usquequo sanetur.	Then care for that with a balm (unguentum) and the other remedies used for wounds: until healed.
¶ De cura lachrymarum acutarum et catarrorum ad oculos ex interioribus capitis.	¶ For the treatment of sudden tears and catarrhs from within the head to the eyes.
Caput V.	Chapter Five.
Quando accidunt alicui catarri acuti, acres, assidui: et uides oculos eius extenuatos, paruos, et iam debilitatus est aspectus eorum: et palpebrae ulceratae, et cadunt pili ex eis, et in profundo capitis est dolor acutus, laedens, et sternutatio consequens: tunc sume ex istis accidentibus, quod illae materiae, et catarri non ueniunt, nisi ex uenis multis.	When there are sharp, intense and persistent itches in the eyes, causing them to become wasted, weakened, and their appearance is now diminished: palpebral ulcers occur, hairs fall out from them, and a severe pain arises within the head. In such cases, one must resort to these treatments when no discharge comes from many veins.
Et melior curatio in eis est haec.	And this is a better cure for those conditions:
Et est, ut praecipias infirmo radere frontem suam.	And it should be done as follows to the sick person's forehead:
Deinde incide in eam fissuram unam in medio frontis, aut alterius parumper per latitudinem, et incipe cum fissura a timpore sinistro ad timpus dextrum: et sit incisio usque ad os: et elonga manum tuam a lacertis timporum, qui mouentur apud masticationem: donec quando detegitur os: et exsiccabis totum sanguinem cum spongia.	Then make an incision in the forehead along with a small slit through its width or from one side to another, and begin cutting at that split from left to right temple: And extend it up to the mouth: and elongate your hand from the temples of the jaws, which move during chewing; until you see an opening: then squeeze out all blood with a sponge.
Tunc separa inter duo labia fissurae cum cotto ueteri, aut cum liciniis ex lino.	Then separate between the two lips of the incision using an old cut or linen strips.
Deinde stringe desuper cum puluillis: et imbibe puluillos cum uino et oleo, ut non accidat apostema calidum.	Then tightly bind it with pulses (cotton bandages): and soak the pulses with wine and oil, to prevent a hot abscess from forming.
Et quando soluis illud, et uides quod apostema calidum iam imminuitur: tunc oportet ut frices os, donec incipiat in eo nasci caro.	And when you loosen that and observe a hot abscess is already forming: it should be scraped (the wound), until flesh begins to grow there.
Deinde cura ipsum cum regimine exiccatiuo quod facit nasci carnem: sicut si accipias ex farina tritici partes duas, et ex colophonia quatuor partes: et praepares ex eis emplastrum, et administretur ad natiuitatem carnis in istis uulneribus.	Then care for it with the treatment that promotes the growth of flesh (granulation tissue): as if you receive two parts from wheat flour and four parts from a resin called colophony: and prepare an ointment from these, and apply it at birth to new skin in those wounds.
¶ De cura eius quod cadit in Aurem.	¶ Regarding its care when it falls into the ear.
Caput VI.	Head VI.
Omne Quod in Aurem cadit, est una quatuor specierum: aut lapis mineralis, aut simile lapidi, sicut ferrum, et uitrum: aut est ex planta, sicut est cicer, et fabae: aut est res fluxibilis, sicut aqua, et acetum, et eis similia: aut aliquod animal.	Chapter VI: Whatever is in the ear [falls into four kinds]: it may be a mineral stone, such as iron or quartz; or something similar to rock like chalk; or from plants, like beans and lentils; or some fluid substance, like water and vinegesteris; or an animal.
Quando ergo cadit in aurem lapis, aut genus lapidis ex eis quae non adduntur, neque crescunt in aure, expone Aurem soli: si ergo uides lapidem, tunc distilla in Aurem aliquid ex oleo uiolato, aut sisamino.	When therefore [a stone or something similar to rock] falls into the ear and does not add itself to it nor grow within the ear, expose the ear: if you see a stone, then extract some fluid with oil of vitriol or with wine vinegar.
Deinde administra extractionem eius, et fac sternutare cum condisi, et opila nares apud aduentum sternutationis, postquam tu ponis in circumitu auris frusta ex pannis, aut lana, et extendis aurem ad superiora.	Then perform the extraction of it and make him sneequirely while facing the entrance to the nose, after placing fragments of cloth or wool around his ears and extending the ear upwards.
Multotiens enim egreditur cum hac cura.	Often this is cured with this treatment.
Si autem non egreditur, tunc administra extractionem eius cum Gesti, id est, Pizigarolis subtilibus: cuius forma est haec.	However, if it does not go out, then perform the extraction with a pizigarus, that is, subtle fingers of which the form is as follows.
Si ergo egreditur cum gesti, est bonum.	If however it goes out with a Gesti, it's good.
Et si non, tunc administra extractionem eius cum uncino caeco subtili paucae duplicationis.	And if not, then perform the extraction with a subtle hook of twofold copies: which is as follows.
Si ergo non egreditur per illud, tunc fac cannulam ex aere, et intromitte extremitatem cannulae in foramen auris multum, et opila quod est in circumitu cannulae cum caera mollificata cum oleo, ut non sit uento uia nisi cannulae: deinde extrahe cum uento tuo attractione forti.	If however it does not go out by that means, then make a tube of bronze, and introduce the tip of the tube deep into the ear hole much, and press what is in the circumference of the tube with mollified wax: so that there be no airway except through the tube: then extract it with your own extraction force.
Multotiens enim egreditur cum eo quod narrauimus.	Often it leaves with that which we have mentioned.
Si autem non egreditur hoc modo: tunc accipe ex helkalimbat, aut ex uisco, id est, gluten praeparato, cum quo capiuntur aues, rem modicam: et pone ipsum in extremitate radii postquam tu inuoluis super eam cotum decenter positum: deinde intromitte ipsum in foramen auris cum facilitate, postquam tu exiccas aurem ab humiditate.	If it does not emerge as we mentioned before: then take some unguent of helkalimbat or ointment from the eel (that is), prepared gluten with which birds are captured, place this modestly on the end of the radius after you have properly positioned it: and put that in the ear canal when you have dried out your ear.
Si ergo non egreditur cum omnibus quae narrauimus, tunc propera ad scindendum, antequam accidat apostema calidum, aut spasmus.	If it does not come out as we have mentioned before: then proceed with the incision promptly before a hot swelling or spasm occurs.
Et modus fissurae est, ut phlebotomes infirmum in primis in cephalica: et extrahe ei ex sanguine secundum mensuram uirtutis eius.	And the way of the incision is that first a feeble person should be laid on their head: and draw out from them blood according to measure of his strength.
Deinde fac sedere infirmum inter manus tuas, et conuerte aurem eius ad superiora, et finde fissuram paruam in radice auris apud adipem eius in loco depresso ipsi: et sit fissura lunaris figurae, donec peruenias ad lapidem: deinde aufer eum cum eo, quod est tibi possibile ex instrumentis.	Then make the patient sit between your hands and turn his ear to the top, and find a small fissure at the root of the ear next to fat on the lower side: it is in the shape of the moon until you reach the stone: then remove it with what is possible from instruments.
Deinde sue fissuram ab hora tua cum uelocitate, et cura ipsam, donec sanetur.	Then address your cleft at its proper time and promptly treat it until healed.
Quod si res cadens in aurem est ex uno granorum, quae crescunt, et inflantur: tunc administra extractionem eius.	If the object that has fallen into the ear is from one of the beans that grow and swell: then provide its removal.
Si autem non obedit tibi ad exitum, tunc accipe spatumile tenue, subtile, secundum hanc formam.	However, if it does not yield to you at the exit, then take a thin and delicate bandage according to this shape.
Et administra cum eo abscisionem illius speciei ex granis, quae cadunt in aurem, et non facias illud, quando tu cogitas, quod illud granum iam humectatum est per uaporem auris, donec ponis ipsum frusta multa: deinde extrahe ea cum uncinis, aut cum gesti subtili, aut cum suctione, sicut diximus, nam extractio eius alleuiatur.	And administer a cutting of the same kind as that which falls into the ear from beans that grow and swell; do not make it when you think that bean has already been moistened by the humidity of the ear, until you place many fragments: then extract them with forceps or with a fine instrument or by suction, as we have said, for its extraction is diminished.
In aqua autem quae ingreditur in aurem, oportet ut utatur infirmus sternutatione cum condisi in primis: et iam impleuit aurem suam cum aliquanto cotto ueteri: et est iacens super illam aurem, in qua est aqua.	However, the water that enters into the ear should be used with weakness and shaken according to its condition at first: and now it has filled up her own ear somewhat from old practice: and lies on top of the ear where there is water.
Si ergo egreditur per illud, est bonum.	If it then is removed through that method, it's beneficial.
Et si non: tunc accipe lapides multos, secundum longitudinem digiti, tenues, lenes, et calefac eos cum igne parumper, et intromittat infirmus ex eis unum in foramen auris suae: et saliat super pedem suum unum ex illa parte, et percutiat cum lapide alio super lapidem qui est in aure.	And if not: then the patient should take many small and thin stones according to the length of their finger, heat them slightly over fire and insert one weakly ill person into his ear hole: he steps on it with one foot from that side, and strikes with the stone another stone which is in the ear.
Non ergo cesset facere illud cum lapide et lapide, donec egrediatur tota aqua.	Do not cease doing this with a stone and a stone until all water has been removed.
Et iam egreditur aqua ita, ut accipias ex parpyro, aut ex iunco unum, et intromittas extremitatem eius unam in aurem: et accendas extremitatem alteram cum igne, donec comburatur plurimum eius.	And now water has been removed so you should take one thing from fire or reed and insert the end of it into your ear: then ignite the other end with fire until most of it is burnt.
Deinde itera iuncum alium, et fac illud multotiens, donec egrediatur tota aqua: et extrahe ipsam cum cannula secundum quod praemissum est in lapide.	Then take another reed and do that multiple times until all the water is removed: then extract it with a tube as previously described in stone.
In extractione autem animalis intrantis in eam, si est parui corporis, ut pulex, et ei simile, cura ipsum sicut dixi in diuisione.	However, when extracting an entering creature such as a flea or similar into it, treat it as I have described in division [of the body].
Sed si est corporis magni, quod appareat sensui: tunc administra extractionem eius cum gesti, et uncinis: et res eius est facilior omnibus, quae tenentur in aure.	But if it is of a body that appears large to the sense: then perform its extraction with levers and hooks, and this makes things easier for those held in the ear.
In extractione autem uermis generati in aure, quando curas eum cum eo quod diximus in diuisione, et in tractatu distilationum, et non confert curatio tua: tunc oportet ut aspicias aurem in sole.	However, when extracting worms generated in the ear, and concerning their treatment as we have discussed in division [of the body], and not complicating matters with your intervention: then one should look at the ear to the sun (or light).
Si ergo apparet illic aliquid ex uermibus, tunc extrahe illud cum gesti, aut cum uncinis subtilibus.	But if something appears from these worms: then extract that with delicate levers or hooks.
Si autem non apparet illic aliquid, tunc accipe cannulam, cuius haec est forma, stricta inferius, ampla superius: et intromitte extremitatem subtilem in aurem secundum quantitatem quod tolerat eam infirmus: deinde suge cum ea suctione forti.	But if nothing appears from these worms, then take the tube (or pipe), which has this shape: it is narrow below and wide above: and insert its slender end into the ear according to how much a sick person can tolerate; then remove by suction with strong pressure.
Fac illud multotiens, donec egrediantur omnes uermes.	Perform that procedure many times until all worms are expelled.
Si autem non obediunt tibi ad exitum, tunc opila circumitum cannulae cum caera, sicut dixi in lapide.	If however they do not obey you to completion, then with a small tube surround the cysts as I have described in stone.
Quod si non egrediuntur cum eo quod diximus: tunc administra distillationes quas iam experti sunt antiqui in interfectione uermium: et inuenies illud in tractatu distillationum.	But if they do not come out as we have said: then employ the treatments for worms that the ancient ones were known to use with distillations; and you will find it discussed in the treatise on distillations.
Et sit effusio tua qua effundis olea et medicinas in aurem cum hoc instrumento, cuius forma depicta est hic.	And let your poultice be as you pour the oil and medicine into an ear with this tool, whose shape is depicted here.
Sicut uides fac ipsum ex argento, aut aere, inferius strictum, in quo sit foramen paruum, amplum superius.	As you see it made of silver or brass with a small opening below and a wider one above.
Sit ergo ut impellens quod est in concauitate cannulae, sit ex aere decenter factum.	So make what is inserted into the hollow of the tube to be properly made from brass.
Et si uis, accipe radium, et inuolue in extremitate eius cottum inuolutione decenti: deinde proiice oleum, aut succum, aut quod uis ex istis medicinis in cannulam: et ipsa sit in aure: deinde intromitte radium cum cotto desuper, et exprime ipsum manu tua compressione temperata, donec impellatur oleum in concauitate auditus, et sentiat ipsum infirmus interius: et illud quod infunditur in aurem, sit iam calefactum cum igne parumper: et caue ne sit res quae distillatur in eam frigida ualde: medicinae enim non tolerant illud.	And if you wish to use the rod, take a reddish-colored wire and wind it around its end with an orderly coil; then pour oil or sulfur into the tube: and that which is poured in from these medicines should be in the ear: and so warm up the rod by placing it over fire just slightly.
¶ De cura opilationis accidentis Auri.	Of treating a gold coin lodged in the throat.
Caput VII.	Chapter VII.
Quandoque egrediuntur quidam infantes ex uentribus matrum suarum non perforati.	Sometimes children are born from the wombs of their mothers without being pierced (by a surgical instrument).
Et iam accidit etiam quibusdam hominibus opilatio in meatu Auris a uulnere, aut carne nata in ea.	And it has even happened to some men that the lodging of a gold coin occurs due to an injury or because flesh was born there (within).
Et haec opilatio quandoque fit in profundo foraminis Auris, quam non consequitur uisus: et quandoque accidit ad exteriora foraminis parum, et consequitur eam uisus.	And sometimes this lodging of a gold coin occurs within the deep part of the ear canal and does not require force (for removal): at other times it occurs nearer to the opening and can be removed with ease.
Illa ergo quae accidit in profundo Auris, et quam non comprehendit aspectus, est in pluribus dispositionibus difficilis sanationis.	Therefore, that which occurs within the deep part of the ear and cannot be grasped by sight is often difficult to cure.
Et in illa quam consequitur uisus, oportet ut ponas Aurem infirmi in sole, et aspicias in ea: tunc si uides opilationem apparentem, aperi eam cum spatumili subtili, cuius forma est haec quae sequitur, sit extremitas eius in qua sit quaedam latitudo parua, cuius quaedam pars sit acuta: et reliquum spatumile sit duarum laterum lenium: ut non laedat aurem.	And in that which can be reached with force (for removal), it is adviseb to place the sick ear towards the light and examine it: then if you see the lodging of the coin apparent, open it with a thin cloth-like sponge, whose shape is as follows: one end should have a slight width, some part of which is sharp; and the rest should be smooth like two edges. So that it does not damage the ear.
Si ergo opilatio est a carne nata in meatu auris: tunc tene eam cum uncino subtili, et incide eam cum facilitate uehementi, donec auferatur tota caro.	If there is inflamm cupped flesh on the ear canal: then hold it with a delicate hook and incise it with great ease until all the flesh has been removed.
Quod si opilatio est in profundo auris: tunc accipe radium subtilem, lenem, et calefac ipsum cum igne parumper: deinde mitte ipsum in meatum auris.	If the inflammation is deep within the ear canal: then take a thin rod, blunt it and heat it slightly with fire: then insert it into the ear canal.
Si ergo senseris opilationem cum eo, quod inuenit infirmus cum grauitate auditus, conare apertionem eius cum facilitate: et caue, ne uulneres neruos auris.	If you feel the inflammation with something that the patient found to be very heavy in terms of hearing, try opening it with ease: and be careful not to injure the nerves of the ear.
Deinde pone in aurem licinium secundum quantitatem amplitudinis foraminis, quod inuoluisti in unguento aegyptio: fac illud aliquot diebus, donec sis securus de consolidatione uulneris.	Then place the licorice syrup you made from the Egyptian ointment according to the size of the opening that was made: let it sit for several days until you are sure about the healing of the wound.
Aut accipe licinium, et infunde ipsum in aqua rosata, et pulueriza super ipsum zegi tritum, et utere ipso.	Alternatively, take the licorice and dissolve it in rose water, then apply a poultice of finely ground meal on top: use that.
Quod si uides aurem iam apostemari: tunc oportet ut extrahas licinium, et permittas ipsum cum licinio alio, quod inuolues in caeroto quod sit factum cum oleo rosato, donec sedetur apostema calidum: deinde cura ipsum usquequo sanetur.	If you see the ear is already starting to stick out: it should be detached from its base using lime and allow it with a compress soaked in rose oil, which was done when an abscess formed on the brain with olive oil; then attend until it heals.
Si autem accidat fluxus sanguinis: tunc submerge spongiam, aut pannos in aqua frigida, et pone super eam aurem: et utere reliqua curatione, quae abscindit fluxum sanguinis praedicta in tractatu distillationum.	However, if bleeding occurs: immerse a sponge or cloths in cold water and place them over the ear; then continue with the rest of the treatment that removes the predicted blood flow as described in the treatise on distillations.
¶ De cura Altheli palpebrarum.	Regarding the cure for Althel's eyebrows: If you notice an injury or a defect, then gently cleanse it with warm water and apply rose oil regularly until healed; if necessary, use small stitches to close larger wounds.
Caput VIII.	Head VIII (This could refer to the eighth chapter in the book but does not require translation).
Isti Althelil qui accidunt in Palpebris oculi, quandoque sunt humidi, et sunt sicci.	These Altheli that occur on the eyebrows and are sometimes moist and dry: (Here would follow a specific treatment from Albucasis's text which is not provided in the original query).
Oportet ergo ut teneas eos cum tenaliis: aut cum uncino, et incidas eos cum spatumili a radicibus suis.	It is necessary that you hold them with forceps or pincers and sever their roots with the Spatulli.
Deinde pone super loca zegi tritum.	Then place it over the triturated wound area.
Si autem ex eis fluat sanguis, tunc cauteriza eos cum cauterio lenticulari subtili.	If blood flows from them, then cauterize with a fine cylindrical cautery.
Et cauterizare eos, est melius post incisionem.	And to cauterize them is better after the incision.
Multotiens enim redeunt quando remanet ex radicibus suis aliquid.	 Often it is necessary to leave something in its original place when roots remain with them.
Et quando cauterizantur cum igne, comburuntur illae radices, et non redeunt.	 And when they are burned with fire, the roots get burnt and do not return.
¶ De cura Grandinum palpebrarum oculi.	 In treating a grand malady of the eyelids.
Caput IX.	 Chapter IX: Eye Care
Multotiens accidit in palpebris aliquid quod assimilatur Crandini in fortitudine sua, et sua duricie, et propter illud nominatur Grando: et est aggregatio humiditatis grossae in palpebra superiore, et palpebra inferiore.	 Often something occurs in the eyelids that is similar to Crandini in its strength and hardness, and for this reason it is called Grand. It's an accumulation of thick moisture in the upper eyelid and lower eyebrow.
Operatio ergo in eis est, ut consideres tunc, si est Grando procedens in eo, quod apparet de palpebra, et mouentur ad omnem partem, et res eius est facilis.	 Therefore, when considering if Grand is emerging from the eyelid and they move to all sides, it's an easy condition.
Finde ergo super eam fissura per latitudinem.	 So find a slit over that gap in width.
Deinde excoria eam ab omni parte cum facilitate, donec euadat.	 Then remove it from every part with ease, until it improves.
Deinde suspende eam cum uncino, et abscinde ipsam.	First suspend it with a hook and then detach it.
Si autem non praeparatur tibi abscisio eius, nisi postquam tu penetras palpebram cum incisione parumper, tunc nocet infirmo illud in aliquo.	If it is not prepared for its excision from you beforehand and if you do not pierce the eyelid with a slight incision until afterward, then that injury will harm the sick person in some way.
Quod si fissura est magna: tunc aggrega ipsam cum sutura: et cura ipsam, donec sanetur.	But if the cleft is large: then bind it with a stitch and care for it until it heals.
Et si est parua, non superueniet tibi malum ex ea.	And if it is small, no harm will come to you from it.
Vnguentum enim restaurat ipsam, et incarnat eam.	For the ointment restores it and makes it reddening.
Et si grando est decliuis ad interiora auris uersus superficiem intrinsecam, tunc inuersa palpebram, et suspende grandinem cum uncino: praeter quod indigeas incisione, et preme eam ab omni parte.	And if the bone reaches towards the interior of the ear against its inner surface, then attack the palpebral fossa with a hook and suspend it using a lever: besides this, you will need an incision from all sides.
Quod si elongatur palpebra per incisionem, non nocet illud in aliquo.	What if the bone is extended through incision? It causes no harm to anything.
Deinde ablue oculum post incisionem grandinis, cum aqua salsa: et cura locum cum eo quod incarnat, donec sanetur infirmus.	Then cleanse the eye after removing the foreign body with a solution of saltwater: and take care of the place as if it were swol circulate to heal.
¶ De cura Axirnath palpebrarum.	Regarding the treatment of eyelids.
Caput X.	Heading XI.
Axirnath est adeps qui generatur in tunicis palpebrae superioris: et plurimum quidem accidit illud pueris: et ipsum grauat oculos eorum, et accidunt eis catarri in matutinis, et non possunt intueri lumen solis, propterea, quod lachrymae properant ad eos, et propter illud uides eos discumbere super facies suas semper, et super eas dormiunt, et sunt palpebrae eorum sub superciliis humidae, quas iam cooperuit inflatio: et eminentia quidem Axirnath apparens est oculo, et quando tu premis locum cum digitis tuis, sentis Axirnath inter eos.	Axirnath is a gland that grows in the upper eyelid skin: it happens particularly to boys; indeed, this causes their eyes to bulge and they develop morning cataracts, so cannot see sunlight because tears flow towards them, and due to this, you see them lying on their faces all the time, always sleeping with wet brows. And these are eyelids that are under humid foreheads, which have already been clogged by inflammation: indeed, Axirnath is visible from the eye when you press it between your fingers.
Et modus operationis eius est, ut ponat infirmus caput suum in sinu tuo.	And the method of this procedure is that you place the sick person's head in your lap.
Deinde accipe pannum lini, et praepara in eo licinia, et fac ex illo licinio circulum secundum quantitatem quod continet Axirnath ab omni parte.	Then take a piece of linen and prepare the wound on it according to the amount that contains Axirnath from every part.
Deinde pone eum super eam, et preme cum digitis tuis ab omni parte, ut aggregetur Axirnath in medio circuli.	Then place it over it and press with your fingers all around so that Axirnath is gathered in the center of the circle.
Deinde finde in medio illius humiditatis cum spatumili incidente fissuras per latitudinem, et non sit fissura maior illa quae fit in phlebotomia in profundo.	Then find a point of moisture with slight cracks across its width, and the main crack should not be as it is done during deep vein puncture.
Aut oportet ut findas cutem totam, donec peruenias ad Axirnath in pluribus enim dispositionibus procedit Axirnath ex fissura secundum formam frusti pinguedinis albae.	Or it is necessary to find skin all around until you reach the swelling, as Axirnath progresses in many forms from the crack according to the shape of a white goose's feather.
Extrahe ergo eam cum panno, quem infiltrasti inter digitos tuos ad exteriora: et tu reuoluis manum tuam ad dextram et sinistram, donec dispergatur: et caue, ne addas in fissura, ut non peruenias cum spatumili ad oculum, et laedas eum.	So extract it with the cloth which you have placed between your fingers: and move your hand to the right and left until dispersed: and be careful that you do not add in the crack, so that you do not reach the swelling or harm it.
Si autem non appareat tibi Axirnath in principio fissurae, tu addas in fissura parum cum facilitate, donec procedat Axirnath.	However, if Axioth does not appear at the beginning of the fissure, you should add it with slight force until Axioth moves forward.
Deinde extrahe eam, sicut diximus.	Then extract it as we have said.
Deinde submerge pannos in aceto et aqua, et pone eos super locum, et stringe eum cum puluillis.	Then soak the bandages in vinegar and water, place them over the area, and press with a sponge.
Et ex hominibus sunt qui terunt salem, et ponunt ipsum in concauitate fissurae, ut liquefiat quod remansit ex illa humiditate.	And there are people who use salt and place it into the depression of the fissure so that what remains from its moisture dissolves.
Deinde cura ipsam, donec sanetur.	Then treat it until it heals.
Si autem accidat in loco apostema calidum, tune cura ipsum cum emplastris sedatiuis, donec sanetur.	However, if it occurs at a hot abscess spot, then treat it with cooling plasters until it heals.
¶ De modis Ataxmir oculi, id est, cum palpebra mollificatur oculi, unde fit ut rugetur sicut non debet.	And about the methods of Ataxmir for the eyes, that is when the eyelid softens from the eye, so it swells as it should not.
Caput XI.	Head Eleven.
Quando nascuntur in palpebris oculi pili additi praeter cursum sub pilis naturalibus, et antiquantur: tunc ipsi nocent oculo, et faciunt accidere modos aegritudinum, sicut lachrymas assiduas, et mollificationem palpebrarum, et albuginem, donec fit illud caussa destructionis oculi.	When hairs are added to the eyelids beyond their natural course and lengthen: they then harm the eye, causing conditions like persistent tears, softening of the eyelids, and pigmentation, until it leads to the destruction of the eye.
Et Ataxmir quidem oculi curatur secundum quatuor modos.	And indeed, the eyes are cured according to four methods.
Aut per cauterium cum igne.	Or with a heated iron.
Aut cum medicina acuta, secundum quod praemissum est in capitulo cauterii.	Or with sharp medicine as is described in the chapter on cauterization.
Aut curatur Ataxmir per incisionem et suturam.	Or by treating Ataxia through cutting and stitching.
Aut per cannas, secundum quod ego dicam.	Or with reeds, as I will explain.
Oportet ut ponas caput infirmi in sinu tuo.	It is necessary that you place the sick person's head in your lap.
Deinde conuerte palpebram oculi manu tua sinistra.	Then turn over the patient's left eyelid with your left hand.
Si ergo conuertitur, bonum est.	If then it is turned, that is good.
Et si non: intromitte acum in eam, in qua sit filum ab inferiori parte palpebrae, et fac penetrare acum cum filo desuper, et sit illud prope pilos ipsos, id est, prope marginem palpebrae, in quo nascuntur pili: et trahe filum ad superiora cum palpebra, et conuerte eam cum radio.	And if not, then insert the needle into it from the lower part of the eyelid, and penetrate with the needle upward, so that it is near the hairs themselves, that is to say, near the edge of the eyelids where the hairs grow: and pull out the thread alongside the upper eyelid, and turn over the eyelid with your finger.
Deinde finde in interiori parte palpebrae sub pilis additis cum spatumili incidente a lachrymali maiore usque ad lachrymale minus.	Then find inside the inner part of the eyelid with added hair and close to the larger tear duct down to the smaller one.
Deinde extrahe filum, et pone sub palpebra puluillum paruum ex cotto, aut panno: deinde signa super palpebram cum encaustro, quod sit sicut figura folii myrti.	Then remove the thread and place it under the eyelid of wool or cloth: then mark on the eyelid with hot cauterization like the shape of a myrtle leaf.
Verumtamen oportet, ut fit figura secundum quantitatem et eleuationem palpebrae: quoniam iam diuersificatur illud in hominibus.	However, it is necessary that the figure follows according to the quantity and elevation of the eyelid: for this has been diversified among men for a long time.
Ex eis enim est, qui indiget ut incidatur ex palpebra quantitas magna, secundum quantitatem quae mollificatur a palpebra.	For those who need the incision to be made from the eyelid in large quantities, it must follow according to the quantity that softens from the eyebrow.
Deinde cum spatumili finde super duas lineas quas signasti, et incipe a lachrymali maiore usque ad lachrymale minus, et sit fissura una prope pilos naturales, sicut est grossitudo radii.	Then find on top of the two lines you marked and start from the larger tear duct to the smaller one, making a single incision near natural hairs like the thickness of a radius.
Deinde intromitte uncinum in uno duorum angulorum cutis.	Insert a hook into one of two angles of the skin.
Deinde excoria ipsam totam.	Then scrape off the affected area completely.
Deinde aggrega cum sutura duo labia, cum acu et filo lana subtili: et absterge sanguinem, et fac adhaerere quod superfluit ex filis super duo supercilia, cum quibusdam rebus inuiscantibus, si uis facere illud: et si non, non cures.	Then join the two edges with sutures using a needle and fine thread: clean up any excess blood, ensure that it sticks to the threads placed over both sides of the wound, using some sticky substances if necessary; and if you do this, don't worry.
Deinde dimitte suturam et fila usque ad tres dies, aut quatuor: postea cura illud.	Then remove the stitches and threads for three or four days, then care for it.
Et si uis, dimitte uulnus absque sutura, et cura ipsum cum eo, quod exsiccat et constringit.	And if you will, let the wound heal without a stitch and care for it as such until it dries out and contracts.
Nam palpebra eleuatur apud sigillationem uulneris et aggregationem eius: sed futura est melior.	Because the eyelid is damaged at the time of sealing and healing, but it will be better in the future.
Hunc modum curandi Ataxmir docuerunt antiqui.	This way of treatment were taught by the ancients.
Verumtamen in eo est sollicitudo super infirmum, et est ex bona operatione, et non est in eo timor.	However, there is concern for the patient and it comes from good surgery, and fear does not exist within it.
Et modus alius est in Ataxmir etiam: et est, ut signes super palpebram figuram, quae sit sicut figura folii myrti, sicut narrauimus.	And another method is also in Atazmiri: and it exists, with signs above the eyelids that are like a leaf of myrtle as we have described.
Deinde eleua palpebram cum tribus uncinis separatis, aut aggregatis, secundum formam hanc quae sequitur, deinde incide quod superfluit cum forficibus paruis, secundum hanc formam, cum aequalitate incisionis.	Next, the eyelid with three separated or connected hooks follows this pattern: then make what is above the eye resembling three small scissors of equal length.
Si autem non est tibi possibile tenere uncinum, et non aequatur illud: tunc accipe acum in qua sit filum, et intromitte ipsum in medio figurae: et intromitte filum aliud prope lachrymale maius, et filum secundum prope lachrymale minus: et aggrega inter digitos tuos fila cum aequalitate.	But if it is not possible for you to hold the hooks equal, and they are unequal: then take an awl where there is thread, and insert that into the middle of the figure: and insert another thread near the lacrimal gland larger; and a third thread close to the smaller one. Then join the threads with your fingers equally.
Deinde eleua manum tuam eleuatione aequali: et eleua cutem super quam est signatum cotum, sicut narrauimus.	Next, raise your hand evenly and then lift the skin above which is marked as we have mentioned.
Deinde aggrega duo labia uulneris cum sutura: et cura ipsum, donec sanetur.	Firstly, gather two lips of the wound with a stitch; and then care for it until it heals.
Si uero accidat apostema apud incisionem tuam, aut fissuram tuam: seda illud apostema cum caeroto, et his similibus, ex unguentis sedantibus.	If indeed there is an abscess near your incision or fracture: tie the abscess with a tourniquet, and heal it using similar medications.
Et quandoque accidit palpebrae etiam, ut conuertantur pili eius.	And sometimes even the eyelids turn into hairs as well.
