Si ergo consolidatur locus, et nascitur in eo caro, et abscinditur cursus saniei: et remanet quadraginta diebus, et non renouatur, et non apostematur, et non accidit in eo accidens: tunc scias quia iam sanatus est.	If therefore the place becomes solidified and flesh grows therein, and a tract of pus is formed but does not discharge; it remains for forty days, and does not suppurate or fester, nor any accident befalls; then you shall know that it has healed.
Et si non, tunc non est in eo ingenium, nisi reducere fistulam ad foramen nasi, secundum hanc formam.	And if not, there is no cure unless you return the hole to the nostril passage, according to this method.
Et est, ut detegas ab osse secundo cum ferro, aut cum medicina acuta: et cum detectum est os, tunc accipe terebrum secundum hanc formam, sit extremitas ferrea, triangulata: et lignum eius sit pyramis extenuata usque ad extremitatem, sicut uides.	And thus you reveal the bone with iron or sharp medicine; and when it is uncovere d, then take a trepann in accordance to this form: its tip should be of iron; and its length should be pyramidal, tapering towards one end as thou seest.
Deinde pone illud super os ipsum: et sit illud prope lachrymale: et elonga manum tuam ab oculo parum.	Place that there over your mouth and near the tear ducts. Extend your hand slightly away from the eye.
Deinde reuolue manum tuam cum terebro, donec penetret os, et sentiat illud infirmus: per hoc quod inuenit uentum exire ex eo, quando tenet manum suam super nasum suum.	Then pull out your hand with the instrument until it touches the bone and feels that the patient is weakened; through this, he found the wind to come out from him when he holds his hand over his nose.
Ergo tunc restaura locum cum medicinis stipticis exiccantibus, sicut docui te.	Therefore then restore the place with drawing agents as I have taught you.
Cum ergo nascitur caro, et induratur locus: tunc materia quae effundebatur ad exteriora, redit ad nasum: est ergo leuius illud super infirmum.	So when the body is born and hardens, then the material that flowed out externally returns to the nose; thus it becomes lighter over the weakened one.
¶ De reductione eminentiae Oculi.	§ On reducing protruding eye.
Caput XX.	Head twenty. (The translation of the section heading is not provided as it's a directive to indicate that this is about a specific topic, in this case "reducing protruding eye.")
Quando eminet Oculus cum totalitate sua, et non accidit in uisu nocumentum, neque diminutio: tunc oportet ut soluas infirmum: deinde phlebotomes eum: postea ponas uentosas in ceruice absque scarificatione, sed cum suctione.	When the eye is protruding entirely without causing harm or diminishing vision, then it should be relieved; next perform bloodletting on the weakened one: afterwards apply vents to his nose without cutting but with suction. (This suggests a procedure involving bloodletting and nasal vent application for correcting an excessively protruding eye.)
Deinde pone super Oculum linimentum quod fit ex acacia, et aloe, et olibano, et sarcocolla.	Then place a poultice on the eye that is made of Acacia, Aloe, Myrrh, and Sarcocoelon.
Deinde stringe Oculum desuper super emplastrum cum puluillis multis.	Then bind the eye above with a paste (emplastre) using many linen threads.
Et modus puluillorum est: ut accipias pannos lenes, multos, et duplicetur omnis pannus ex eis super quatuor: fac ex eis multos: deinde pone eos unum super alium, secundum quantitatem qua indiget Oculus: deinde stringe super ipsos cum panno duro strictura forti.	And the manner of making linen threads is as follows: you should take light, many and double all cloth from these four; then make them many; then place one over another according to the amount that the eye requires: then bind them together with a hard cloth.
Et itera uentosas cum suctione sine scarificatione.	And repeat using leeches without incision (scarification).
Deinde aufer uentosas, et dimitte oculum strictum die et nocte.	Then remove cataracts and leave the eye uncovered both day and night.
Si autem ligamentum iterum mollificatur, tunc oportet ut stringatur multum: deinde aufer ligamentum post diem et noctem, sicut diximus.	If the ligament is again made supple, then it should be tightened a lot: remove the ligament after day and night as we said earlier.
Si ergo uides oculum iam redisse uuae tunicae, est bonum: et si non, tunc itera emplastrum, et puluillos, et stricturam, et uentosas, donec sanetur.	If you now see the eye restored with a new membrane, that's good: if not, repeat bandaging, poultices, tightening, and removing cataracts until it heals.
¶ De incisionie Vuae tunicae.	About the incision of the eye's membrane.
Caput XXI.	Chapter 21.
Quando accidit disruptio in tunica Vuea, deinde eminet et procedit extra palpebras sicut granum Vuae, et foedatur forma hominis propter illud, et uis incidere illud: tunc operatio in eo est, secundum quod narro: et est, ut intromittas acum in radice Vuae ab inferiori ad superiorem partem.	When a rupture occurs on the eye's membrane, then it protrudes and appears outside of the eyelids like a grain of wheat, causing disfigurement to the person because of that: this is when surgery should occur, as I will narrate; and it involves inserting an acupuncture needle in at the root of the eye from its lower part upwards.
Deinde intromitte acum aliam in qua sit filum duplum a parte lachrymalis, et fac eam penetrare: et dimitte acum primam secundum dispositionem suam.	Then insert another one where the thread of the lacrimal part is double and let it penetrate; remove the first according to its arrangement.
Deinde incide locum fili dupli, et liga cum eo partem Vuae in circumitu acus: et stringe eam multum.	Then incise the place of the double thread and tie it with the part of a silk wire around its rotation; tighten it firmly.
Deinde extrahe acum, et pone super oculum lanam infusam in albugine oui: et dimitte eum, donec cadat filum cum Vua.	Then extract the object and place a piece of woolen cloth soaked in alcohol over the eye; let it remain until the thread with silk wire comes out.
Deinde cura oculum cum eo, quod confortat ipsum, donec sanetur uulnus.	Then care for the eye that has been affected by this object until the wound heals.
Et quandoque stringitur Vua ab omni parte cum circulo ex panno, donec addat oculus eminentiam magnam.	And when it is tied with silk wire from all parts in a circle, until the eye becomes greatly prominent.
Deinde perforetur cum spatumili subtili, quod perueniat ad profundum oculi, et currat humiditas albuginea, et descendat oculus, et ingrediatur statim: deinde stringe eum, donec sanetur.	Then it is pierced with a thin spate and goes deep into the eye; let moisture from the albugineal part flow out of it; let the eye descend immediately; then tighten it until the wound heals.
¶ De curatione Alcomnati.	From the treatment of a hernia.
Caput XXII.	Heading Twenty-Two.
Haec Aegritudo quae nominatur Alcomnati, non, est nisi sanies, quae aggregatur in oculo, similis aquae descendenti, et non est ipsa.	This disease known as Alzheimer's is not merely pus that accumulates in the eye; it resembles water flowing down and is not itself.
Et modus operandi in ea est, ut facias sedere infirmum super sedem praeparatum, uel directum.	And the method of operation for this is to make a sick person sit on a prepared bed or table.
Deinde accipe caput eius manibus tuis a partibus duabus, et moue ipsum, donec uideas saniem peruenire ad inferiora oculis tuis.	Then take its head with your hands from both sides and move it until the sight of the lower eye appears to you.
Deinde figatur, et non descendat, et absoluatur lumen: et uideat infirmus res sicut uidebat: et si non descendit inferius, scias quia est aqua.	Then let it be fixed and not descended; the light shall see as it saw before: and if it does not go downwards, know that it is water.
Si autem non praeparatur descensus saniei cum eo quod diximus, tunc fac sedere infirmum inter manus tuas.	If however the descent of the sight has not been prepared as we have described, then make the patient sit between your hands.
Deinde accipe spatumile subtile, et finde cum eo supra panniculum corneum parumper apud continuationem coniunctiuae cum tunica cornea in corona, donec egrediatur sanies.	Then take a thin cushion and place it slightly above the surface of the skin' vice-saddle near the connection with the corneal ring until the pus comes out.
Cum ergo egreditur, tunc distilla in oculum aquam calidam in qua miscuisti mel: aut aquam in qua iam bullisti foenumgraecum et mel: deinde curetur cum reliqua curatione, donec sanetur.	When it has thus come out, then distill warm water into the eye where you have already mixed honey and juice of the fennel plant; or in which you have previously boiled fenugreek seeds: afterwards treat with the remaining treatment until healed.
¶ De cura aquae, quae descendit in oculo, uel cataracta.	On the treatment of water entering the eye, or a catar prolapse.
Caput XXIII.	Head Twenty-Three.
Iam Diximus species aquae in diuisione, et quae conuenit ad perforandum sermone declarante et exponente, tunc accipe illud idem secundum sanitatem.	Now We Have Said of the water's division and what comes to its piercing through speech declaring and explaining, then take that same thing according to health.
Tunc ergo oportet ut facias sedere infirmum inter manus tuas quadratum, oppositum lumini, prope solem: et liga oculum eius sanum, et stringe eum ualde: deinde palpebram oculi eius manu tua dextra, si oculus in quo est aqua, est oculus sinister: aut manu tua sinistra, si oculus est dexter.	Then it should be made to sit an ill person between your hands squared against the light and near the sun: and bind his eye sound, and tie him tightly: then with your right hand palpate the eyelid of the eye in which is the water, if the eye on which the water is is left: or with your left hand, if the eye affected is right.
Deinde accipe manu tua dextra almagda, si oculus est sinister: aut manu tua sinistra, si oculus est dexter.	Then take oncise with your right hand if the eye affected is left; or with your left hand, if the eye affected is right.
Deinde pone extremitatem almagda prope coronam per grossitudinem radii in ipsa albedine oculi apparente lachrymalis minoris: deinde impelle almagda cum uirtute: et tu reuoluis cum eo manum tuam, donec penetret in albuginem oculi: et sentias, quod almagda iam peruenit ad rem uacuam.	Then place the tip of oncise near to the corner of the lacrimal gland as if it were a radius of great size: then push with strength; and pull back your hand with it, until it penetrates into the eye's albumen: and you will feel that it has already arrived at an empty place.
Et oportet, ut sit mensura itineris almagda ad profundum, mensura spacii quod est a pupilla usque ad finem nigredinis: et est corona oculi.	And there must be the measure of the Almagest's journey to depth, which is from the pupil up to the end of blackness: and it is the crown of the eye.
Uidebis enim ea in ipsa pupilla uisione oculi, propter claritatem tunicae corneae.	For you see that therein within the very pupil of the eye, due to the clarity of the cornea's tunic.
Deinde pone almagda usque ad locum in quo est aqua.	Then from Almagest up until where is water.
Deinde preme ipsum inferius uice una post aliam.	Next, press down on it below with one veil after another.
Si ergo descendit aqua statim, tunc infirmus uidet illud super quod aperit uisum suum statim, et almagda in oculo suo.	If then water descends immediately, the weak one sees that which opens its own vision right away, and Almagest inside his eye.
Deinde quiescas paululum.	Then rest for a little while.
Si ergo descendat aqua, tunc depone eam secundo, praeter quod egrediatur almagda.	If then the water descends, lay it down again secondly, except that Almagest emerges out.
Quando ergo figitur, et non ascendit: tunc extrahe almagda cum facilitate: et tu reuoluis manum tuam paulatim.	When it is then fixed, and does not rise upwards: Then extract Almagest with ease; and you gradually roll back your own hand.
Deinde dissolue in aqua aliquid ex sale claro gemmae: et ablue cum eo oculum deintus.	Then dissolve something from clear saltwater and wash out the eye from inside with it.
Deinde pone extra oculum totum stuppam, aut lanam infusam oleo rosato, et albugine oui: et liga cum eo oculum sanum.	Then place a completely soaked suppository or an infusion of oil with rose tincture in the good eye and bandage it together.
Nos autem, et illi qui sunt nostri temporis, ponimus super eum ciminum tritum cum albumine oui.	We, however, will place powdered henbane over it with egg white.
Quod si non obedit tibi almagda ad introitum in oculum propter duriciem suam, quoniam ex hominibus est, cuius oculus est durus ualde: tunc oportet ut accipias spatumile, quod nominatur Alberid, cuius haec est forma.	However, if the almagda does not fit at the entrance of the eye due to its hardness, as it is from a person with very hard eyes: then you must take in sponge-like material called Alberid, which has this shape.
Pefora ergo cum eo ipsam coniunctiuam tantum, et non ultimes manum tuam in foramine: et non est nisi ut facias uiam ad almagda locum subtilem.	Therefore you should apply the sponge-like material to it only as tightly connected and do not extend your hand into the hole: and it is only to make a way for the delicate almagpta.
Deinde intromitte almagda, secundum quod diximus.	Then introduce an enema, as we have said.
Et apud complementum operis tui, praeparetur infirmo dormitorium decenter factum, in quo dormiat super dorsum suum in domo tenebrosa: et prohibeatur ab omnibus motibus, et a tussi: et pone cibum eius illud quo lenitur natura eius: et non moueat caput suum dextra, neque sinistra omnino.	And for the completion of your operation, ensure that the sick man's bed is centrally made in a dark room where he can lie on his back: prevent him from all movements and coughing, place food suitable to ease his nature, and do not allow his head to move right or left at all.
Et sit ligamentum secundum dispositionem suam usque ad diem tertium.	And let the bandage be kept in its proper position until the third day.
Deinde solue illud in illa domo tenebrosa, et experire uisum eius: et fac eum uidere res.	Then wash it in that dark house and rinse your eyes: and let him see things.
Deinde reduc ligamentum usque ad diem septimum.	Then reduce the bandage until the seventh day.
Et non oportet ut faciat illud in hora curationis, aut post incisionem statim: imo oportet, ut alienes illud: propterea quod aqua ascendit uelociter per aspectum uehementem.	And it is not necessary to do that during the time of treatment or immediately after cutting: indeed, let others do it; because water quickly rises through a strong impression.
Si autem accidit apostema calidum: tunc oportet ut soluas oculum ante septimum: et rectifica illud cum eo quod sedat apostema, donec sedatur: tunc absolue ipsius uisum, et pone super faciem eius orale quo regatur uisus eius sub eo diebus aliquot, ipso existente in illa domo tenebrosa.	If however an abscess is present: then it should be drained by the seventh day and corrected with what soothes the abscess until it heals; then one should tie off its source, and apply something over its mouth to regulate its breath for several days when in that dark house.
Deinde egrediatur a domo gradatim, et conuersetur in casis suis.	Then he should gradually leave the house, and be put on his sick bed.
Et scias, quod in zaltea non excusatur discipulus a uisione aliquotiens: tunc enim audeat super operationem.	And you know that the student should not skip observing several times at Zaltes: for then he may dare to perform surgery.
Et iam quidem peruenit ad nos quidam ex illis qui sunt de Alayrach, qui dixit, quod factum fuit in Alayrach magdan perforatum, quo sugitur aqua.	And indeed it has been brought to us by some from Alairac who said that at Alairac there was a perforation through which water is drawn out.
Verum ergo non uidi aliquem in terra uostra, qui fecerit illud: neque legi illud in aliquo ex libris antiquorum: et est possibile, ut sit illud nouum.	But indeed I have not seen anyone on your land who has done this; nor is it written about anywhere in ancient books; and it could be that this is new.
Et istae sunt formae specierum ex magda, ut stet super ea qui ea ignorat.	And these are forms of tumors from a maedan, as it remains unchanged if one who does not know this.
Fiant ex aere proprie: et sint extremitates eorum cum hac eadem subtilitate triangulatae, et extremitas acuta.	Let these be made from pure metal: and their ends are three-cornered with the same fineness.
Formae magda.	Forms of tumors. (The term 'magda' seems to refer to a type or category within surgical procedures, likely related to tumor removal or treatment as per Albucasis.)
¶ De cura Carnis natae in naso.	On the treatment of meat generated in the nose." (This appears to discuss a condition related to tissue growth inside the nose, possibly referring to polyps or other benign tumors, and how Albucasis advised treating them.)
Caput XXIIII.	Chapter eighty-four. (In medieval manuscripts like this one, chapters were often numbered using Roman numerals; here it refers to the chapter in which Albucasis discusses a specific surgical procedure or topic.)
Quandoque nascuntur in naso Carnes diuersae additae, ex quibus est aliquid quod assimilatur scorpioni multorum pedum: et ex ea est caro cancerosa, lapidea, fusci coloris: et ex ea est quae est caro lenis, non fusci coloris.	When various types of flesh are formed in the nose for a long time, among which is something similar to scorpions with many feet: and among them is a cancerous meat, stone-like, dark colored: and among them there is a soft flesh, not dark-colored." (Albucasis likely describes different types of growths that can occur within the nasal cavity. He categorizes them into three distinct forms based on their characteristics - one resembling scorpions suggesting a pulsating or crawling sensation when touched; another hard and stone-like, indicating perhaps a calcified tumor like osteoma; and a third that is soft in texture but not dark colored which could imply a more benign form such as an epithelial polyp.)
In ea ergo quae ex istis carnibus est lenis, non fraudulenta, neque cancerosa, oportet ut facias sedere infirmum inter manus tuas oppositum soli, et aperi nares eius, et proiice uncinum in illas carnes: deinde trahe eas ad exteriora, et incide quod comprehendisti ex eis cum spatumili subtili acuto a parte una, donec scias quod caro tota iam ablata est.	In the case that what is taken from these soft, honest, and non-cancerous tissues should be placed weakly opposite your hands, open its nostr**ls, and insert a hook in those flesh: then pull out to the exterior, and incise what you have enclosed with a thin sharp knife on one side, until you know that the entire flesh is already removed.
Quod si remaneret aliquid ex ea cuius abscisio non est possibilis: tunc rade illud cum uno instrumentorum subtilium cum facilitate, donec non remaneat ex eo aliquid.	If there remains something from that which cannot be removed by abscision: then scrape it off with a single sharp instrument until nothing is left of it.
Si autem sanguis tibi dominatur, aut accidat apostema calidum: tunc oppone ei per id quod oportet: aut est ex apostematibus malignis, tunc propera cauterizando eum, donec abscindatur sanguis, et auferantur omnes carnes.	However, if blood controls you or a hot swelling happens: then oppose it with that which is necessary: but if it's from malign swellings, then quickly cauterize it, until the blood and all flesh are removed.
Deinde proiiciatur in nasum post incisionem acetum, et aqua, aut uinum.	Then propel vinegar (or water or wine) into his nose after making an incision.
Si autem aperitur nasus, et procedat ex eo humiditas usque ad palatum, tunc scias quia iam sanus est.	If however a nose is opened and there proceeds from it moisture up to the palate, then you will know that he is already healthy.
Si uero non penetrat humiditas, secundum quod oportet, tunc scias quod intra ipsum est caro nata in superioribus ossibus naris, ad quae non peruenit cum incisione instrumentum.	If however the moisture does not penetrate as it should, then you will know that there is a flesh-eating entity within the upper bones of the nose, to which the tool did not reach with incision.
Tunc ergo oportet, ut intromittas filum lini cui sit quaedam grossitudo, et noda in eo nodos multos: et pone inter omnem nodum quantitatem digiti, aut minus: et ingeniet infirmus, ut mittat extremitatem unam fili in nasum cum radio, aut cum quo possibile est ei postquam fecerit ipsum simile azer: et trahat odoratum suum, donec perueniat usque ad caassum, et egrediatur super guttur suum.	Therefore, it should be introduced a thread of linen with some thickness and tied many knots on it: and place between every knot the amount of a finger or less: and let an infirm person pull out one end of the thread from the nose with their little finger, or as much as possible after doing so: and pull out the smelly substance until it comes to its casing.
Et multotiens quidem faciunt simile huic Attomi pueri in scholis: et est res facilis ei, qui uult.	And they do this many times like the boys at school: and it is easy for those who want to.
Deinde pone duas extremitates fili, extremitatem unam quae egreditur super nasum, et alteram quae remansit in naso.	Then place two sticks on either side of the child, one that extends beyond the bridge of the nose and the other remaining within it.
Deinde ac ministra serraturam carnis cum nodis qui sunt in filo.	Next, use a scalpel with knots to secure flesh.
Fac illud donec scias quod carnes iam sunt cum nodis fili.	Do this until you know that the flesh of the child is now full of nodes.
Deinde extrahe filum: et pone in nasum post abstersionem sanguinis licinium quod imbibisti in unguento aegyptio: fac illud tribus diebus, aut plus, donec unguentum corrodat totum quod remansit ex carnibus.	Next, extract the thread. Place it in the nose after washing with an Egyptian ointment that you have taken: do this for three days or more, until the ointamoat softens all remaining flesh.
Deinde pone in fine rei in nasum cannulam de plumbo, diebus aliquot, donec sanetur.	Next, place a lead tube at the end of this matter: do this for several days until it heals.
Si autem indiget curatione quae exiccet, utere illa.	If however, it requires additional treatment that removes it, use that one.
Ad caputpurgium faciendum, cum quo distillantur olea, et aliae medicinae in nasum, fac illud ex argento, aut aere: quod sit simile lampadi paruae, apertum sicut conchula: et meatus eius similiter.	For making the head treatment, as with which oil is distilled and other medicines are placed in the nose; do this from silver or copper: what will be similar to small lampshades, open like little shells: and its passageway similarly.
Et si uis fac cannulam clausam, sicut canna.	If you want to make a closed tube like a reed, follow this method.
Et conchula instrumenti ad caputpurgium faciendum, sit plena, detecta: cui sit manubrium in postremo eius, cum quo teneas ipsam, quando calefacis in ea oleum, aut quod uis ex succis, et rebus fluxibilibus.	And the instrument for head cleansing shall be filled, with its handle at the end; use it to hold when heating that oil or any viscous substance and fluid materials.
Et haec est forma instrumenti.	This is the form of the instrument.
¶ De cura Thelul nasi.	Here is how to treat a nose thrombosis.
Caput XXV.	Head XXV. (Note: "XXV" means "twenty-five," but it's unclear what specifically this refers to without more context.)
Multotiens nascitur in extremitate nasi Thelul, et magnificatur, et augmentatur cum diebus, donec foedus fit aspectus eius.	Often a thrombosis occurs in the end of the nose and it is enlarged with days until it becomes visible.
Et propter illud oportet, ut in cidas illud in principio apparitionis eius, et eradices totum eius.	And for that reason, it is necessary at the beginning of its appearance to extract the entire thing.
Deinde pone super locum, aut cauterium, aut medicinam comburentem quae stat loco eius.	Then place over the location, either a cautery or a burning medicine at that spot.
Si ergo tardatur incisio eius, donec magnificetur, tunc considera, si est lapideum, durum, fusci coloris, pauci sensus: tunc non tangas ipsum cum ferro: quoniam apostema est cancerosum.	However, if the incision is delayed in healing until it swells and hardens, then consider, if it's stone-like, of a dark color, with few sensations: do not touch it with iron as it is an inflamed tumor.
Multotiens enim uidi, qui incidit hmoni apostema, et accidit ex eo malicia magna super illum qui ipsum habebat.	Often I have seen those who suffer from a tumor, and great mischief occurs to the one who has it himself.
Et si apostema est lenis tactus, non fusci coloris, et uides quod incisio possibilis est in toto eius, tunc euacua infirmum, et incide ipsum sine timore, absque pauore: et cura locum cum eo quod exiccat et constringit, donec sanetur.	And if the tumor is a soft touch, not dark color, and you see that it can be cut out in its entirenerness, then thoroughly disinfect the weak one, and incise without fear or hesitation: And treat the place where it exudes and binds until healed.
¶ De sutura nasi, et labii, et auris.	Concerning a suture of the nose, lips, and ears.
Caput XXVI.	Chapter 26.
Scias Quia quando accidit solutio continuitatis in una harum cartilaginum, parum confert in ea operatio, nisi in quibusdam hominibus.	Know that when there is a rupture of the continuity of one or both of these cartilages, little strengthens it in operation unless on certain people.
Oportet ergo quando accidit alicui aliquid ex illo, ut consideres, si est uulnus recens cum sanguine suo: et tunc aggrega duolabia uulneris cum sutura: deinde cura ipsum, donec sanetur.	It is necessary then when something of that kind occurs to you, consider if the wound is fresh with its own blood: and then add griefs of the wound with stitches: next treat it until healed.
Et si solutionis continuitatis labia iam separata sunt, et facta est unaquaeque pars sana: tunc oportet ut excories omnem partem a cute sua apparente, donec sanguinetur.	And if the lips of the dislocation have already been separated and each part is healed: then it should be that every visible piece of skin from its underlying tissue be excised until bleeding occurs.
Deinde aggrega duo labia cum sutura, et stringe ea, et pulueriza super ipsum sanguinem draconis, et olibanum trita: et pone supra pulueres frustum emplastri diafinicon, et alicuius alterius ex emplastris consolidatiuis: et dimitte ipsum ligatum duobus diebus, aut tribus.	Then connect the two lips with sutures and bind them tightly, and press over the bloody area with a draug marshmallow leaf paste and ground olibanum: place on top of the poultice an oblong piece from the dressing diaphragm, and another one attached to consolidated bandages. Release it for two or three days.
Deinde solue ipsum, et permuta medicinam: et dimitte ipsum, donec abscindantur fila per se.	Then wash off the wound and apply a poultice: leave it until the threads are pulled apart by themselves.
Deinde cura ipsum cum unguento, donec sanetur.	Then treat it with ointment: allow time for healing.
Modus autem suturae est, ut aggreges solutionem continuitatis, aut cum acubus, sicut narrauimus in sutura uentris: aut aggrega solutionem cum filo, sicut feci te scire.	The way to suture is as follows, you should gather the dislocation just like we described when performing a labia suturing: or gather the separation with thread, as you know how to do so.
¶ De extractione nodorum labiorum.	From the removal of breast lumps.
Caput XXVII.	Chapter  groaner and twenty-seven (about) The Extraction of Breast Lumps.
Multis Quidem hominibus accidunt plaerumque in interioribus labiorum suorum apostemata dura similia granis herbi: et quaedam eorum minora, et maiora.	For many people it happens and is pleasant that they have hard knots within their breasts similar to grains of grass: some smaller ones, others larger.
Ergo oportet ut conuertas labium, et findas super omnem nodum eius, et suspendas ipsum cum uncino, et incidas ipsum ab omni parte.	Therefore, it is necessary to turn the breast and touch upon all its lumps, and attach a hook thereon, and cut into every part of it.
Deinde impleas locum post incisionem zegi trito, donec abscindatur sanguis.	Then fill in the place after cutting with well-cooked lint, until the blood is drained out.
Deinde colluatur cum aceto, et curetur locus cum eo, in quo est stipticitas, usquequo sanentur uulnera.	Then it should be washed with vinegar and treated with the said vinegar where there is a stiffness until wounds are healed.
¶ De incisione carnis natae super gingiuam.	From an incision on the skin of the thighs over the groin.
Caput XXVIII.	Head XXVIII.
Multotiens nascitur super gingiuam caro addiat, quam antiqui nominant abuluss.	Often a tumor grows on the side of the body close to the skin that ancient writers have called an aboulus.
Oportet ergo ut suspendas eam cum uncino: aut teneas eam cum forcipibus, et incidas eam apud radicem suam, et dimittas saniem currere, aut sanguinem.	It should therefore be hung with a hook or held with forceps and cut at its root; allow the veins to run off.
Deinde pone super locum zegi tritum, aut alios pulueres stipticos, exiccatiuos.	Then place over a prepared site or other sticking plasters.
Quod si redit illa caro post curationem, nam multotiens redit, tunc incide eam secundo, et cauteriza ipsam: ipsa namque non redit post cauterium.	If the tumor returns after treatment, as it often does, then incise it a second time and burn it: for it will not return following burning.
¶ De rasione Dentium cum ferro.	Concerning tooth extraction with iron.
Caput XXIX.	Chapter 29.
Quandoque aggregantur in superficiebus Dentium ab interiori et extetiori parte, et inter gingiuas cortices asperi, turpes, et quandoque denigrantur, et citrini fiunt, et uirides, donec peruenit ex illo corruptio ad gingiuam, et foedi fiunt dentes per illud.	When aggregated on surfaces of teeth from both internal and external parts, and when gums become rough, discolored, turning yellow or green until the decay reaches the gum, causing foulness in teeth.
Oportet ergo ut facias sedere infirmum inter manus tuas, et caput eius in sinu tuo, et rade molam et dentem, in quo apparent tibi cortices, et res similis arenae: donec non remaneat ex eis aliquid, et similiter fac de nigredine, et uiriditate, et citrinitate, et aliis donec mundentur.	It is therefore fitting that you make the sick person sit between your hands and place their head in your lap. And scrape off a bone with teeth where there appears to be cortex, and something similar to sand: until nothing remains of them, and do similarly with blackness, greenish hues, yellowish tones, and others until they are cleaned.
Si ergo auferatur quod in eis est a principio rasionis, bonum est: et si non, tunc itera super eos rasionem die alio, secundo, et tertio, donec ad ultimum perueniat studium in eo quod uis.	If something is removed from them at the beginning of reason (i.e., treatment), this is good: but if not, then apply rubbing with a rag another day, secondly, and thirdly, until it finally reaches its aim through persistent effort.
Et scias, quod dens indiget rasoriis diuersarum formarum, multarum figurarum: secundum quod praeparatur operationi tuae: proptera, quod rasorium quo raditur dens ab inferiori parte, est aliud a rasorio quo raditur inter dentes, secundum formas alias.	And know that the tooth requires different forms of scrapers according to your surgery: for a scraper used to remove a tooth from its lower part is different from one that cuts between teeth, depending on other cases.
Et istae formae rasoriorum sint apud te praeparatae, quas uides.	These forms of razors are prepared for you as they appear.
¶ De extractione doloris Dentium.	On the removal of a toothache.
Caput XXX.	Chapter Thirty.
Oportet ut cures Dentem a dolore suo cum omni ingenio, et tardes in eradicatione eius.	It is necessary that one heals the tooth from its pain using every means and diligently works on its extraction.
Non est enim quod uicem eius suppleat quando eradicatur: quoniam est substantia sublimis: donec quando non est excusatio de eradicatione eius, tunc oportet quando cogitur infirmus eradicare ipsum, ut firmetur, et certificetur apud te dens dolens.	It is not fitting for him when it is removed: since the matter is lofty: until there is no excuse of its extraction, then you should be unwell in removing it, so that it can be solidified and confirmed by a tooth-aching person.
Multotiens enim decipit infirmum dolor, et putat quia est in dente saha et eradicat ipsum: deinde non recedit dolor, donec eradicetur dens infirmus.	Often, the ill one is deceived by pain and believes that it lies within a weak tooth and removes it: then the pain does not go away until an unwell tooth is removed.
Nos enim iam uidimus illud ex operatione phlebotomatorum.	We now see this through the action of phlebotomists.
Cum ergo certificatur apud te dens dolens ipsemet, tunc oportet ut scarifices in circumitu dentis cum spatumili, in quo sit quiddam uirtutis, donec soluatur gingiua ab omni parte: deinde moue ipsum digitis tuis, aut cum forcipibus subtilibus in primis paulatim, donec concutias ipsum.	When therefore a toothache becomes present with you, it is necessary that you incise around the tooth with a knife until a certain point of strength, and loosen the gum from all sides: then move it with your fingers or with fine forceps gradually, until it breaks.
Deinde loca tunc in eo forcipes magnos locatione bona, et caput infirmi inter genua tua: quod iam bene tenuisti, ita quod non moueatur: deinde trahe dentem secundum rectitudinem, ut non frangas ipsum.	Then place large forceps firmly in that location and your head between your knees: what you have already held well, so that it does not move: then pull the tooth straight out, so as not to break it.
Si ergo non egreditur, tunc accipe aliquod illorum instrumentorum, et intromitte ipsum sub eo ab omni parte cum facilitate, et conare motionem eius, sicut fecisti in primis.	But if it does not come out, then take something of those instruments and introduce it undernee from all sides with ease, and try to move it as you did at first.
Si autem dens est perforatus, aut corrosus: tunc oportet ut impleas illud foramen panno: et stringas ipsum cum extremitate radii subtilis, ut non frangatur in hora constrictionis tuae super ipsum cum forcipibus.	But if the tooth is perforated or eroded: then you must fill that hole with cloth: and secure it tightly with a thin piece of radius (wrist), so that it does not break during your compression using forceps.
Et oportet, ut exquisite agas cum scarificatione in circumitu gingiuae ab omni parte multum.	And it is necessary that you should examine with great care around the entire jaw area.
Et custodi fortitudinem tuam, ut non frangas ipsum, et remaneat pars eius, et redeat super infirmum ex ea malicia quae sit maior dolore eius primo.	And be watchful to prevent it from breaking and that part remains intact, and returns above the sick individual with the initial severity.
Et caue, ne facias illud quod ignorantes faciunt phlebotomatores in festinatione sua, et audacia ipsorum super eradicationem eius, praeter quod administrent illud quod narrauimus.	And make sure you do not do what the uninformed leech collectors do hastily, and their boldness exceeds the procedure's removal, apart from that which they administer as we have mentioned.
Multotiens enim faciunt euenire super homines infirmitates magnas, quarum difficiliores sunt ut frangantur, et remaneant radices eius omnes, aut quaedam earum: aut ut extrahant ipsum cum quibusdam ossibus mandibulae: sicut testificati sumus multotiens illud.	For often severe ailments occur in men, which are difficult to break and all its roots remain intact or some of them; such as extracting it with certain jawbones: as we have frequently witnessed.
Deinde colluatur post eradicationem eius cum uino, aut cum aceto et sale.	Then wash after its removal with wine, or vinegar and salt.
Quod si accidat fluxus sanguinis ex locis (multotiens enim accidit) tunc tere aliquid ex zegi, et imple cum eo locum: et si non, cauteriza ipsum si non confert tibi zegi.	If blood flow occurs often from certain places then insert something into a wax plug and fill it with that; and if not, burn the area to prevent further bleeding.
Formae forcipum subtilium quibus mouetur dens in primis, sint longarum extremitatum, breuis manubrii, grossi, ut non duplicentur quando cum eis premitur super dentem: sint sicut uides grossorum manubriorum, donec quando stringis cum eis, non dent seipsas, neque duplicentur: breuium extremitatum, et sint ex ferro indo, aut ex faled decenter facti, directarum extremitatum: et in eorum extremitatibus sint dentes, quorum quidam ingrediantur in quosdam, et stringant constrictione decenti, forti.	The forms of the pliers with which a nail is first moved should have extended ends, short handles, be thick so as not to fold when pressed onto teeth: they should look like those of large pliers until you press them against something and they do not bend or double over; their extremities should be brief and made from iron or somewhat crookedly fashioned with round-shaped points at the ends.
Et quandoque fiunt extremitates sicut forma oris auis quae nominatur ciconia, et sunt fortis constrictionis.	And sometimes they have parts that resemble a stork's beak called 'ciconia', and are strong in compression.
¶ De eradicatione Dentium, et extractione ossium mandibularum fractorum.	Regarding the removal of teeth and extracting bones from a broken jaw.
Caput XXXI.	Chapter Thirty-One.
Quando remanet apud eradicationem Dentis qui frangitur aliquid, tunc oportet ut ponas super locum cotum cum butyro die uno, aut duobus diebus, donec mollificetur locus: deinde intromitte ad ipsum algasti, aut forcipes: quorum extremitates assimilantur ori auis quae nominatur ciconia.	When the tooth remains after extraction of something that breaks it, then one must place something over the socket with butter for a day or two until softened: then insert an algasti or forceps whose ends resemble the beak of a bird known as ciconia.
Forma autem haec est forcipum.	However, this is the form of these tools.
Sint extremitates eorum factae sicut lima deintus: aut sicut aliskilfegi.	The ends are made like an inside lever: or like a screwdriver.
Si ergo non obedit tibi ad exitum cum istis forcipibus, tunc oportet, ut caues super radicem, et detegas carnem totam, et intromittas instrumentum quod nominatur Palanca parua, cuius forma est haec.	If these tools do not work for you in extracting the tooth, then it is necessary that on top of cutting into the root, and revealing all flesh, one inserts an instrument called a small lever, whose form is as follows:
Sit breuis extremitatis, grossae parumper: et non sit imbibitum, ut non frangatur.	Let its ends be made short and not very thick: so that it does not break.
Si ergo egreditur radix per illud, est bonum: et si non, iuuare oportet cum istis instrumentis aliis quorum formae sunt istae.	If thus the root emerges through this [method], it's good; and if not, one must heal with other instruments of those forms.
Forma primi triangulatae extremitatis, in qua est quaedam grossitudo.	The shape of the first side of a triangle has some thickness.
Forma triangulatae extremitatis subtilis.	The shape of the second side of the triangle is thin.
Etiam iuuatur cum hoc instrumento habente duos ramos, cuius haec est forma.	Also heal with this tool that has two branches; here's its form.
Et cum aliis instrumentis et ferramentis quae praecesserunt in rasione dentium.	And with other instruments and tools that preceded in cutting teeth.
Etiam sit iuuamentum cum hoc instrumento quod assimilatur uncino magno, huius formae, triangulatae extremitatis tortae, in qua est quiddam grossitudinis, ut non frangatur: et sit non imbibitum.	And let there be healing with this tool resembling a large hook; its shape is the curved side of a triangle with some thickness so that it does not break: and [let it] be unsoaked.
Et scias, quod instrumenta dentium sunt multa: et similiter reliqua instrumenta non computantur, et artifex prudens, subtilis in arte sua inuenit per se ipsum instrumentum, secundum quod significant ei operatio et aegritudines ipsae.	And you know that the instruments for teeth are many: and similarly other tools do not count, and a skilled artisan, subtle in his craft, found by himself an instrument according to what represents the operation and pains themselves.
Quoniam ex agritudinibus sunt ad quas non dixerunt antiqui instrumentum, propter diuersitatem specierum earum.	Since these tools are from materials not previously mentioned by the ancients due to their variety of species.
Si autem frangatur os ex mandibula, aut ex aliis ossibus oris, aut putrefit: tunc perscrutare super ipsum in loco suo cum eo quod conuenit ei ex instrumentis et forcipibus quae dixi in extractione radicum, et iuuare cum gesti, cuius forma est haec.	If however the bone is broken from the jaw or other facial bones, and it putrefies: then to search over it at its place with that which I mentioned for extracting roots using pliers as described above, and healing with a bandage in this shape.
Sit in eo quiddam grossitudinis paulatim, ut stringatur, uel teneatur cum eo os, et non fugiat et uadat, donec egrediatur os: et restaura locum cum medicinis conuenientibus ad illud.	Let there be a gradual hardening in that matter, as it tightens and holds with the bone, and does not escape or spread out until the bone emerges: and restore the place with appropriate medicines for this purpose.
Si autem in osse est putredo parua, tunc rade ipsum a putredine sua, et cura ipsum, donec sanetur.	If there is a small rot on the bone, then scrape off that rot from itself, and care for it until healed.
De serratura Dentium eminentium super alios.	On the lock of the prominent teeth over others.
Caput XXXII.	Head XXXII.
Quando Dentes eminent non secundum cursum suum naturalem, foeda fit per illud forma: et praecipue quando accidit illud in mulieribus, et puellis, scilicet uenalibus.	When teeth erupt out of their natural course, an unsightly form is created by this: especially when it happens to women and girls, particularly unmarried ones.
Oportet ergo ut consideres.	It should therefore be considered.
Nam si dens est natus post dentem alium, et non locatur, uel est possibilis eius serratura, neque limatura ipsius: tunc eradica ipsum: et si est annexus cum dente alio, tunc incide ipsum cum isto instrumento, cuius haec est forma.	For if a tooth has been born behind another and does not find its place, or if it cannot be removed by the use of shears, nor trimmed: then extract this tooth; and if it is attached with another, then cut it off using that instrument, which tool shall take this form.
Est simile rostro paruo, et fit ex ferro indo, acutae extremitatis ualde.	It resembles a small face and is made of iron, with very sharp tips.
Et sit incisio tua qua ipsum incidis in diebus multis, et propter duriciem dentis, et ut non commoueatur alius ex dentibus.	And make this incision on many days, and because of the hardness of the tooth, so that another tooth is not displaamoent.
Si autem est eminens expositus limaturae suae: tunc lima ipsum cum lima ex indo, cuius forma est haec.	But if it protrudes too much from the shears of its own making: then file it with an iron file, which tool shall take this form.
Sit totum ex indo, et manubrium eius minutorum punctorum ualdae, sicut lima cum qua fiunt acus: cum quo limetur dens paulatim in diebus multis cum facilitate, ut non commoueatur dens, et cadat: deinde leni ipsum, in fine rade ipsum cum quibusdam rasoriis.	It is all from the hand and the top of its nails with a file, as a whetstone upon which axes are sharpened: it should be gradually ground over many days so that it does not move the tooth, but falls off: then gently itself, at last carefully with some rasors.
Quod si est dens, ex quo frangatur pars, et laedit linguam: tunc oportet ut limes eum etiam, donec auferatur asperitas illius fractionis, et aequetur: et applanetur, et non laedat linguam, neque corrumpat sermonem.	If the tooth is broken and damages the tongue: it should be filed down until its roughness from the breakage is removed, smoothened out, and does not damage the tongue or impair speech.
¶ De retatione Dentium cum filis auri.	On reattaching teeth with gold wires:
Caput XXXIII.	Chapter XXXIII:
Quando accidit Dentibus anterioribus concussio et commotio a percussione, aut casu: et non potest infirmus stringere super illud quod comedit ut non cadat: et curasti eos cum medicinis stipticis, et non ualuit curatio: tunc ingenium in eis est, ut stringantur cum filo auri: quoniam argentum fit uiride, et putrefit post dies: sed aurum nunquam mutatur.	When anterior teeth suffer from impact or motion due to an accident and the patient cannot keep what has been removed in place: even with medical adhesives, treatment is not effective: then it becomes necessary for them to be bound together using gold wire, as silver corrocks after a day, but gold never changes.
Et sit filum medium in subtilitate et grossicie secundum quantitatem quod capiat inter Dentes.	And let the wire have a medium thickness and width according to the space between the teeth.
Et forma quidem retationis est, ut accipias filum, et intromittas duplum eius inter duos dentes sanos: deinde texeas cum duabus extremitatibus fili inter dentes motos, siue unus sit, aut plures, donec peruenias cum tela usque ad dentem sanum alterius partis.	The technique is as follows: take the wire and insert it double between two healthy teeth; then bind with threads on both ends of the wire to the movable teeth, whether one or more, until you reach a sound tooth on the other side.
Deinde itera texturam usque ad partem a qua incaepisti: et stringe manum tuam cum subtilitate et sapientia, donec non remoueatur prorsus: et sit constrictio tua qua stringis filum, apud radices dentium, ut non euadat.	Then continue to follow the layer until you reach where you cut it; and tightly bind with your hand skillfully and wisely until it is completely removed: make sure that the tension of the binding resembles a thread near the tooth roots so that it does not recede.
Deinde incide extremitates fili superfluentes cum forficibus: et aggrega utrumque, et conuerte eas cum gesti: et occulta ipsas inter dentem sanum et dentem motum, ut non laedat linguam: deinde dimittatur ita strictum dum remanet.	Then cut the excess threads with scissors; and bring them together, then twist them securely: ensure that they are hidden between a healthy tooth and one on the move so as not to harm the tongue; then release while keeping it firm until removed.
Si autem soluitur, aut inciditur, stringe eos cum filo alio, et stabit cum eo taliter tempore toto.	If however it is loosened or cut, bind them tightly with another thread, and stand together for the whole time.
Et haec est forma Dentium, et figura retationis duorum dentium sanorum, et duorum dentium motorum, sicut uides.	And this is the form of teeth, and the shape of repositioning two healthy teeth and two moving teeth as you see it.
Et quandoque fit, ut redeat dens unus, aut duo post casum urriusque in locis suis, et retentur sicut narrauimus, et remaneant: et non facit illud nisi artifex, prudens, et expertus.	And sometimes it happens that a tooth or two returns after an accident and settles back into its place as we described; this is only done by an artist who is skilled, wise, and experienced.
Et quandoque aptatur aliquod ex ossibus uaccinis: et fit ex eo sicut forma dentis, et ponitur in loco, ex quo munitur dens et stringitur, sicut diximus: et remanet, et seruitur cum eo tempore longo.	And when it is occasionally attached to a piece of the vagina bone: and formed in such way as the form of a tooth, and placed where the teeth are set and clenched, just as we said before: and remains, and serves with it for a long time.
¶ De incisione ligamenti quod accidit sub lingua, et prohibet loquelam.	From the incision that occurs under the tongue, which prevents speech.
Caput XXXIIII.	Chapter XXXIV.
Quandoque ligamentum hoc quod accidit sub lingua, est aut naturale, cum quo nascitur homo, aut accidentale, a uulnere quod iam consolidatum est.	When this ligament that occurs under the tongue is either natural, with which man is born, or accidental, from an ulcer that has already healed.
Et operatio in eo est, ut aperias os infirmi in capite eius in sinu tuo, et eleua linguam eius: deinde incide illud ligamentum neruosum per latitudinem, donec soluatur lingua a retentione sua.	And the operation on this is to open up the weakened bone at its head within your cavity and stretch out the tongue: then incise that neural ligament across its width until the tongue is released from its restriction.
Quod si in eo fuerit quiddam duriciei et nodationis, et fuerit illud ex consolidatione uulneris: tunc proiice in illud uncinum, et finde illud per latitudinem, donec incidas ligamentum, et soluatur nodatio.	What if there is something hard and knotted in it, and that came from the consolidation of an ulcer: then protrude into this hook and go through it across its width until you cut the ligament, and the knotting is separated.
Et caue, ne sit fissura in profundo carnis, et incidas arteriam illic, et accidat fluxus sanguinis.	And if there is a crack within the deep flesh, then pierce the artery there and let blood flow.
Deinde colluatur in uestigio incisionis cum aqua rosata, aut cum aceto, aut aqua frigida.	Then wash with rosewater or vinegar, or cold water at the site of the incision.
Deinde pone sub lingua licinium ex lino, quod teneat infirmus in omni nocte: ut non consolidetur secundo.	Then place under the tongue linen bandages that should be held by a weak person throughout every night to prevent hardening.
Si autem accidat fluxus sanguinis, tunc pone super locum zegi tritum.	However, if blood flow occurs, then apply lint over the wound area.
Si uero uincit te sanguis, tunc cauteriza locum cum cauterio lentiginoso, quod conuenit ad illud: deinde cura ipsum cum reliqua curatione, donec sanetur.	However, if blood overwheats you, then burn the wound area with a smoldering iron that is suitable for it: afterwards care for it as usual until healed.
¶ De extractione Ranulae quae fit sub lingua.	¶ On extracting a ranula under the tongue.
Caput XXXV.	Chapter n35: "On removing ranulas beneath the tongue.
Quandoque accidit sub lingua apostema quod assimilatur Ranae paruae, prohibens linguam ab operatione sua naturali: et fortasse magnificatur adeo, donec implet os.	Occasionally a small swelling beneath the tongue resembling a frog is formed due to its own nature and prevents speech through its swelling; at times it may be greatly enlarged until it fills the mouth.
Et operatio in eo est, ut aperias os infirmi coram sole: et considera apostema.	The operation is performed by opening up a wound on the diseased bone while it's exposed to sunlight and then inspecting the abscess.
Si ergo uides ipsum fusci coloris, aut nigri, durum, cui non inuenit infirmus sensum: tunc non tangas ipsum, quoniam est cancer.	If you observe that it has a dark or black color and is hard without any feeling to the patient'nounces it as cancer.
Et si est decliue ad albedinem, in quo est humiditas, tunc proiice in ipsum uncinum, et incide ipsum cum spatumili subtili, et libera ipsum ab omni parte.	And if it has decayed to a whiteness and there is moisture in it, then insert an instrument into it, make a careful incision within the abscess, and free it from all sides.
Quod si uincit te sanguis in hora tuae operationis, tunc pone super ipsum zegi tritum, donec abscindatur sanguis: deinde redi ad operationem tuam, donec extrahas ipsum cum complemento eius.	If blood overcomes you during your surgery, then place a piece of linen on it until the bleeding stops, and return to your procedure once it has been removed.
Deinde colluatur cum aceto et sale: et cura ipsum reliqua curatione conueniente ad illud, donec sanetur.	Then cleanse with vinegar and salt: then proceed in the remaining treatment appropriate to it until healed.
¶ De curatione apostematis duarum Amigdalarum.	Regarding the treatment of two tonsils, firstly ensure that they are thoroughly cleaned. Then consider if there is pus or a foul smell coming from them: in this case, proceed with their removal and then perform an incision to drain the abscess. If it appears healthy but swollen, apply vinegar and salt; afterwards, continue its appropriate treatment until recovery.
Caput XXXVI.	Chapter Thirty-Six.
Quandoque accidunt inter guttur godad, id est, glandulae, quae similantur algodad, quae accidunt deforis: et nominantur duae Amigdalae: quas quando curas cum eo quod diximus in diuisione, et non sanantur, tunc considera.	Whenever glands arise with an inflammatcuation that resembles a bullseye or 'bull's-eye', known as "Glandulae quae similantur algodad", and do not heal, then we should consider the two Amigdalas: which we discussed in detail previously.
Si ergo est apostema durum, fusci coloris, pauci sensus: tunc non tangas ipsum cum ferro.	If there is a hard abscess and it has a darker color with few symptoms: then do not prick the skin with a needle.
Et si est rubei coloris, et radix eius est grossa: tunc non tangas ipsum etiam cum ferro, timens fluxum sanguinis, imo dimitte ipsum, donec maturetur.	And if it is red in color and has a large root: then do not puncture it with iron even though there may be bleeding; rather leave the area until it heals naturally.
Et tunc aut perforabis ipsum: aut rumpetur per se.	T'en dehoreus est et cum mala cogaritur : oui per se ruptum erit.
Et si est albi coloris, rotundum, et est radix eius subtilis: tunc oportet ipsum incidi.	And then you may puncture it: or it will burst by itself. And if it is white and round, and its root is thin; then it must be cut open.
Et operatio in ipso est, ut consideres ante operationem suam, si quieuit apostema eius calidum quiete completum, aut imminuitur quadam diminutione: tunc ergo fac sedere infirmum coram sole, et caput eius sit in sinu tuo: et aperi os eius, et accipiat seruiens inter manus suas, et premat linguam eius inferius cum instrumento, cuius haec est forma.	And then you should perform the operation itself when it is coo cued with warmth and rest; or if there's a slight reduction: then he must sit in front of the sunlight, and his head shall be under your hand: and open its mouth with an instrument, this is the method.
Fiat ex argento, aut aere, quod sit subtile sicut cultellus.	Let it be made of silver or brass as thin as a knife.
Cum ergo premis cum eo linguam, et ostenditur tibi apostema, et cadit super ipsum uisus tuus: tunc accipe uncinum, et fige ipsum in amigdalam, et extrahe eam ad exteriora quantum potes, praeter quod trahas cum ea aliquid ex tunicis.	Then take hold of the tongue with it and show him his swelling; and if he falls on his side, take a hook and fasten it to your thumb as far as you can, but pull out something from its tunics.
Deinde incide eam cum instrumento, cuius haec est forma quae sequitur.	Then cut it with an instrument, this is the method that follows.
Assimilatur forficibus: uerumtamen extremitates eius sint curuatae, ita quod orificium cuiusque earum est in directo alterius acute: unde cura ut sit ex ferro indo, aut alfuled imbibitum.	After that, cut with an instrument, this is the method to follow.
Si autem non est praesens hoc instrumentum, tunc incide ipsum cum spatumili, cuius haec est forma.	However, if there's no such tool available, then you should cut it using a similar one: this is the method to apply.
Sit acutum a parte una, non acutum a parte altera.	The incision should be made on one side only, not both sides at once.

Caput XXXVII.	Heading: Chapter Thirty-Seven
Quando descendit catarrus ad uuulam, et apostematur, et est long: tunc ipsa nominatur perpendicularis: et si est in inferiori parte grossa, rotunda, tunc ipsa nominatur uua. Et quae ex ea est aggregata rotunda, et non est ei longitudo, et est sanguinea, aut fusci coloris, aut nigri, et non est ei sensus: tunc oportet ut deuites incisionem eius.	And when the abscess is rounded and does not have lengthening; and it's either bloody or dark in color, or black and without feeling: then one must open (drain) that of it.

¶ De apertione Apostematum, et eorum sectione, et cura in genere.	On the opening of pustules and their sections, and care generally.

This Latin passage discusses different types of skin ulcers that can occur due to wounds.

This sentence is a medical prescription from Albucasis in the medieval Latin text on surgery: "However, it should be punctured with a simple incision (not deep), like shallow boils." Donec quando erit dies tertius, sicut diximus, tunc oportet ut soluas apostema, et abstergas ipsum, et administres in curatione eius quod ei conuenit, donec sanetur.	When the third day comes, as we have said before, then you should wash out the abscess with vinegar or wine vinegar mixed with oil and fat (oleo), and that which is appropriate for its condition until it heals.

If you observe that nothing remains after two applications, repeat the cautery on the next day and inspect the wound afterwards.
Quod si apostema continet nodum pinguem: tunc seca ipsum secundum hanc formam, sectione habente formam crucis: et proiice uncinos inter duolabia sectionis, et excoria ipsum ab omni parte: et conare uirtutem tuam in extractione tunicae quae continet ipsum.	If the sore wound is a hard knot (grant you have examined it well): then cut along this pattern, making two separate cuts shaped like a cross: and remove all thorns from the parts of division; And apply your care in removing the skin that contains the pus.
Si autem contrarietatem facit tibi arteria, tunc fac illud quod narrabo tibi post.	If however the vein causes you opposition, then do this which I will describe to you afterward.
Et similiter fac in apostemate, si est lapideum, ex sectione, et curatione eadem, secundum quod diximus.	Do similarly with a sore that is made of stone, by cutting and treating it the same way as we have mentioned earlier.
Et sectio super apostema lapideum est facilior: quoniam est pauci sanguinis et humiditatis.	And the sectioning over a pus-filled wound is easier, because it contains few blood vessels and fluid.
Et quandoque sunt quaedam horum apostematum quae sunt in capite in quibusdam hominibus, cum quibus penitus non est humiditas.	In certain cases of swelling on a person's head, there are some that have no discharge inside the skull.
Quod est: quia ego secui super apostema in capite mulieris uetulae, et inueni apostema sicut lapis solidus et durus, asper, albus, qui non poterat frangi: et si percuteretur cum eo aliquis proiiciendo, uulnerat ipsum.	That is: because I treated a woman's swelling in the head that was hard and solid as a diamond and white; when it was struck with something, it wounded it.
In aliis uero apostematibus accidentibus in capite, praeter haec scilicet apostemata quae accidunt in capitibus puerorum, et apud radices aurium, sectio eorum omnium sit sectio superficialis.	In other cases of swelling on the head, apart from those that occur at the roots of hair or among children's heads, a surgical incision should be made over them shallowly.
Vel pone perforationem eorum semper ab inferiori parte eorum, ut alleuietur cursus saniei ad inferiora.	Or always from their lower part through perforations, so that the flow of pus runs to the inferior regions.
Deinde cura ea cum eo quod conuenit eis ex curatione.	Then heal it with what comes into contact with them during treatment.
¶ De sectione Strophularum in collo.	As for the surgery of a lump on the throat,...
Caput XLII.	Heading Forty-Two in a medieval Latin translation of an Arabic medical text from the 1 cuisine bears some interesting similarities with "Al-Tasrif" by Al-Zahrawi, or Albucasis's work on surgical techniques. This chapter deals extensveeley with treatment and management of hernias, a frequent problem in medieval medicine. It provides detailed instructions for the use of various instruments such as scalpels, spatulas, probes, ligatures, catheters and even includes an early description of a special tool used to treat haemorrhoids.
Multotiens acccidunt ista apostemata in collo, et sub assellis, et inguinibus: et quandoque accidunt in reliquo corpore.	These boils are often found on the neck and under the arms; they also occur at times on other parts of the body.
Et super illa quae ex eis accidunt in collo, sunt unum, et multa: et generantur ab inuicem: et omnis Strophula ex eis est intra tunicam propriam ei, sicut est in nodis et apostematibus capitis, sicut narrauimus.	These boils often occur on the neck and under the arms; sometimes they can also appear on other parts of the body. The ones that arise there are either one or many: and they originate from within themselves: and all types of Strophula come into their own skin, just as with lumps and boils on the head, as we have described.
Et species harum Strophularum sunt multae.	There are many kinds of these abscesses.
Et ex eis enim sunt lapideae: et ex eis sunt quae continent humiditates: et ex eis sunt malignae, quae non obediunt curationi.	They have stone-like features; and some retain moisture; and others are malevolent, which do not respond to treatment.
In illa ergo quam ex eis uides bonae dispositionis in tactu, cuius manifestum est propinquum colori cutis, et mouetur ad omnem partem, et non est annexa cum neruis colli, neque cum guidegi, neque cum arteria, neque est profunda: oportet ut seces eam sectione superficiali a superiori parte ad inferiorem partem corporis ex linea, b. ad lineam, g. et excoria eam ab omni parte: et extende duo labia cutis cum uncino, aut cum uncinis multis, si indiges illo, sicut diximus in apostematibus capitis, et extrahe eam paulatim.	In this particular case of these abscesses, which is evident by the coloration similar to that of healthy skin, and can move from one part to another, they are not attached with nerves or veins in the neck or groin area. It should be cut superfaturally on the upper side towards the lower part of the body: extend two flaps of skin using a hook (uncinus) or multiple hooks as we have described regarding cystic swellings, and gradually remove them from all sides.
Et est super cautelam, ut non incidatur uena, aut neruus.	And it is above a veil, so as not to be injured, nor an abscess.
Et sit spatumile non acutum ualde: ut non addat tibi manum tuam cum incisione, aut inquietet infirmum, et incidas quod non est necesse.	And it is not sharp enough to cut with a knife or an indifferent wound.
Si autem incidis uenam, aut arteriam, aut prohibet te ab operatione, tunc pone in uulnus zegi tritum, aut quosdam pulueres qui abscindunt sanguinem, et stringe uulnus, et dimitte ipsum, donec quiescat acuitas apostematis, et mollificetur uulnus: uel incipit et uult putrefieri.	However, if you are injured and have an artery cut, or experience severe pain after the operation, lay a tourniquet on it to stop bleeding, then apply a compress made of wool which extracts blood, soothes inflamm cuff, and relieves swelling. If the wound begins to turn gangrenous (necrotic), the wound must be opened with clean tools.
Nam sanguis abscinditur tuncia Redi ergo ad operationem tuam, donec compleas.	For blood is extracted from the wound by using the technique of tunnica Reidi; until it heals.
Deinde inquire digito tuo indice, si remansit aliquid ex Strophulis aliis paruis: ergo incide eas, et munda eas.	Then check with your index finger if there is anything left from the Staphylococcus bacteria; thus remove them.
Quod si est in radice Strophulae uena magna: tunc oportet ut non incidas illam Strophulam ex radice sua: imo oportet ut liges eam cum filo duplato forti, et dimittas eam donec cadat per se absque nocumento.	If you have a large ulcer on the root of your tongue, it is recommended that you not cut off the stomach from its origin; rather, one should apply doubled strong thread to it until it heals by itself without any harm.
Deinde imple uulnus coto ueteri, quod iam submersisti in unguento aegyptio.	Then you should insert the old wound with Egyptian ointment.
Deinde cura ipsum.	Then he took care." (In Medieval Latin)
Si inciditur Strophula tota, tunc oportet ut aggreges labia duo uulneris: et suas ipsum statim, postquam uides quia prorsus non remansit superfluitas.	If the sinew is completely severed, one must then bind together the two edges of the wound with a ligature (a thread or bandage) immediately so that excessive swelling does not occur.
Si autem uides quod remansit superfluitas propter magnitudinem Strophulae, tunc oportet ut intendas ad incidendam radicem eius, et extrahendam eam: et administra suturam quam diximus.	If the swelling remains due to the size of the Strophula (a type of suture or stitching method), then it is necessary that you immediately make an incision at its root and remove it: and close with the ligature we have described earlier.
Et quae ex Strophulis continet humiditates, perfora illam perforatione superficiali: ut appareat tibi locus maturitatis eius: et pone perforationem ab eo quod sequitur inferius corporis, sicut diximus.	And what is held by Strophula (a type of surgical needle or instrument) contains humors; when it appears ripe in the wound, you should puncture a superf cuff perforation there: and place the perforation from there to below the body as described above.
Deinde administra post perforationem licinia cum unguento, et similia eis, ut corrodat quod remansit ex corruptione, donec quando uides uulnus iam mundatum esse: tunc cura ipsum cum unguento generatiuo carnis, donec sanetur.	Then apply the ligature with ointment and similar treatment as what remains from decaying tissue: when you see that the wound is clean, then care for it thoroughly with a topical application of fatty substances until healed.
¶ De sectione Epiglotis ab apostemate intra guttur accidente.	On Sectioning of a Swelling in the Throat Caused by an Abscess Within the Neck.
Caput XLIII.	Chapter ebxliii: On Incisions and Dissection within the Neck for an abscess in the throat area.
Dixerunt antiqui hanc sectionem in Epigloti, et non uidi aliquem in terra nostra, qui eam fecerit: et haec est scriptura sermonis eorum.	In olden times it was said that no man on earth had performed this procedure before them; and hence they named the section as their own discovery. This is their teaching.
In habentibus autem synanchiam, oportet ut deuitetur sectio Epiglotis: cum non fiat iuuamentum per illud: propterea, quod omnes uenae et pulmo sunt infirmi.	However, in those with an abscess in the throat area, it is necessary that a section should be made of the epiglottis; because for all vessels and lungs are ill (sick).
In illis uero qui habent apostema calidum in ore, aut gutture, aut duabus amigdalis, quando non est aegritudo in cannali, oportet uti sectione Epiglotis, ad fugiendum ex perditione quae fit ex praefocatione.	However, in those who have hot abscesses either in the throat or at both tonsils and epiglottis, if there is no inflammvee of the channel, a section should be made on the epiglottis to prevent deaths that occur as a result of suffocation.
Oportet ergo quando uolumus illud, ut secemus Epiglotim sub tribus circulis Epiglotis, aut quatuor, sectione parua per latitudinem, in eo quod est inter duos circulos per quantitatem, quod sit sectio in sifac, non in cartilagine: et iste quidem locus est conueniens sectioni, quoniam est priuatus carne, et uasa sanguinis ab eo sunt longinqua.	Therefore, when we want to make a small cut on the epiglottis, either between three or four circles across its width, this shall be a minor incision, not in cartilage: and indeed this particular area is most suitable for sectioning because it is fleshy and far from blood vessels.
Quod si medicator est timidus, tunc oportet ut extendat cutem gutturis cum uncino.	If the physician is afraid, then he should loosen his throat with a hook. This line from a medieval Latin text suggests that if a surgeon (physician) lacks confidence or feels hesitant, it would be beneficial for him to proceed carefully in treating wounds involving the throat using an instrument like a hook or similar tool.
Deinde findat cutem, donec quando peruenit ad cannalem: deuitet uas sanguinis, si uidet ex eis aliquid.	Next, he finds the wound until it reaches a canal: as soon as something is found from them, let it be removed with your sword.
Deinde secet sifac quod narrauimus: et significatur super sectionem cannalis ex phlegmate quod egreditur ex ea, cum eo quod disrumpitur, et abscisione uocis.	And then the following is mentioned: and it signifies what emerges from the canal when something breaks out of it and a parting is made.
Et dimitte uulnus apertum tempore aliquo.	Then let an open wound be dismissed after some time.
Cum ergo remouetur hora in qua timetur praefocatio, aggrega duo labia uulneris cutis, et sue ipsam solam absque cartilagine.	And also when the hour of danger is coming, they unite two lips of the skin and remove it without cartilage.
Deinde administra medicinas quae faciunt nasci carnem, usquequo sanetur.	Next, he applies remedies that generate meat (tissue growth) and cures (heals).
Inquit Albucasis.	Albucasis said.
Summa huius sermonis quem narrauimus, expositio non est, nisi quando uident, quod aliquod horum apostematum iam opilauit guttur infirmi: et sublimatus est infirmus super mortem, et uult intersecari anhelitus eius: uadunt ad secandum Epiglotim, ut respiret infirmus super locum uulneris quadam respiratione, et saluetur a morte: et propter hoc praeceperunt dimittere uulnus apertum, donec consumatur malicia aegritudinis, et est malicia eius tribus diebus, et quasi ipsa: tunc ergo praecaeperunt suere uulnus, et curare ipsum, donec sanetur.	As we described above, Albucasis explains that when he observes a swelling in the throat (probably due to an abscess or boil), it signifies that something has erupted from the canal and there's been a separation of skin. The patient becomes more ill during this period, and a part is cut into his throat; the operation heals after three days when the inflammamoent subsides.
Et illud quod uidi per me ipsum est, quod una ancilla accaepit cultellum, et misit cum in guttur suum, et incidit cum eo partem cannalis pulmonis.	This is the tool that I saw by Albucasis, which an assistant held against his throat and struck with a section of the windpipe.
Et uocatus sum ad curationem eius, et inueni eam mugire, sicut est mugitus mortui.	I have been appointed for its treatment, and I found it groaning like a dead man.
Detexi ergo a uulnere, et inueni sanguinem qui egressus fuerat ex uulnere paruum.	I examined it carefully, and the ulna was found to have an exit wound of superficial cuts from arrows or stabbing instruments.
Confisus ergo sum, quod ipsa non absciderat uenam, neque guidegi: et uentus egrediebatur ex uulnere.	I have been vested with the authority to heal it, and discovered that a wound had not healed from the fracture site; but also an effusion of blood was coming out.
Properaui ergo, et sui uulnus, et curaui ipsum, donec sanum est: et non accidit ancillae aliquid, nisi raucedo in uoce: et rediit post dies ad meliorem dispositionum suarum.	I therefore treated it accordingly and healed the wound until it was well; but there occurred a complication with the servant girl other than this: she had nothing else, except for weakness in her voice as if from laryngitis: after a few days, however, she returned to better conditions.
Hinc ergo dico: quod in sectione Epiglotis non est timor.	So, I state that there is no fear for the surgery on the epiglottis.
¶ De sectione Herniae gutturis.	The title "De sectione Herniae gutturis" is Latin and it can be translated as "On the Section of Strangulation in the Throat". This textbook by Albucasis, a renowned Arabic surgeon from the medieval era (936–1018 AD), likely deals with surgical procedures related to removing foreign objects or repairing injuries within the throat.
Caput XLIIII.	42. Caput (Chapter) LXII
Hoc Apostema nominatum Hernia gutturis, est apostema magnum, secundum colorem corporis: et est in mulieribus multum.	This is a large abscess of the throat which occurs often in women.
Et est secundum duos modos: aut enim est naturale: aut est accidentale.	It is indeed an apostema, which is significant; it follows the nature's course and thus can be twofold: either natural or accidental.
In naturali certe non est ingenium.	Indeed, not by chance alone is talent present.
Accidentale uero est secundum duos modos: quorum unus est similis nodis pinguibus.	However, it accidentally occurs in two ways and one of which resembles buboes (boils).
Et modus alter, est similis apostemati quod fit ex nodatione arteriae.	The other way is similar to an abscess resulting from the swelling of an artery.
Et in ipso est timor, et non oportet ut praesumptio fiat ad ipsum cum ferro, nisi in eo quod est paruum: et tu proba ipsum, et inuestiga ipsum cum Intromisso.	And this is fear; and it should not be assumed as such without a thorough examination of the patient with an instrument similar to iron (probably referring to a probe). However, if you are certain that there's only soft tissue involvement in the case, then one may proceed.
Si ergo inuenis ipsum simile nodo pingui, et non est suspensum cum aliqua uenarum: tunc seca ipsum, sicut secantur nodi: et extrahe ipsum cum eo quod continet ex kisti, si est in kisti: et si non, tunc perscrutare totum eius.	However, if you find that it is similar to a node and not filled with blood clots or pus: then excise it as for nodes; and probe the entire lump if it contains abscesses; but if there are no such contents in it: then thoroughly investigate.
Deinde cura locum cum eo quod oportet ex curatione, donec sanetur.	Then care for that spot until it is healed.
¶ De sectione super species Nodorum.	And regarding the treatment of a nodule.
Caput XLV.	Concerning surgery on a lump or knot.
Nodorum multae sunt species, et ego iam dixi omnes species eorum in diuisione: et oportet ut narrem hic differentiam inter Nodum, et Exituram: cum sit dubitationem faciens.
